# Vue Clamp 1.4.0 to 1.5.0 performance analysis

## Data source

This note is based on the package benchmark matrix generated from `/tmp/vue-clamp-matrix-2s-cv`
and stored locally as `journey/research/310-package-benchmark-matrix.local.json`.

The benchmark compares published package versions through the public component API. The report
sampling mode uses at least 2 seconds of measured wall time per scenario, a minimum of 3 measured
samples, median active time as the primary timing value, and active-time CV as the low-confidence
marker.

Later audit note: the stored JSON is the source of truth for this section. A previous draft mixed
numbers from an earlier render with `310-package-benchmark-matrix.local.json`, which incorrectly
showed an InlineClamp timing improvement. Recomputing from the stored JSON gives the table below.
The Line/Inline/Rich timing movements are small and should be treated as low-confidence timing
noise unless supported by structural counters or non-overlapping MOE intervals. The benchmark
tooling has since been tightened to use production Vue runtime defines, at least 5 measured samples
in report mode, and active-time MOE-overlap low-confidence marking.

## Aggregate result

| Component     | 1.4.0 active | 1.5.0 active |  Delta | Rect reads | Item slot calls | Interpretation                                                              |
| ------------- | -----------: | -----------: | -----: | ---------: | --------------: | --------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| LineClamp     |    2894.2 ms |    2981.6 ms |  +3.0% |       0.0% |             N/A | Timing-only movement in the same measured work shape; low confidence.       |
| InlineClamp   |    1314.2 ms |    1347.0 ms |  +2.5% |       0.0% |             N/A | Timing-only movement in the same measured work shape; low confidence.       |
| RichLineClamp |    2209.9 ms |    2296.8 ms |  +3.9% |       0.0% |             N/A | Timing-only movement in the same measured work shape; low confidence.       |
| WrapClamp     |    7600.7 ms |    3675.3 ms | -51.6% |     -46.4% |          -70.0% | Dominant improvement from less DOM probing and fewer item slot invocations. |

Across all comparable scenarios in the stored matrix, 1.5.0 improves active time by 26.5%, settled
time by 8.6%, bounding-rect reads by 58.0%, item slot calls by 70.0%, and long-task count by 24.1%.

## Main improvements

The 1.5.0 improvement is dominated by WrapClamp. The largest scenario wins are all grow-heavy
wrapped-item cases:

| Scenario                                | Active delta | Rect reads | Item slot calls |
| --------------------------------------- | -----------: | ---------: | --------------: |
| `wrap-no-affix-tiny-item-wide-grow`     |       -80.0% |     -87.4% |          -92.5% |
| `wrap-no-affix-heavy-item-grow`         |       -66.8% |     -67.5% |          -72.2% |
| `wrap-no-affix-hidden-grow`             |       -65.9% |     -67.5% |          -72.2% |
| `wrap-static-before-dynamic-after-grow` |       -62.8% |     -71.8% |          -63.6% |
| `wrap-static-after-grow`                |       -63.3% |     -77.5% |          -68.0% |
| `wrap-before-affix-grow`                |       -55.9% |     -43.4% |          -78.6% |

The source-level reason is the WrapClamp solver rewrite in 1.5.0:

- It records item widths during real measurements and reuses those widths for later estimates.
- It can estimate no-affix / static-flow counts without rendering every candidate item.
- Grow paths materialize a bounded frontier and then toggle existing item shells during search
  instead of repeatedly re-rendering each candidate prefix.
- The fallback linear settlement still exists, but it is reached after cheaper proof/hint paths.

The item slot call reduction is especially important because the benchmark intentionally renders
many WrapClamp rows with public `item` slots. In 1.4.0, grow paths repeatedly invoked item slots for
candidate prefixes. In 1.5.0, the renderer only renders up to the visible count or bounded
materialized count, so heavy item content no longer scales with every probe.

InlineClamp also improves in continuous width-sweep scenarios:

| Scenario                              | Active delta | Work counters |
| ------------------------------------- | -----------: | ------------- |
| `inline-path-middle-batch-continuous` |       -17.3% | unchanged     |
| `inline-path-end-batch-continuous`    |       -17.0% | unchanged     |

Because DOM-read counters are unchanged, this is best attributed to component-shell/render-path
changes from the SFC migration and local state simplification, not to a changed text-clamp search
algorithm.

## Main regressions

The largest timing regressions are:

| Scenario                               | Active delta | Absolute delta | Work counters | Confidence      |
| -------------------------------------- | -----------: | -------------: | ------------- | --------------- |
| `line-summary-batch-continuous`        |       +44.6% |       +50.9 ms | unchanged     | CV 4.2% -> 0.7% |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous`      |        +9.0% |       +46.8 ms | unchanged     | CV 2.5% -> 2.3% |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` |        +4.6% |       +24.5 ms | unchanged     | CV 1.3% -> 1.9% |
| `inline-path-middle-batch-jitter`      |        +5.2% |       +23.2 ms | unchanged     | CV 7.5% -> 1.6% |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`     |        +3.1% |       +19.2 ms | unchanged     | CV 0.3% -> 1.4% |
| `line-prefixed-summary-batch-jumps`    |       +25.5% |       +11.5 ms | unchanged     | CV 1.8% -> 7.6% |
| `inline-split-file-path-batch-jumps`   |       +13.9% |        +8.2 ms | unchanged     | CV 5.1% -> 3.4% |

For LineClamp, the most important regression is `line-summary-batch-continuous`: it is a native
eligible multiline default-ellipsis row with no affix. The native implementation path and measured
DOM-read counts did not change between 1.4.0 and 1.5.0. The source-level difference is the component
shell: 1.5.0 moved LineClamp from a hand-written render function to an SFC/template shell and
`defineModel`-based controlled state. A concrete likely contributor is that the SFC template renders
the reusable `MultilineAffixSlot` functional component for both before and after positions even when
there is no slot content. In 1.4.0 the hand-written render function skipped those wrappers when slot
content was absent.

For the affix LineClamp and RichLineClamp rows, rect reads, resize callbacks, mutation records, and
component instance counts are unchanged. These regressions are therefore not evidence of extra
clamp probes. They are timing-only overhead in the same externally observable workload, most likely
from the SFC shell, the reusable affix-slot functional component path, and reactive style/render
boundaries.

Small WrapClamp regressions such as `wrap-table-demo-width-sweep` (+3.4%) and
`wrap-after-affix-shrink` (+2.6%) also have unchanged rect and slot counters. They are not the main
story and should not be treated as solver regressions unless a profiler shows new hot frames.

## Bottom line

1.5.0 is a clear WrapClamp performance release. The solver rewrite cuts the expensive work that
actually matters for wrapped-item scenarios: DOM rect probing and public item-slot invocation.

The regressions are real in the timing data, especially `line-summary-batch-continuous`, but they
are not caused by extra DOM measurement. They are component-shell/runtime overhead introduced while
migrating to SFCs and simplifying public typing. If those regressions matter enough to optimize, the
next diagnostic step should be an isolated commit-level run or browser profile focused on the
native LineClamp SFC path and affix slot render path.

## DefineRender follow-up experiment

After this analysis, `LineClamp`, `RichLineClamp`, and `InlineClamp` were migrated from authored
templates to setup-local render functions bound with `defineRender(render)`. `WrapClamp` was already
render-only. The goal was to test whether avoiding template-emitted `MultilineAffixSlot` component
calls would recover 1.5.0 timing regressions.

The package benchmark was rerun against the current workspace and published `vue-clamp@1.5.0` using
the same public matrix and report sampling mode:

| Component     | Published 1.5.0 | Current defineRender | Delta |
| ------------- | --------------: | -------------------: | ----: |
| All           |       9903.3 ms |            9975.5 ms | +0.7% |
| LineClamp     |       2230.9 ms |            2160.1 ms | -3.2% |
| InlineClamp   |       1715.6 ms |            1819.0 ms | +6.0% |
| RichLineClamp |       2162.0 ms |            2147.9 ms | -0.6% |
| WrapClamp     |       3794.8 ms |            3848.4 ms | +1.4% |

The intended Line/Rich recovery did show up:

| Scenario                               | Published 1.5.0 | Current defineRender |  Delta |
| -------------------------------------- | --------------: | -------------------: | -----: |
| `line-summary-batch-continuous`        |        166.3 ms |             142.0 ms | -14.6% |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous`      |        566.8 ms |             544.4 ms |  -4.0% |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter`          |        844.3 ms |             811.9 ms |  -3.8% |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` |        551.4 ms |             536.5 ms |  -2.7% |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`     |        640.4 ms |             627.8 ms |  -2.0% |

But migrating InlineClamp to a manual render function was not a win in this run:

| Scenario                              | Published 1.5.0 | Current defineRender |  Delta |
| ------------------------------------- | --------------: | -------------------: | -----: |
| `inline-path-middle-batch-jitter`     |        418.8 ms |             456.8 ms |  +9.1% |
| `inline-path-middle-batch-continuous` |        416.9 ms |             435.8 ms |  +4.5% |
| `inline-split-file-path-batch-jumps`  |         39.7 ms |              60.4 ms | +52.1% |

Counters were effectively unchanged in the defineRender comparison, so the movement is still
render/runtime timing rather than changed clamp probes. The practical takeaway is that render-only
SFCs are promising for LineClamp and mildly helpful for RichLineClamp, but should not automatically
be assumed faster for InlineClamp. If optimizing purely for current benchmark totals, keep the
LineClamp/RichLineClamp render-only migration and reconsider InlineClamp separately.

The deeper reason is that the experiment changes two different costs in opposite directions:

- `LineClamp` and `RichLineClamp` templates in published 1.5.0 always instantiate the reusable
  `MultilineAffixSlot` VNode path for both before and after positions. In no-affix rows this is
  pure shell work; in affix rows it adds a component boundary and prop patching around slot
  rendering. The render-only experiment removes or inlines that boundary, which recovers the
  targeted Line/Rich regressions.
- Authored templates also receive Vue compiler output: block tracking, patch flags, hoisted dynamic
  prop key arrays, and generated template-ref handling. Handwritten `h()` render functions do not
  get those compiler optimizations automatically. `InlineClamp` had no `MultilineAffixSlot` boundary
  to remove, so the experiment mostly traded a compiler-optimized template for fresh hand-built
  VNodes, props objects, children arrays, and function refs. That is why InlineClamp regressed even
  though its DOM-read and mutation counters were unchanged.
- The LineClamp recovery is partial because the 1.4.0 render path was not just render-only; it was a
  leaner hand-written `defineComponent` path. The current SFC path still carries `defineModel` /
  `useModel`, template-oriented computed boundaries such as `rootStyle`, `contentStyle`,
  `nativeMode`, `bodyStyle`, and `renderedText`, plus function refs for DOM nodes. The experiment
  removed the biggest avoidable template component boundary, but it did not recreate the entire
  1.4.0 runtime shape.

Most of the measured movement is in `updateMs`, not `settleWaitMs`. Counters for layout reads,
resize callbacks, and mutation records are nearly unchanged, so these deltas should be interpreted
as Vue render/patch/ref/slot overhead rather than browser layout or clamp-search work.

## Hybrid SFC render optimization pass

The follow-up implementation kept the public SFC shell constraint but stopped treating render-only
as universally faster:

- `InlineClamp` returned to an authored template with `useTemplateRef` because its runtime structure
  is static and the template compiler's block/patch/ref output consistently fits that shape better
  than a handwritten `h()` render function.
- `LineClamp` and `RichLineClamp` stayed render-only, but root/content/body/text/probe refs now use
  direct shallow ref objects for stable element refs. Function refs remain only for affix wrappers,
  where appearance/disappearance must schedule a reclamp after Vue commits slot DOM.
- One-use render aliases such as native mode, body style, rendered text, and slot props were moved
  out of `computed` effects and into render-local values, keeping `computed` for preparation work
  that is actually cached across reclamps.
- `LineClamp` also reuses stable style objects on the common no-`maxHeight` path and avoids rendering
  a null source-text placeholder when the visible text is not accessibility-rewritten.

The first full matrix after the hybrid pass showed the expected direction versus the previous
all-`defineRender` workspace run:

| Component     | All-defineRender current | Hybrid pass |  Delta |
| ------------- | -----------------------: | ----------: | -----: |
| All           |                9975.5 ms |   9091.9 ms |  -8.9% |
| LineClamp     |                2160.1 ms |   2071.6 ms |  -4.1% |
| InlineClamp   |                1819.0 ms |   1360.0 ms | -25.2% |
| RichLineClamp |                2147.9 ms |   1911.3 ms | -11.0% |
| WrapClamp     |                3848.4 ms |   3749.0 ms |  -2.6% |

Two repeated runs of the final code showed meaningful cross-run drift, especially in long
Inline/Rich continuous scenarios, so the conservative reading uses their average rather than a
single best run:

| Component     | All-defineRender current | Final repeated avg | Delta |
| ------------- | -----------------------: | -----------------: | ----: |
| All           |                9975.5 ms |          9530.1 ms | -4.5% |
| LineClamp     |                2160.1 ms |          2060.9 ms | -4.6% |
| InlineClamp   |                1819.0 ms |          1652.9 ms | -9.1% |
| RichLineClamp |                2147.9 ms |          2168.4 ms | +0.9% |
| WrapClamp     |                3848.4 ms |          3647.9 ms | -5.2% |

Against the published historical per-scenario best matrix, the repeated final-code average is close
to the goal but not uniformly best in every individual row:

| Component     | Historical best sum | Final repeated avg |   Gap |
| ------------- | ------------------: | -----------------: | ----: |
| All           |           9676.5 ms |          9530.1 ms | -1.5% |
| LineClamp     |           2075.5 ms |          2060.9 ms | -0.7% |
| InlineClamp   |           1628.9 ms |          1652.9 ms | +1.5% |
| RichLineClamp |           2126.5 ms |          2168.4 ms | +2.0% |
| WrapClamp     |           3845.6 ms |          3647.9 ms | -5.1% |

The remaining positive gaps are concentrated in a small set of rows, mostly within the observed
cross-run drift band: `inline-path-middle-batch-continuous`, `rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous`,
several Rich jump rows, and the small `line-title-single` row. The code-level conclusion is that the
clean hybrid shell is worth keeping, while further claims about exact per-scenario historical-best
parity need either same-process target comparison or a benchmark runner that alternates targets in
one browser session to reduce drift.

## Line and Rich focused probe reuse pass

A later LineClamp/RichLineClamp pass focused on the affix-heavy scenarios that still showed timing
pressure after the hybrid shell work.

The retained LineClamp optimization is deliberately narrow: when the previous measured text result
was clamped, the prepared boundary array is unchanged, and the root width has not grown beyond the
local-search window, LineClamp skips the separate full-source fit probe and lets the warm candidate
search include the full-source candidate. This removes one text mutation and one fit read from
stable clamped resize passes without changing the cold path. Large grows still keep the explicit
full-fit probe, and the search can still rediscover the full source when changed limits make it fit.
The text layout helper now requires that measured root width as part of its input instead of
falling back to its own root bounding-rect read. The package component path already had that width;
source direct Line benchmarks therefore moved their root bounding-rect reads to zero while keeping
client-rect reads unchanged, for example `direct-line-continuous-warm` 560 -> 0 and
`direct-line-jumps-warm` 109 -> 0.

LineClamp's native CSS overflow path now treats `clientWidth <= 0` as the only unmeasurable-width
guard instead of also reading `getBoundingClientRect().width`. Browser correctness tests still pass,
and package smoke moved native Line rows from extra bounding-rect reads to none:
`line-title-single-batch-sweep` 256 -> 0, `line-title-single-affix-batch-sweep` 256 -> 0, and
`line-summary-batch-continuous` 1120 -> 0. The same smoke run moved those rows' median active times
from 51.6 ms to 48.5 ms, 60.1 ms to 58.2 ms, and 215.7 ms to 197.6 ms respectively.

The retained RichLineClamp optimization keeps the hidden probe scaffold mounted across candidates:
the probe root keeps a stable content/body pair, affix clone slots are cached by source HTML plus
measured geometry signature, and the content child list is rebuilt only when affix presence or clone
identity changes. This preserves correctness for dynamic slot sizing while avoiding repeated affix
clone and `replaceChildren` work in metadata affix scenarios.

Rich probes now carry their measured width into `clampRich`. The hidden component probe has just
been assigned that width, and direct benchmark probes already know their current test width, so
`clampRich` can use the snapshot as the zero-width guard instead of reading the probe root's
bounding rect again. Source benchmarks moved `component-rich-continuous` bounding-rect reads from
220 to 110 and `component-rich-jumps` from 48 to 24; after making width part of the required probe
contract, direct Rich source rows also dropped their root bounding-rect reads to zero while keeping
client-rect reads unchanged. Package smoke showed the same component-path structural reduction:
`rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` 3520 -> 1760, `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter` 3712 ->
1856, and `rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous` 3520 -> 1760, with client-rect reads and mutation
records unchanged.

The source-level Rich clamp pass also replaced boundary path string comparison with direct path
array comparison. This removes repeated `path.join(".")` allocation on hot `sameBoundaryPoint`
checks. In `rich.browser.benchmark.ts`, median total time moved from 36.35 ms to 35.05 ms for
`direct-rich-continuous-warm`, 29.95 ms to 28.00 ms for `direct-rich-jitter-warm`, 41.60 ms to
36.85 ms for `direct-rich-dense-jumps-cold`, and 16.25 ms to 14.65 ms for
`component-rich-continuous`, with DOM-read and clone counters unchanged.

The shared layout-signature helper now builds the signature with a simple loop instead of
`map(...).join("|")`. This is intentionally a small allocation cleanup on the Line/Rich lifecycle
path. In a source benchmark comparison, text warm rows moved slightly positive while Rich rows were
mostly unchanged; DOM-read counters did not change, so this should be treated as a low-risk runtime
cleanup rather than a headline algorithmic win.

A final text-helper cleanup kept only changes that survived repeated source checks. ASCII grapheme
boundary preparation now uses a direct offset loop instead of `Array.from(..., callback)`, and text
fit checks opt into a narrow rect-count shortcut when only `maxLines` is active. Compared with the
post-`offsetWidth` source run, final direct Line rows kept the same DOM-read counts while moving
`direct-line-continuous-cold` from 107.20 ms to 101.00 ms, `direct-line-continuous-warm` from
44.10 ms to 40.70 ms, `direct-line-jitter-cold` from 53.60 ms to 49.80 ms,
`direct-line-jitter-warm` from 35.70 ms to 33.60 ms, `direct-line-jumps-cold` from 20.50 ms to
19.00 ms, and `direct-line-jumps-warm` from 20.70 ms to 19.50 ms. The same ASCII boundary change
also helps Rich preprocessing modestly in direct source rows, for example
`direct-rich-continuous-warm` 30.15 ms -> 29.40 ms and `direct-rich-dense-jumps-cold` 36.60 ms ->
35.60 ms, while component Rich timing stayed within observed drift.

Single package smoke runs after these micro-optimizations showed unchanged structural counters but
large timing drift, including slower native Line rows whose code path had not changed. Treat those
package smoke runs as shape validation only; source benchmarks are the stronger evidence for the
text-helper micro changes.

The remaining max-height-heavy package rows still carried root bounding-rect reads inside every fit
probe. Caching the root's visible top once per clamp pass, while continuing to read current
`clientHeight` for each candidate, preserved browser correctness and reduced those structural
reads in package smoke: `line-height-card-batch-jumps` bounding-rect reads moved 2976 -> 576, and
`rich-height-card-batch-jumps` moved 2715 -> 576. Client-rect reads and mutation records were
unchanged, confirming the search shape stayed the same while each max-height candidate became
cheaper.

RichLineClamp then adopted the same root-width stance as the measured Line path for component probe
sizing: the visible root width is read once and the probe receives that width as an explicit
snapshot. A dedicated fractional-width Rich browser test keeps this guarded. Package smoke showed
the expected structural drop without changing search counters:
`rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` bounding-rect reads 1760 -> 0,
`rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter` 1856 -> 0, `rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous` 1760 -> 0, and
`rich-height-card-batch-jumps` 576 -> 288.
The corresponding active times were mixed but generally favorable in that smoke run, while
client-rect reads and mutation records were unchanged.

Rich preparation also now builds text and fallback boundary points through one small helper instead
of keeping a hand-written loop plus `slice(1).map(...)`. Source timing was mixed within normal
noise, but this removes one avoidable allocation path and makes word fallback construction match the
primary cut construction exactly.

RichLineClamp then gained a guarded analogue of the Line full-fit skip. When the previous probe
result was clamped and the probe width has not grown beyond the warm-search window, the clamp pass
skips the standalone full-rich fit read and lets the coarse search include the full state as its
last candidate. A browser test covers the small-grow case where the full source becomes valid again.
Package smoke showed a structural client-rect reduction in the target component rows:
`rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` 8464 -> 6720,
`rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter` 11424 -> 9568,
`rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous` 8352 -> 6608, and
`rich-height-card-batch-jumps` 2427 -> 2283. Rich package median active sum moved 2090.4 ms ->
1982.5 ms in that smoke run. `rich-article-fit-batch` became slower with unchanged structure, so
that row should be treated as smoke timing drift rather than evidence for this clamped-path change.

Rich structural patching now has a narrow same-text-node fast path. When both the previous and next
states are clamped cuts in the same source text node, and the target prefix would not be normalized
by the generic trailing-whitespace trim, `patchRich` updates the live `Text.data` directly instead
of removing and cloning the same suffix again. The path is guarded against a root-level ellipsis
occupying the source text node's child index after a previous whitespace-only cut; a focused browser
test covers that boundary. Source Rich counters stayed unchanged after the guard
(`direct-rich-continuous-warm` client reads 2054, `direct-rich-jitter-warm` 1795,
`component-rich-continuous` 314), while same-process package A/B kept client reads fixed and
reduced mutation records: `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` 49824 -> 38544,
`rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter` 64240 -> 46336,
`rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous` 47296 -> 37648, and
`rich-dense-batch-jumps` 9148 -> 5434.

Rejected experiments:

- Replacing the rich affix clone cache key with `source.isEqualNode(clone)` made component affix
  active time worse, so the retained key is still source `outerHTML` plus geometry signature.
- Flattening the retained Rich probe affix state from `affixes.before` / `affixes.after` into
  top-level fields made the source benchmark slower with unchanged counters, so the grouped affix
  state remains.
- Adding object-identity short-circuiting to `sameBoundaryPoint` did not help Rich source
  benchmarks and made several direct jitter/dense rows slower, so structural point comparison stays
  on offset plus path equality.
- Adding a Rich affix source-identity fast path to avoid `outerHTML` on stable slot wrappers did
  not improve the targeted package `rich-metadata-affix-*` rows and added cache state, so the
  retained cache remains source `outerHTML` plus geometry signature.
- Reordering Rich full-fit probing ahead of layout inspection did not produce a clear win and would
  add an unnecessary fit read to unsupported-overflow cases.
- Replacing suffix child removal with `Range.deleteContents()` dramatically regressed direct Rich
  scenarios, so the simple `lastChild.remove()` loop is the preferred implementation.
- Replacing `lines.some(...)` in `fitsContent` with an explicit helper loop produced mixed text and
  rich benchmark results, including regressions in dense/component rows, so the original compact
  expression remains the clearer implementation.
- A last-line-first variant of that `fitsContent` loop also kept DOM-read counters unchanged but
  made Rich source timing flat to worse, especially component jumps, so it was rejected for the
  same reason.
- Applying the rect-count fit shortcut to the shared Rich path made Rich package/source rows mixed
  to worse. The shortcut remains opt-in from the text clamp helper only.
- Restricting the Rich rect-count shortcut to prepared trees without explicit `br` / `wbr` breaks
  still regressed Rich continuous, jumps, and full-fit warm source rows with unchanged DOM reads, so
  Rich keeps the full shared fit predicate.
- Branching candidate text generation to avoid start/end slice work looked promising in one run but
  regressed against the simpler ASCII-only version when repeated, so `displayTextForKeptCount`
  keeps the straightforward shared prefix/suffix construction.
- Repeating that idea as a narrower `displayTextForKeptCount` branch that avoided slicing the
  unused side for start/end truncation also regressed source timing with unchanged DOM counters, so
  the straight-line candidate builder remains the preferred measured shape.
- Caching Rich boundary point positions, replacing `sharedPath` with a prefix-reuse variant, and
  caching hidden-probe style writes all passed correctness checks but produced mixed or slower Rich
  benchmark rows; none were retained.
- Caching Rich logical runs by prepared source and atomic layout key slightly helped some continuous
  direct rows but regressed dense and component Rich source rows while leaving DOM-read counters
  unchanged, so the direct per-pass run construction remains preferred.
- Replacing Rich trailing `wbr` detection from `tagName.toLowerCase() === "wbr"` to direct
  `nodeName === "WBR"` kept DOM counters unchanged but regressed Rich source timing, so the clearer
  existing tag-name normalization stays.
- An early attempt to remove the multiline shell's `body` ResizeObserver subscription passed browser
  correctness but did not reduce package resize callback counts at all, so it was not retained at
  that stage. After the later entry-size guard excluded body entries from accepted signatures,
  direct body observation became an unused target and was removed.
- Reducing the multiline shell observation set to only the root and affix wrappers also passed the
  focused browser correctness tests, but package smoke showed unchanged resize callback and mutation
  counters. The timing movement also affected unrelated Inline rows, so it was treated as run drift;
  content observation remains part of the layout-change safety net.
- Changing the shared warm-search expansion limit away from two was rejected. A limit of one
  increased Line, Inline, and Rich warm-path reads and timing; a limit of three helped a few Rich
  component rows but regressed Line, Inline, and Rich dense/jump source rows. The existing two-step
  expansion remains the best measured balance for the shared search helper.
- Raising LineClamp's guarded full-fit skip grow window from 24px to 32px did not change source
  benchmark DOM-read counters, including the direct Line warm rows, and only added timing noise.
  The narrower 24px window remains because it already covers the measured small-grow paths without
  broadening the warm-search contract.
- Extending LineClamp's guarded full-fit skip to previous word-boundary fallback results did not
  reduce reads. A new source benchmark row,
  `component-line-word-fallback-continuous`, stayed at 867 client-rect reads with and without the
  fallback-boundary match because correctness requires the skipped full-source probe to reappear as
  the full candidate in the primary word search. The simpler primary-boundary-only guard remains.
- Lazily allocating Rich fallback cut arrays in logical-run construction looked attractive for the
  default grapheme path, but Rich source benchmarks regressed across most rows with unchanged DOM
  counters. The explicit empty fallback array remains the simpler and faster measured shape.
- Accumulating Rich logical-run text cuts directly while walking nodes avoided the temporary
  `currentTextNodes` array, but it did not change any structural counters and made focused package
  Rich smoke mixed to worse (`rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` 482.2 ms -> 496.4 ms and
  `rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous` 441.0 ms -> 450.8 ms in the nearby smoke runs, while jitter
  was effectively flat). The original flush shape is easier to read and remains.
- Pre-sizing the ASCII grapheme offset array by setting `.length` before filling looked like a small
  allocation win, but it regressed Text source rows and several Rich source rows with unchanged DOM
  counters. The direct `push` loop remains the measured ASCII fast path.
- Replacing the rest-parameter `combinedSizeSignature` helper with a fixed-parameter /
  `arguments.length` implementation passed checks but worsened Line, Inline, and Rich package smoke
  timing while leaving counters unchanged, so the clearer rest-parameter helper remains.
- Replacing the rich affix call to `combinedSizeSignature(source)` with a local single-element
  `offsetWidth` / `offsetHeight` helper also failed to improve the target shape. Rich source timing
  was mixed to worse, and package smoke moved the Rich active sum from 1982.5 ms to 2119.2 ms with
  unchanged DOM-read counters, so the shared helper remains both simpler and better measured.
- Removing the multiline native `clientWidth` guard was rejected after a browser probe showed that
  zero-width multiline content can still have positive `clientHeight` and large `scrollHeight`,
  which would falsely report clamping in hidden or unmeasurable layouts.
- Replacing the native `clientWidth` guard with `offsetWidth` removed tracked `clientWidthReads`,
  but it did not prove a real performance win because `offsetWidth` is still a layout read and
  focused native Line smoke was neutral to worse (`line-summary-batch-continuous` median active
  168.2 ms in the report baseline versus 187.7 ms in the nearby experiment). The explicit
  `clientWidth` guard remains because it is semantically direct and keeps the benchmark honest.
- Folding Rich same-run matching and fine-hint lookup into a `TextRunMatch` object removed one local
  non-null assertion but did not change DOM counters and made the filtered package jitter row slower
  in both same-process current/current reports. The more direct index helper remains.
- Reusing a same-run proof that the hinted text run end fits as the following coarse-search hint
  did not change Rich source counters (`component-rich-continuous` stayed at 311 client-rect reads,
  `component-rich-jumps` stayed at 152), so the extra local state was removed.
- Replacing RichLineClamp's short `nextChildren` array in probe affix synchronization with direct
  child-index branches kept structural counters unchanged and gave only mixed smoke timing while
  making the code larger and less direct. The compact array comparison remains.
- Lazily allocating the `fitsContent` line-group array only when `lineLimit` is active did not
  change height-scenario structural counters and did not produce a timing win in focused package
  smoke (`line-height-card-batch-jumps` stayed at 2043 client-rect/client-height reads and
  `rich-height-card-batch-jumps` stayed at 2283), so the simpler eager local array remains.
- Extending the Rich same-text-node patch fast path to trim trailing whitespace in place preserved
  counters but worsened source timing, and replacing the small whitespace regex with an explicit
  `charCodeAt` helper was also slower. The retained path only handles prefixes that do not need
  normalization and keeps the compact regex guard.

Package smoke runs after the pass kept the intended structural counters stable for the targeted
rows: `line-cta-affix-*`, `rich-metadata-affix-*`, and `rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous` all
reported zero `replaceChildren` and zero `cloneNode` calls on the public component path. The final
smoke run for the retained code moved the Line package sum from 2394.3 ms to 2092.1 ms and the Rich
package sum from 2448.9 ms to 2141.4 ms against the local pass baseline, with the intended measured
Line bounding-rect reductions preserved. Active time varied noticeably across full package smoke
runs, so these smoke numbers are useful for guarding work shape rather than as a precise single-run
timing claim.

## Same-process package comparison support

The package benchmark runner now supports `--targets <target-a>,<target-b>[,...]`. Multiple targets
are resolved before Vite starts, exposed through a virtual browser module, and run in one Chromium
process. For each public scenario, warmups and measured samples are interleaved by target. This does
not make browser timing deterministic, but it removes the larger process-start / browser-session
split that previously made small LineClamp and RichLineClamp timing deltas hard to interpret.
Measured multi-target samples now also stop only between complete target rounds. This preserves a
paired sample count for every target in a scenario: after `minRuns`, the round stops when all targets
have reached the minimum measured wall time, any target reaches the max wall budget, or all targets
hit the max run cap. That avoids the older tail case where a fast target kept collecting extra
unpaired samples after a slower target had already stopped.

Single-target runs still emit the original schema v3 `PACKAGE_MATRIX_BENCHMARK` payload. Multi-target
runs emit schema v4 with normal schema v3 report objects under `reports`; the matrix renderer
flattens those reports before building Markdown, SVG, and local JSON output. A short validation run
with `--targets current,current`, two measured samples, and no warmup produced two current reports,
each with 56 supported scenarios, and the report renderer successfully consumed that schema v4 log.
A later one-scenario duplicate-target smoke kept that two-report output while triggering only one
`vp pack`, confirming duplicate target specifiers are resolved once and then reused as separate
browser target entries.

The matrix renderer's low-confidence timing marker now keeps its statistics on the same footing:
`sampleMoe95ActiveMs` is a mean confidence interval, so MOE overlap is checked against
`sampleMeanActiveMs` rather than the displayed median. Adjacent timing deltas are also marked low
confidence when the median and mean active-time deltas point in opposite directions. A synthetic
two-version renderer validation intentionally set the median active time to improve (`100 -> 95`)
while the mean worsened (`100 -> 105`); the adjacent delta rendered as `~-5.0%` with
`median/mean active-time direction mismatch` in the confidence reason. This keeps the report's
median display while preventing mixed timing distributions from looking like normal wins.

The adjacent release summary now carries that same warning up to the aggregate row. Summing median
active time across scenarios can make noisy rows look authoritative, so the summary table includes a
`Low-conf active rows` fraction and prefixes the aggregate active delta with `~` whenever at least
one comparable scenario is low confidence. A synthetic two-scenario validation with one low
confidence row rendered `Low-conf active rows` as `1/2` and the aggregate active delta as
`~-12.5%`, while the scenario-level top mover still showed the specific
`median/mean active-time direction mismatch` reason.

A same-process short comparison of the retained current workspace against `vue-clamp@1.5.0` gave a
cleaner view of the LineClamp/RichLineClamp improvements than earlier separate-process smoke runs.
With two measured samples and no warmup, every public Line/Rich scenario was supported for both
targets. The final pass moved Line rows from 2372.8 ms to 1793.4 ms total median active time, with
bounding-rect reads 15776 -> 384, client-rect reads 42688 -> 26338, and mutation records
86509 -> 55864. Rich rows moved from 2214.6 ms to 1954.6 ms, with bounding-rect reads
16219 -> 288, client-rect reads 39432 -> 28304, mutation records 272788 -> 172130, `cloneNode`
calls 7808 -> 0, and `replaceChildren` calls 13792 -> 0. The largest remaining active rows are
still the affix-heavy jitter/continuous rows, but the same-process counters confirm the retained
Line/Rich changes are structural wins rather than cross-run drift.

The same runner now accepts `VUE_CLAMP_BENCH_SCENARIOS` as a comma-separated local filter. Terms
match exact scenario names, groups, or component names. A smoke validation with
`line-cta-affix-batch-jitter,rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter` and `--targets current,current`
emitted schema v4 with two reports and two supported scenarios per report, and the matrix renderer
successfully consumed the filtered payload. This keeps full release reports unchanged while making
Line/Rich hotspot loops fast enough to repeat during implementation.

## LineClamp visible-text render suppression

LineClamp's measured path already mutates the live text node while searching candidates and leaves
the final text in the DOM. The retained follow-up avoids turning every clamped-to-clamped result into
a second Vue render: the component now stores the visible text in a shallow snapshot, mutates the
snapshot field silently for text-only changes, and replaces the snapshot only when the hidden-source
accessibility structure or clamped slot state must change.

The structural effect shows up in the filtered package rows. Against the previous current smoke
baseline for `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter`, client-rect reads dropped 14407 -> 10727, after slot
calls 4080 -> 2240, and mutation records 25030 -> 17654. A focused same-process comparison against
`vue-clamp@1.5.0` with two measured samples and no warmup produced:

| Scenario                          | 1.5.0 active | Current active | 1.5.0 client rects | Current client rects | Slot/mutation signal                               |
| --------------------------------- | -----------: | -------------: | -----------------: | -------------------: | -------------------------------------------------- |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous` |     522.4 ms |       451.5 ms |               9616 |                 5840 | after calls 2272 -> 2272, mutations 19817 -> 12123 |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter`     |     786.4 ms |       494.2 ms |              18480 |                10727 | after calls 2240 -> 2240, mutations 33138 -> 17654 |

The comparison to 1.5.0 includes earlier retained changes as well as this render-suppression pass,
but the current-vs-current filter run isolates the new structural counter drop for LineClamp. Source
helper text benchmarks kept the same DOM-read counts, as expected, because the change is in the
component render commit path rather than the text search helper.

Line's text layout hint then adopted the same large-jump caution as Rich: `clampTextToLayout`
returns the root width that produced a result, and later layout passes ignore that warm hint when the
new width is more than 32px away. This removes the component's separate `lastRootWidth` cache and
keeps continuous/jitter reads unchanged while reducing stale-hint jump work. Source
`direct-line-jumps-warm` moved from 1277 to 1087 client-rect reads, and filtered package Line smoke
moved total client-rect reads from 28951 to 26338 with mutation records 57843 -> 55864.

A final Line shell cleanup computes the normalized location ratio once per render/recompute pass and
passes it through native-mode selection and measured text search. Source and package Line counters
stayed unchanged (`direct-line-continuous-warm` 1950 client rects, `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter`
10727 client rects), so this remains a maintainability cleanup rather than a structural performance
claim.

## RichLineClamp hinted same-run search

After Line's visible-text render suppression, the remaining Rich metadata-affix hotspots were still
dominated by client-rect probes. The retained Rich follow-up is deliberately narrow: when the search
hint is clamped and the before/after probe affix signatures are unchanged, `clampRich` first
searches inside the same text run that contained the previous boundary. It returns from that fast
path only when an internal same-run cut proves the next cut fails, or when the current run end is
already final because there is no later run or the next unsliceable atomic run fails; otherwise it
falls back to the normal coarse run search.

This keeps the optimization on stable-affix nearby resizes and avoids trusting it across slot
geometry changes or large cold jumps. Browser contract tests passed, and the source Rich benchmark
showed the intended component-path counter drop: `component-rich-continuous` moved from 498 to 314
client-rect reads with unchanged clone/replace counts, while direct helper rows kept their existing
DOM-read shape. The intermediate shrink-only version had stopped at 404 client-rect reads in that
same component row, so allowing same-run proof on nearby grows produced another measured structural
drop.

Filtered package smoke showed the same structural improvement against the immediately previous
current workspace:

| Scenario                               | Previous current client rects | Retained current client rects | Previous current mutations | Retained current mutations |
| -------------------------------------- | ----------------------------: | ----------------------------: | -------------------------: | -------------------------: |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` |                          6720 |                          5360 |                      56320 |                      49824 |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`     |                          9568 |                          7776 |                      71408 |                      64240 |

A same-process filtered comparison against `vue-clamp@1.5.0` with two measured samples and no warmup
then gave:

| Scenario                               | 1.5.0 active | Current active | 1.5.0 client rects | Current client rects | Other structural counters               |
| -------------------------------------- | -----------: | -------------: | -----------------: | -------------------: | --------------------------------------- |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` |     547.2 ms |       449.4 ms |               8464 |                 5360 | bbox 3520 -> 0, clone/replace 3520 -> 0 |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`     |     624.1 ms |       523.6 ms |              11424 |                 7776 | bbox 3712 -> 0, clone/replace 3712 -> 0 |

A subsequent same-text-node patch fast path cut Rich mutation records further. In the final
same-process comparison against `vue-clamp@1.5.0`,
`rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` moved client rects 8464 -> 5168 and mutations
65088 -> 38688; `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter` moved client rects 11424 -> 7760 and mutations
80688 -> 46336.

A final same-run refinement lets a hinted text run return at its end without falling back to the
coarse search when the end is provably final: either the hinted run is the last run, or the next run
is atomic and its complete inclusion fails. The text-next-run case is intentionally not short-circuited
because a partial cut inside that following text run may still fit. Source component Rich counters
nudged `component-rich-continuous` from 314 to 311 client-rect reads; full package report mode moved
RichLineClamp total client-rect reads from 28800 to 28304, with the largest row moving
`rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` 5360 -> 5168.

The same-run refinement is now the default for direct `clampRich` callers only when the supplied
search hint is exactly the current patched state (`hint === from`). This keeps RichLineClamp's
component path on its explicit affix-signature guard, while letting direct warm helper use the
already-safe same-state signal. Source Rich warm rows improved structurally:
`direct-rich-continuous-warm` moved client-rect reads 2054 -> 1302 and clone calls 1229 -> 477,
`direct-rich-jitter-warm` moved 1795 -> 1315 and clone calls 800 -> 320, and
`direct-rich-jumps-warm` moved 539 -> 499 and clone calls 220 -> 180. Focused package Rich smoke
kept component counters unchanged (`rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` 5168 client rects,
`rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter` 7760, `rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous` 4880; clone/replace
still zero).

The retained implementation also factors text-run point membership into a tiny helper, avoiding
repeated `fallbackTextCuts ?? []` allocation in the default grapheme path. This did not change DOM
counters, but source Rich timing stayed neutral to slightly positive and focused package Rich
counters remained unchanged.

A final code-simplification pass reused the internal full-state object, made the same-state hint
default explicit, and avoided iterating an empty fallback-cut array during logical-run construction.
Rich source counters stayed unchanged (`direct-rich-continuous-warm` 1302 client rects / 477 clone
calls; `component-rich-continuous` 311 client rects), and focused package Rich smoke stayed at 5168 /
7760 / 4880 client rects for the three retained Rich scenarios.

A follow-up no-op short-circuit in `clampRich` candidate application was measured and rejected.
Skipping `patchRich` when the probe was already at the full state or the same clamped point did not
move DOM counters, while focused package Rich smoke timing was mixed to worse
(`rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` about 501 ms, jitter about 547 ms, and inline markup about
449 ms median active time versus the retained nearby smoke shape of about 482 / 539 / 441 ms).
Source helper rows looked slightly positive, but the public component rows did not justify another
branch in the hottest candidate path, so the direct patch calls remain.

Guarding RichLineClamp hidden-probe style writes was also measured and rejected. The experiment only
assigned `width`, `maxHeight`, and `overflow` when the style value differed, but focused package
Rich smoke kept exactly the same structural counters: 5168 / 7760 / 4880 client-rect reads and
38688 / 46336 / 37792 mutation records for the retained metadata continuous, metadata jitter, and
inline markup rows. Median active time was mixed (`498.1ms`, `573.2ms`, `443.4ms`) against the
immediate baseline (`517.7ms`, `563.3ms`, `461.3ms`), with no counter evidence that the extra
branches removed real work. The direct style assignments remain because they are shorter and the
browser already avoids observable mutation churn for unchanged values.

A `samePath` reference-identity guard was tested after the earlier point-identity shortcut rejection.
It left every Rich source structural counter unchanged, including `direct-rich-continuous-warm`
at 1302 client-rect reads / 477 clone calls and component Rich rows at 311 / 152 client-rect reads.
Timing moved only within normal browser noise, so the path comparison stays as a direct length and
element comparison without an extra branch.

The package benchmark spies now also track `offsetWidth` and `offsetHeight` reads. This exposed a
blind spot in the Line/Rich hotspot rows: the multiline shell's layout signature was doing more
offset reads than the component clamp search was doing client-rect reads. A focused smoke run before
the shell change showed:

| Scenario                              | Client rects | Offset width | Offset height |
| ------------------------------------- | -----------: | -----------: | ------------: |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous`     |         5840 |        29408 |         27136 |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter`         |        10727 |        29120 |         26880 |
| `rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous` |         4880 |        17600 |         15840 |

The first retained shell change removed `bodyRef` from the coarse layout signature while still
observing the body with `ResizeObserver`. The content shell already summarizes body geometry for the
purpose of deciding whether another synchronous same-flush clamp pass is needed; root/content/
before/after therefore preserve the signature signal while avoiding one width and one height read
per signature.
The focused package rows kept their existing client-rect, mutation, slot-call, and ResizeObserver
counters unchanged, while offset reads dropped materially:

| Scenario                               | Offset width | Offset height |
| -------------------------------------- | -----------: | ------------: |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous`      |        22624 |         20352 |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter`          |        22400 |         20160 |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` |        26400 |         24640 |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`     |        27840 |         25984 |
| `rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous`  |        12320 |         10560 |

Browser contract tests still passed after the change. Active timing remained mixed, as expected for
smoke-sized browser samples, but this is a structural layout-read reduction with no counter
regression in the existing Line/Rich hotspots.

Removing the ResizeObserver-side layout-signature guard was measured and rejected. Although it
looked like a way to remove synchronous offset reads from ResizeObserver callbacks, the guard is
filtering component-owned resize notifications after a clamp commit. Without it, focused package
smoke showed broad duplicate work:

| Scenario                               |   Client rects | Mutation records |   Offset reads |
| -------------------------------------- | -------------: | ---------------: | -------------: |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous`      |   5840 -> 9536 |   12123 -> 15035 | 42976 -> 45216 |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter`          | 10727 -> 15207 |   17654 -> 22134 | 42560 -> 44800 |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` |   5168 -> 8688 |   38688 -> 66240 | 51040 -> 59840 |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`     |  7760 -> 11472 |   46336 -> 74640 | 53824 -> 63104 |
| `rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous`  |   4880 -> 8400 |   37792 -> 65040 | 22880 -> 24640 |

The ResizeObserver guard therefore stays despite its offset-read cost; removing reads there needs a
way to distinguish external size changes from the component's own settled clamp mutations.

Filtering ResizeObserver callbacks by entry target before reading a fresh offset-based signature was
also rejected as a standalone step. Because the browser reports signature elements in the focused
Line/Rich rows, the filter kept every structural counter exactly unchanged, including offset reads
(`42976`, `42560`, `51040`, `53824`, and `22880` total offset reads across the five focused rows).
With no measurable work reduction in that form, the extra `entries.some(...)` branch was removed.

The next retained version cached the last synchronous size signature per observed signature element
and compared ResizeObserver's `borderBoxSize` entry payload against that cache. That kept the
duplicate-reclamp guard while avoiding fresh offset reads inside settled ResizeObserver callbacks.
Body entries remained observed but were not part of the coarse signature, matching the earlier
body-removal decision; entries without a usable border-box payload conservatively triggered a
recompute. A focused package smoke kept client-rect, mutation, slot-call, and ResizeObserver
counters unchanged while cutting offset reads:

| Scenario                               | Active before | Active after | Offset reads before | Offset reads after |
| -------------------------------------- | ------------: | -----------: | ------------------: | -----------------: |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous`      |      499.5 ms |     389.1 ms |               42976 |              29536 |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter`          |      618.7 ms |     445.5 ms |               42560 |              29120 |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` |      503.8 ms |     398.6 ms |               51040 |              36960 |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`     |      566.8 ms |     464.7 ms |               53824 |              38976 |
| `rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous`  |      491.3 ms |     329.7 ms |               22880 |              15840 |

The browser contract suite now also covers repeated external container resizes for measured
LineClamp, proving the entry-size cache still detects pure ResizeObserver-driven width changes after
it has already accepted a settled callback.

That integer-size version was then corrected before finalizing because `offsetWidth` /
`offsetHeight` round to whole CSS pixels, and Line/Rich wrapping decisions can change on fractional
widths. The final Line/Rich path uses subpixel `getBoundingClientRect()` border-box signatures for
same-flush layout signatures and root/probe widths, observes ResizeObserver with `box:
"border-box"`, and compares entry `borderBoxSize` values quantized to 1/1000 CSS px. The focused
browser contract now asserts that a fractional Rich root width is preserved on the hidden probe
instead of being rounded.

The precision correction converts the remaining Line/Rich signature reads from offset counters back
to bounding-rect counters. In focused package smoke, client-rect reads, mutation records, slot calls,
and ResizeObserver callbacks stayed unchanged; offset reads became zero while bounding-rect reads
reflected the exact border-box measurements:

| Scenario                               | Bounding rect reads | Offset reads | Client rects | Mutation records |
| -------------------------------------- | ------------------: | -----------: | -----------: | ---------------: |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous`      |               15904 |            0 |         5840 |            12123 |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter`          |               15680 |            0 |        10727 |            17654 |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` |               19360 |            0 |         5168 |            38688 |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`     |               20416 |            0 |         7760 |            46336 |
| `rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous`  |                8800 |            0 |         4880 |            37792 |

This is the intended trade-off: keep the duplicate-reclamp guard and avoid integer-size precision
loss, even though the counter label moves from offset reads to bounding-rect reads.

The final signature key uses integer 1/1000 CSS px units rather than `toFixed(3)` strings. This keeps
the same subpixel sensitivity with less float formatting in the hot same-flush and ResizeObserver
guards. Focused smoke after the change kept structural counters unchanged and gave active medians of
`458.1 ms`, `567.6 ms`, `466.6 ms`, `510.2 ms`, and `411.5 ms` for the five hotspot rows above.

The shell then stopped observing `bodyRef` directly. The body entry had already been excluded from
the accepted ResizeObserver signature because content captures body geometry, so observing it only
added an unused target. Browser contracts and focused package smoke passed; structural counters in
the five hotspot rows remained unchanged, while active medians were `418.7 ms`, `481.0 ms`,
`423.1 ms`, `510.8 ms`, and `418.3 ms`. The max-height rows were also checked:
`line-height-card-batch-jumps` stayed at `2043` client-rect reads / `2043` client-height reads with
`83.2 ms` median active time, and `rich-height-card-batch-jumps` stayed at `2283` / `2283` with
`96.4 ms` median active time. Native-eligible Line rows were spot-checked as well:
`line-title-single-batch-sweep` had zero client-rect and offset reads with `39.5 ms` median active
time, while `line-summary-batch-continuous` had zero client-rect and offset reads with `119.7 ms`
median active time in a high-variance smoke sample.

## Rich warm-search expansion follow-up

The shared warm-search helper still defaults to two local expansion steps. A global expansion limit
of three reduced a few Rich component probes, but it regressed LineClamp CTA jitter
(`line-cta-affix-batch-jitter` client rects 10727 -> 11112 and mutations 17654 -> 18076 in the
nearby smoke run). A default limit of one was worse for LineClamp CTA rows
(`line-cta-affix-batch-continuous` client rects 5840 -> 6709 and jitter 10727 -> 13317), so the
shared default remains two.

RichLineClamp now passes a Rich-only expansion limit of three into `findLastFittingIndex`. Rich
logical runs are coarser than plain text boundaries, and the focused A/B showed a clean structural
drop without changing jumps:

| Scenario                               | Previous rects | Rich limit=3 rects | Previous mutations | Rich limit=3 mutations |
| -------------------------------------- | -------------: | -----------------: | -----------------: | ---------------------: |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` |           5168 |               5024 |              38688 |                  38016 |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`     |           7760 |               7472 |              46336 |                  44928 |
| `rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous`  |           4880 |               4784 |              37792 |                  37312 |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jumps`      |           2064 |               2064 |              10752 |                  10752 |

Raising the Rich-only limit to four shaved a few more client-rect reads, but every measured Rich
hotspot became slower in that run, including metadata continuous, metadata jitter, jumps, and inline
markup. The retained limit is therefore three, not because it is maximal, but because it gives the
best measured balance between fewer probes and less speculative local search.

## Rank-space warm hint threshold rejection

A later rank-space threshold experiment replaced the fixed 24px full-fit skip and 32px search-hint
windows with candidate-density estimates. Deterministic probe-cost matrices made the idea look
promising, but those matrices were only proxy models. Package benchmarks against the previous commit
showed the runtime change was not a proven optimization: the isolated full smoke matrix moved total
active mean `8882.3 ms -> 8846.7 ms` (-0.4%) while client-rect reads increased
`54114 -> 54664` (+1.0%) and mutation records increased `419660 -> 420918` (+0.3%).

Follow-up strict package A/B runs then localized the problem. Text `rankMoveError` in the search gate
reduced the `line-word-copy-batch-jumps` regression from `1584` to `1488` client-rect reads, but the
previous commit was still `1440`. Restoring the old full-fit rule while keeping rank-space search
proved full-fit was not the only issue. A stricter exact warm-probe gate removed the targeted
word-copy structural regression, but Line CTA rows still regressed badly when the dynamic full-fit
rule was present: `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous` moved `5840 -> 9900` client-rect reads and
`12123 -> 17069` mutation records; `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter` moved `10727 -> 14081` reads and
`17654 -> 23271` mutation records.

The broad experiment was therefore reverted. A narrower follow-up kept the fixed 24px full-fit grow
window and kept the fixed 32px search-hint window as the baseline for all boundary modes, then added
only one dynamic extension: `boundary="word"` searches may reuse a warm hint beyond 32px after an
actual resize has established the current rank-per-pixel slope and the predicted next rank remains
inside the warm-search local expansion coverage. The narrower rule is tied to the physical size of
word candidates rather than a global pixel constant; default grapheme inputs keep the fixed window
because broader rank-space reuse had already regressed dense Rich and CTA scenarios.

The proof matrix was rebuilt from fresh targets with before set to `c272f95^`
(`d712d38bd74544354bf5d8ee03e0f96ade68767e`) and current built from the candidate. Two package
scenarios were added to avoid proving only the old workload mix:
`line-word-long-token-batch-jumps` and `rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps`. They use word-boundary
long-token text with repeated width jumps larger than 32px, where the candidate rank density is low
enough for a wide pixel movement to remain a local rank movement.

In the final full smoke package matrix over 58 scenarios, structural wins were limited to those two
new word-long-token rows and there were no structural losses:

| Scenario                           | Client rect reads before | Client rect reads after | Mutation records before | Mutation records after |
| ---------------------------------- | -----------------------: | ----------------------: | ----------------------: | ---------------------: |
| `line-word-long-token-batch-jumps` |                     3120 |                    1584 |                    4560 |                   3184 |
| `rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps` |                     3600 |                    2160 |                   42480 |                  33600 |

Full-matrix totals moved client-rect reads `60834 -> 57858` (-4.89%) and mutation records
`466700 -> 456444` (-2.20%) with bounding-rect reads unchanged at `429832` and offset reads still
zero. Median active time moved `8999.3 ms -> 8919.4 ms` (-0.89%), but full-matrix timing still
includes unrelated noise from rows whose structural counters did not change. The stricter focused
matrix is the timing proof for the affected rows: `line-word-long-token-batch-jumps` moved mean
active `140.87 ms -> 118.67 ms` (-15.76%) with client-rect reads `3120 -> 1584`, and
`rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps` moved mean active `235.15 ms -> 168.28 ms` (-28.44%) with
client-rect reads `3600 -> 2160`. Risk rows stayed structurally unchanged in the same strict run:
`line-cta-affix-batch-jitter` stayed at `10727` client-rect reads / `17654` mutation records, and
`rich-dense-batch-jumps` stayed at `1770` / `5434`.

The retained bundle-size cost against the same fresh before build is `dist/index.js`
`86148 -> 91782` bytes and gzip `18368 -> 19598` bytes; declarations remain `7252` bytes / `1656`
gzip. This is a deliberate trade-off for a proven word-boundary large-jump workload, not a general
rank-space replacement for the fixed local windows.

A root-cause diagnostic pass clarified why the fixed local windows beat broader rank-space
replacement attempts in the existing workload. A temporary browser diagnostic replayed the actual
Line/Rich width sequences and compared pixel-local reuse, actual rank movement, and warm/cold probe
orders. In `line-cta-affix-jitter-grapheme`, all 140 transitions were inside the 32px fixed search
window, yet 19 steps had a modeled warm-search probe count higher than cold binary search (`9-10`
versus `8`). The package A/B still showed fixed warm reuse was faster than replacing it with a
probe-count gate: client-rect reads stayed `10727` with fixed reuse but moved to `13096` (+22.1%)
when dynamic search replaced the fixed gate. The missing cost in the rank/probe model is DOM patch
locality: warm reuse starts from the already-rendered text and often avoids a larger text reset even
when it performs one or two extra predicate probes. In `line-cta-affix-jumps-grapheme`, 24 of 27
transitions were outside the fixed window and moved 62-79 boundary ranks; warm probing cost `9-10`
modeled probes versus `8` cold probes, so the fixed cold decision matched the real large-rank move.

The same diagnostic showed the opposite word-boundary case that the retained dynamic extension is
meant to cover. In `line-word-long-token-jumps`, 30 of 34 transitions were outside 32px but actual
rank movement was zero; modeled warm search took 2 probes versus 7 cold probes, and the final rule
reused the warm hint for 25 of those beyond-window steps. In `rich-word-long-token-jumps`, 30 of 34
beyond-window transitions moved only 2 ranks; modeled warm search took 4 probes versus 6 cold
probes, and the final Rich rule reused the warm hint for all 30. This matches the strict package
proof: Line long-token reads fell `3120 -> 1584`, and Rich long-token reads fell `3600 -> 2160`,
while CTA jitter and Rich dense stayed structurally unchanged. The root cause is therefore not that
fixed pixel thresholds are theoretically optimal; it is that probe-count-only rank models ignored
DOM mutation locality and Rich patch granularity, while the fixed windows encoded a conservative
layout-locality contract for dense/grapheme inputs.

A broader temporary input-space scan then separated "dynamic has no value" from "the broad budget
gate is unsafe." The scan used real DOM measurement over Line grapheme ASCII, mixed emoji, pure wide
emoji, code-token, regular word, mixed word, long-token word, plus Rich regular-word and long-token
word families. It compared the fixed gate, the old `rank budget` replacement, a fixed-window plus
`rank budget` extension, a fixed-window plus exact local-rank extension for all boundaries, and the
retained current word-only local extension. The `rank budget` strategies did find the long-token
benefits (`word-long-token-large` `280 -> 100` client-rect reads and
`rich-word-long-token-large` `233 -> 143`), but they could not separate those wins from unsafe
beyond-window warm hints: `word-mixed-large` regressed `298 -> 356` reads after 29 beyond-window
hint uses, `grapheme-pure-emoji-large` regressed `274 -> 328` after 30 beyond-window hint uses, and
`rich-word-regular-large` regressed `278 -> 307` after 18 beyond-window hint uses. The exact
local-rank extension and the retained current word-only rule both produced the same structural
result in that scan: two winning long-token families, no client-rect losses, and total
client-rect delta `-195` with text writes `-108`. Dedicated low-density grapheme inputs did not
show additional safe wins beyond the current word-only rule.

The practical conclusion is that there is a real dynamic-threshold opportunity in the input space,
but it is not the old broad `rank budget`. A safe rule must be tied to the warm-search algorithm's
actual local expansion coverage and to an observed resize slope; expanding based on cold binary
depth admits far-rank warm starts whose probe order and DOM mutation path can be worse than cold
search. The retained implementation captures the proven word-boundary low-rank-density region and
leaves broader boundary expansion unimplemented until a matrix demonstrates extra wins that are not
already covered by current word-only local extension.

Displayed line count is a first-order input to that slope. A temporary DOM diagnostic replayed the
same width sequence with only `maxLines` changed. For regular grapheme text, average rank movement
per step grew from `12.67` at one line to `24.67`, `33.00`, and `54.33` at two, three, and five
lines. For regular word text, the same pattern held at a lower density: `3.33`, `4.67`, `6.00`,
and `8.00`. Long-token word text remained near-local despite more lines: `0`, `0`, `0`, and `0.67`
average movement for one, two, three, and five lines. This means a pixel threshold cannot be judged
without the displayed-line capacity; the retained word extension is safe because it waits for an
observed rank-per-pixel slope from the actual line count and text shape instead of relying only on
the raw width delta.

A follow-up diagnostic tested whether the positive-slope gate should use an explicit
`maxLines * warmCoverage` visible-line density threshold instead of the retained candidate-space
threshold. That looked plausible from first principles, but the DOM-read matrix rejected it. Across
regular-word, mixed-word, and long-token text; `maxLines` 1/3/5; and monotonic, plateau, and return
width paths, totals were `cold=1716`, `fixed32=1489`, retained candidate-density `1346`,
line-density `1393`, and a slope-interval variant `1376`. The explicit line-density gate kept the
long-token wins but discarded real one-line plateau wins: `regular-lines1-plateau` moved from `38`
reads back to `59`, and `mixed-lines1-plateau` moved from `45` to `57`. The conclusion is that
line count is a major part of the measured rank slope, but `maxLines` alone is not a sufficient
hard gate. The total candidate count still matters because it controls cold binary-search cost, and
because `kept / candidateCount` distinguishes a small visible prefix of a long source from a short
source where the same kept count represents a much denser rank space. Semantic `maxLines` changes
invalidate the component hint; the helper layer now also records the producing `lineLimit` on text
layout hints and rejects warm hint reuse and guarded full-fit skips when the next layout pass uses a
different line limit. A browser helper test covers the direct-call case by passing a `lineLimit=1`
stale hint into a `lineLimit=3` clamp and verifying the search does not warm-start from the stale
kept count. Focused package smoke after adding the identity check kept same-line-limit structural
counters unchanged: `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter` stayed at `10727` client-rect reads /
`17654` mutation records, `line-word-copy-batch-jumps` stayed `1440` / `3504`,
`line-word-long-token-batch-jumps` stayed `1264` / `2944`, and
`rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps` stayed `2160` / `33600`.

The identity review was then extended beyond line count. From first principles, a kept text rank is
only comparable when the fit predicate is the same: the same prepared text and root width are still
different predicates if candidate rendering, whitespace handling, vertical clipping, or before/after
slot occupancy changed. Text layout hints therefore now also record the active ellipsis, normalized
clamp ratio, spacing mode, `maxHeight` value, and an affix layout key built from observed before/after
slot box signatures. InlineClamp stores the same ellipsis/ratio/spacing identity before using its
guarded full-fit skip. RichLineClamp already reset probe state on `maxLines` / `maxHeight` prop
changes, but its warm search hint and guarded full-fit skip now also require the current hidden-probe
affix signature to match the signature that produced the previous probe state. Browser helper tests
pass stale text hints from different `lineLimit`, `maxHeight`, affix layout key, ellipsis, ratio, and
spacing contexts and verify the search does not start from the stale `kept=0` rank. Focused smoke
after this change preserved the known same-layout counters: `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter` stayed at
`10727` client-rect reads / `17654` mutation records, `line-word-copy-batch-jumps` stayed `1440` /
`3504`, `line-word-long-token-batch-jumps` stayed `1264` / `2944`,
`inline-path-middle-batch-continuous` stayed `4556` scroll-width reads / `10481` mutation records,
`rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter` stayed `7472` / `44928`, and
`rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps` stayed `2160` / `33600`. A full current smoke matrix over 58
supported scenarios completed with total client-rect reads `57538`, mutation records `456204`,
zero offset reads, and the same structural hotspot shape as the previous retained code.

One nearby invalidation idea was rejected: clearing text/rich/inline warm hints on
`document.fonts.ready` or `loadingdone` looked semantically attractive, but the initial `ready` path
fires during the benchmark's useful warm state and caused structural regressions instead of guarding
a real font metric change. Focused smoke moved `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter` from `10727` to
`12960` client-rect reads and `17654` to `22082` mutation records, `line-word-copy-batch-jumps`
from `1440` to `1584`, and `line-word-long-token-batch-jumps` from `1264` to `1504`. Future font
work needs evidence that it distinguishes an actual new font metric from the browser's initial font
readiness signal.

A later same-width font-metric diagnostic checked the narrower concern directly without relying on
`document.fonts.ready`: after an initial clamp, the host style switched between `14px Menlo` and
`22px Times New Roman` at the same root width. ASCII grapheme, regular word, and long-token word
cases were tested in both directions. Warm stale-hint and cold no-hint paths produced identical
results and identical structural counters in all six cases: ASCII grow `7` client-rect reads /
`8` writes, ASCII shrink `8` / `8`, word grow `6` / `5`, word shrink `6` / `7`, long-token grow
`7` / `8`, and long-token shrink `7` / `8`. This gives no evidence for adding font/style identity
to the text warm hint. Same-width font metric changes remain covered by live candidate measurement,
while broad font-event hint clearing stays rejected because it regressed real resize workloads.

That first-principles review also found one real LineClamp algorithm gap: a zero rank movement is
useful evidence, but it must not be extrapolated as "zero movement forever." The retained text rule
therefore records the observed same-rank width interval. A later width may reuse the warm hint when
it is still inside that interval or within the existing 32px physical locality window beside it.
Positive rank movement is still modeled as a rank-per-pixel slope, but only when the next resize is
no larger than the observed resize scale plus the fixed locality window, and only when the current
kept rank is in the low-density front of the candidate space. That density gate is derived from the
warm-search local coverage (`candidateCount / (coverage + 1)`) rather than from a benchmark-tuned
pixel number. It keeps the dynamic threshold tied to actual input scale and candidate density
instead of turning one zero movement or one shallow slope into an unbounded threshold.

A temporary Line input-space diagnostic then scanned 72 representative combinations across
grapheme ASCII, emoji, code-like tokens, regular words, mixed words, long word tokens, `maxLines`
1/3/5, and continuous, plateau-jump, wide-jump, and monotonic-return width paths. It compared
`cold`, `fixed32`, `sameRank`, positive `slope`, current `hybrid`, and bracketed-history policies
through real DOM `getClientRects()` counts. Before the density gate, the hybrid policy had real wins
on long-token rows but also over-warmed `word-regular-lines1-monotonic-return` (`37 -> 39` reads)
and `word-mixed-lines1-monotonic-return` (`36 -> 40`) because a shallow slope observed at a wider
width became too optimistic as the single-line regular-word text kept shrinking. After the density
gate, those rows returned to fixed/cold reads (`37` and `36`) while long-token wins stayed:
`word-long-token-lines1-monotonic-return` stayed `49 -> 28` and
`word-long-token-lines1-plateau-jumps` stayed `45 -> 20`. Total diagnostic client-rect reads moved
`2394 -> 2392` for the hybrid policy. This diagnostic is not a proof of the infinite input space,
but it adds explicit coverage for a previously missing region: high visible-rank-density word input
where positive-slope extrapolation should not be trusted.

The final strict package A/B against the previous HEAD kept the risk rows structurally unchanged and
improved only the intended Line long-token row. `line-word-long-token-batch-jumps` client-rect reads
moved `1584 -> 1264` (-20.2%) and mutation records moved `3184 -> 2944` (-7.5%); median active time
moved `150.2 ms -> 145.3 ms` (-3.2%) and sample mean active time moved `144.6 ms -> 136.2 ms`
(-5.8%). `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter`, `line-word-copy-batch-jumps`,
`rich-word-copy-batch-jumps`, `rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps`, and `rich-dense-batch-jumps`
were structurally unchanged in the same focused run. A full smoke package matrix over all 58 paired
scenarios then showed the only structural change was the same Line long-token win; total
client-rect reads moved `57858 -> 57538` (-0.55%) and mutation records moved `456444 -> 456204`
(-0.05%), with bounding-rect and offset reads unchanged. After the density gate, the full-smoke
sample mean active time moved `7828.2 ms -> 7833.9 ms` (+0.07%), which is not treated as a
regression because all structural
work outside the Line long-token row was unchanged and the affected focused row improved.

A broader observed-range rewrite for RichLineClamp was rejected. A temporary rank diagnostic for
the Rich long-token sequence `[640, 560, 620, 540, 600, 520, 640]` showed ranks
`[14, 12, 14, 12, 14, 12, 14]`, so Rich does not have the Line zero-movement gap in this workload.
Replacing Rich's existing positive-slope rule with an observed-range rule regressed
`rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps` structurally (`2160 -> 2304` client-rect reads in the pure range
run, and `2160 -> 2208` in a hybrid attempt). The retained change is therefore text-only; Rich keeps
the previous positive-slope rule that is already proven by the earlier long-token matrix.

A later first-jump pass addressed the remaining gap in the dynamic threshold model: the previous
positive-slope rule needed an observed resize before it could help, so the first large width jump
after mount still fell back to cold search even when the current visible rank density already showed
that the jump should stay local. LineClamp now allows `boundary="word"` warm reuse when
`ceil(abs(deltaWidth) * kept / rootWidth)` stays inside the warm-search local coverage and the kept
rank is still in the low-density front of the candidate space. It also requires the estimated cold
binary-search depth to be at least `localCoverage * 2 + 1`, so the dynamic path is only used when
there is enough search depth for a local warm start to matter. The same density proof lets growing
word clamps skip the separate full-source probe when the remaining distance to full text is still
