larger than local warm-search coverage. This is still tied to displayed line count because
`kept / rootWidth` grows when more visible lines fit more candidates at the same width.

The proof matrix added `maxLines: 1` and `maxLines: 5` package rows for Line/Rich word-copy and
long-token inputs. A same-session smoke A/B against the immediately previous implementation showed
structural wins only where the density model predicted them: `line-word-long-token-batch-jumps`
moved `1264 -> 1040` client-rect reads and `2944 -> 2560` mutation records, and
`line-word-long-token-lines1-batch-jumps` moved `1280 -> 960` and `2960 -> 2400`.
`line-word-long-token-lines5-batch-jumps` stayed `2160` / `3584`; Line word-copy at `maxLines`
1/3/5 stayed unchanged; all Rich word-copy and long-token line-count rows stayed unchanged. The
original risk rows stayed structurally unchanged in the final focused smoke:
`line-cta-affix-batch-jitter` stayed `10727` / `17654`,
`rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter` stayed `7472` / `44928`, and
`rich-dense-batch-jumps` stayed `1770` / `5434`.

A broader direct-helper input-space diagnostic then scanned 180 combinations across word regular,
word mixed-token, word long-token, grapheme ASCII, grapheme emoji; start/middle/end clamp ratios;
`maxLines` 1/3/5 plus max-height-only; and jumps, plateau, and return width paths. After fixing the
diagnostic to match the real old full-fit skip semantics, fixed 32/24px totaled `9445`
client-rect reads and `7783` text writes, while the current dynamic policy totaled `8736` reads and
`6942` writes. No row had current reads higher than cold. The remaining current-vs-fixed differences
were concentrated in long-token word rows: 21 winning rows totaling `-709` reads and `-841` writes.
Two regular/mixed one-line return-path micro-regressions found before the cold-depth margin were
removed by requiring enough cold binary-search depth; the only remaining mixed signal was
`word-long-token/middle/lines3/return`, which moved `78 -> 80` reads but `84 -> 78` writes. The
margin rule was kept because it removes regular-word over-warming without reducing package-proven
long-token wins.

Affix occupancy was tested as another first-principles input. A temporary Line direct-helper
diagnostic added fixed inline before/after affixes of `0`, `96`, `160`, and `96+96` px to regular
and long-token word inputs across `maxLines` 1/3 and jumps, plateau, and return width paths. It
compared the retained root-width density against an alternative that used
`rootWidth - beforeWidth - afterWidth` as the warm-hint metric. Fixed and current policies using the
root-width metric totaled `4327 -> 3541` client-rect reads and `4093 -> 3183` text writes. The
available-width metric produced `3557` reads and `3206` writes for the current policy, slightly worse
than root width. The conclusion is that affix geometry must remain part of hint identity, but it
should not replace root width as the density denominator in the retained Line heuristic.

Custom ellipsis and word fallback were also scanned because they change the candidate rendering
surface. A temporary Line direct-helper diagnostic covered default `…`, ASCII `...`, medium
`[more]`, and long `-- continue reading --` markers across regular word, long-token word, and
single-token word-fallback inputs; `maxLines` 1/3; and jumps, plateau, and return width paths. The
retained current policy totaled `6633` client-rect reads and `6374` text writes versus fixed
32/24px at `7517` / `7366` and cold at `8145` / `7998`. The structural differences were all
long-token wins across marker lengths; word-fallback rows did not differ, which confirms the current
primary-boundary guard still avoids reusing fallback grapheme hints as word-rank evidence.
That fallback input is now also represented in the public package matrix by
`line-word-fallback-batch-continuous`. The latest current smoke for that row recorded `443.8 ms`
active time in the targeted row run, and `408.2 ms` in the later full-matrix run, with `3072`
bounding-rect reads, `11230` client-rect reads, `15941` mutation records, and
zero offset reads. It is intentionally a guardrail rather than a claimed optimization win: the
direct-helper evidence says fallback rows should stay structurally neutral while long-token rows
carry the dynamic-threshold wins.

A later follow-up tested whether that fallback grapheme hint should also participate in the
guarded full-source fit skip. The idea was plausible because a fallback result stores
`fallbackBoundaryOffsets`, while the next `boundary="word"` layout pass normally rejects that hint
for full-fit skipping. The package row rejected the change: allowing fallback hints into
`canSkipFullTextFit` moved `line-word-fallback-batch-continuous` from the retained `11230`
client-rect reads and `15941` mutation records to `11461` reads and `16125` mutations. The retained
behavior therefore keeps fallback hints available only for the fallback search itself; using them
to skip the preliminary full-source fit creates more search/write work in this input family.

The public package matrix also now includes `line-word-long-token-middle-batch-jumps`, because the
direct-helper ratio scan showed that start/middle/end candidate rendering belongs in the input
space even though the dynamic hint identity already records the normalized ratio. The targeted row
run recorded `105.6 ms` active time, and the later full-matrix run recorded `101.6 ms`, with
`1440` bounding-rect reads, `2240` client-rect reads, `3664` mutation records, and zero offset
reads. This row guards the
word-boundary long-token win under middle truncation instead of assuming the default end-location
rows cover every ratio.

The public package matrix also now includes `line-word-long-token-affix-batch-jumps`, because the
direct-helper affix scan showed that affix occupancy belongs in hint identity even though root width
remains the better density denominator than `rootWidth - affixWidth`. The targeted row run recorded
`110.9 ms` active time, and the later full-matrix run recorded `115.7 ms`, with `2400`
bounding-rect reads, `2240` client-rect reads, `3424` mutation records, and zero offset reads. This
row guards the word-boundary long-token dynamic path while fixed before/after slot boxes reserve
inline space.

Strict A/B timing for the affected Line rows was kept focused on rows whose structural counters
changed. With 10 samples, the risk row `line-word-copy-batch-jumps` stayed structurally unchanged
while sample mean active time stayed effectively flat (`85.5 -> 84.7 ms`). With six samples,
`line-word-long-token-batch-jumps` moved median active time `128.5 -> 118.5 ms` and sample mean
active time `124.6 -> 111.3 ms`; `line-word-long-token-lines1-batch-jumps` moved
`137.0 -> 123.0 ms` median and `135.2 -> 122.3 ms` sample mean. The 95% relative margin of error
was still broad for the `maxLines: 3` row (`9.2%` before, `14.4%` after), so structural counters
remain the primary proof, but the timing direction now matches the workload reduction in both
affected rows.

Two wider variants were rejected. Applying the same first-jump density gate to default grapheme
searches did not change structural counters in the existing grapheme risk rows, so the broader rule
was not kept. Applying it to RichLineClamp's first unobserved rank hint also produced no structural
changes in the added Rich line-count rows, so Rich keeps its previous observed-slope rule.

A separate Rich direct-helper input-space diagnostic covered 48 combinations across regular word,
long-token word, dense rich markup, grapheme emoji; `maxLines` 1/2/5 and max-height-only; and jumps,
plateau, and return width paths. The component-equivalent current Rich policy totaled `3662`
client-rect reads versus `3800` for fixed 32px reuse and `4212` for cold search. Rich first-jump
visible-density and dynamic full-fit variants produced the same `3662` reads, so they did not add a
new Rich optimization. Two stricter variants were also rejected: a low-density rank gate removed
some small current-vs-fixed return-path regressions but raised total reads to `3720`, and an observed
resize-scale gate raised totals to `3677`. The current Rich rule is therefore retained: it is better
than fixed/cold over the scanned space, while the stricter gates remove too much useful warm reuse.

The retained bundle-size cost of the Line density gate plus dynamic full-fit skip is `dist/index.js`
`94700 -> 95715` bytes and gzip `20075 -> 20216` bytes; declarations remain `7252` bytes / `1663`
gzip. The final full smoke matrix now has 66 supported scenarios after adding the eight line-count
coverage rows. Excluding those new rows to compare the original 58-row shape, totals moved from the
previous `57538` client-rect reads / `456204` mutation records to `57314` / `455820`; bounding-rect,
scroll-width, and offset reads stayed unchanged. The eight new line-count rows add `12896`
client-rect reads and `87024` mutation records to the expanded matrix baseline.

Before the later zero-movement refinement, the post-revert full smoke package matrix compared
`vue-clamp@1.4.0`, `vue-clamp@1.5.1`, and then-current in one browser process. Relative to `1.5.1`,
then-current active time moved `11608.9 ms -> 10067.7 ms` (-13.3%), client-rect reads
`82120 -> 54114` (-34.1%), mutation records `641231 -> 419660` (-34.6%), and offset reads
`742556 -> 0`. Group active totals also improved: Line -19.1%, Inline -10.7%, Rich -13.6%, and Wrap
-10.2%. Relative to `1.4.0`, then-current active time was -34.5%, client-rect reads were -34.1%, and
mutation records were -24.2%. The built JS bundle returned to `86.15 kB` / `18.37 kB gzip`, with
type declarations unchanged at `7.25 kB` / `1.66 kB gzip`.

Other rejected follow-ups from this loop:

- Deferring `onUpdated` layout-signature reads while a multiline clamp pass was running preserved
  browser correctness but reduced only two focused rows structurally (`line-cta-affix-batch-continuous`
  bbox 15904 -> 15808 and `line-height-card-batch-jumps` 2304 -> 2112). It did not help Rich
  counters and made Rich active timing worse in the nearby A/B, so the simpler synchronous
  `onUpdated` signature read remains.
- Narrowing Line/Text hint reuse from a 32px root-width window to 24px did not reduce structural
  counters in Line or Inline rows, so the existing 32px search-hint window remains.
- Caching Rich logical runs by prepared source and atomic layout key helped one metadata continuous
  timing run, but regressed rich inline and jump rows with unchanged DOM counters. The direct
  per-pass run construction remains simpler and more predictable.

After the Rich-only warm expansion was retained, a full same-process report-mode comparison against
published `vue-clamp@1.5.1` over the Line/Rich public matrix showed no active-time regressions above
5%. Across 20 comparable scenarios, current total median active time was 3318.5 ms versus
4295.4 ms for published 1.5.1 (-22.7%). Client-rect reads were 54114 versus 82120 (-34.1%),
offset reads were 0 versus 415136 (-100.0%), and mutation records were 225434 versus 358145
(-37.1%). Bounding-rect reads were higher, 115792 versus 31963 (+262.3%), because the retained
precision work moved Line/Rich shell signatures from integer offset boxes to subpixel border-box
signatures; the active-time and mutation/client-rect totals still improved.

The final comparison's largest Line/Rich wins were:

| Scenario                               | Current active | 1.5.1 active |  Delta | Current rects | 1.5.1 rects | Current mutations | 1.5.1 mutations |
| -------------------------------------- | -------------: | -----------: | -----: | ------------: | ----------: | ----------------: | --------------: |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter`          |       478.4 ms |     836.3 ms | -42.8% |         10727 |       18480 |             17654 |           33138 |
| `line-height-card-batch-jumps`         |        79.9 ms |     118.2 ms | -32.4% |          2043 |        3312 |              3660 |            5526 |
| `line-custom-marker-batch-jumps`       |        82.5 ms |     122.0 ms | -32.4% |          2256 |        3888 |              3536 |            6000 |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous`      |       391.5 ms |     519.4 ms | -24.6% |          5840 |        9616 |             12123 |           19785 |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` |       426.3 ms |     541.6 ms | -21.3% |          5024 |        8464 |             38016 |           65088 |
| `rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous`  |       413.0 ms |     506.3 ms | -18.4% |          4784 |        8352 |             37312 |           60064 |
| `rich-dense-batch-jumps`               |        66.0 ms |      81.4 ms | -18.9% |          1770 |        1890 |              5434 |            9868 |

## Inline and Wrap exact-signature follow-up

The Line/Rich precision correction left one broader concern: `InlineClamp` and `WrapClamp` still
deduplicated layout work through integer offset-box signatures. That can miss fractional width
changes even when text wrapping or flex wrapping changes at the subpixel boundary.

A naive global replacement of the old offset helper with exact `getBoundingClientRect()` signatures
was rejected. It removed offset reads, but increased synchronous bounding-rect work everywhere and
made the focused Inline/Wrap comparison mixed, including a slower
`inline-path-end-batch-continuous` row in the local A/B.

The retained version keeps the exact signatures local to the two components and reuses the same
ResizeObserver-entry guard shape as Line/Rich:

- `InlineClamp` tracks parent and root subpixel border-box signatures.
- `WrapClamp` tracks root, content, before, and after subpixel border-box signatures.
- ResizeObserver callbacks observe with `box: "border-box"` and compare entry `borderBoxSize`
  payloads against the last settled signature instead of reading offsets.
- `WrapClamp` preserves its same-flush Vue update semantics: unchanged-geometry updates still
  invalidate measured item widths, while external geometry changes settle through ResizeObserver.

Focused package A/B against the previous offset-signature workspace kept mutations unchanged and
removed production offset reads:

| Scenario                             | Active delta |     Bbox reads | Offset reads | Mutations |
| ------------------------------------ | -----------: | -------------: | -----------: | --------: |
| `inline-path-end-batch-continuous`   |        -6.5% |  1824 -> 10880 |   25408 -> 0 | unchanged |
| `inline-path-middle-batch-jitter`    |       -27.0% |  1920 -> 11760 |   27360 -> 0 | unchanged |
| `inline-split-file-path-batch-jumps` |       -23.8% |    288 -> 1440 |    3456 -> 0 | unchanged |
| `wrap-table-demo-width-sweep`        |        +0.7% | 14400 -> 19000 |   20600 -> 0 | unchanged |
| `wrap-table-demo-width-churn`        |        -0.2% |  5800 -> 10800 |   16000 -> 0 | unchanged |
| `wrap-no-affix-shrink`               |        -1.8% |   5900 -> 7500 |    6400 -> 0 | unchanged |
| `wrap-no-affix-hidden-grow`          |        -0.4% | 23000 -> 25000 |   10000 -> 0 | unchanged |
| `wrap-no-affix-large-n`              |        +0.9% |   7120 -> 7600 |    2400 -> 0 | unchanged |

The retained trade-off is the same as Line/Rich: more explicitly counted bounding-rect signature
reads, but no integer-size precision loss and no offset-box reads in production clamp paths.
`WrapClamp` now also has a browser contract that changes the root from `151.49px` to `150.51px`:
both states report the same integer `offsetWidth`, but the component must reclamp because the third
50.4px item moves to the next flex line.

A final focused smoke after the browser contract and code simplification kept the same structural
shape: all eight Inline/Wrap rows reported zero offset reads, unchanged mutation counts versus the
retained A/B, and bounding-rect signature counts of `10880`, `11760`, `1440`, `19000`, `10800`,
`7500`, `25000`, and `7600` respectively.

## Inline visible-body render suppression

`InlineClamp` had the same avoidable work shape that LineClamp previously had: the candidate search
already writes the final clamped body text into the live DOM node, but the component then updated a
template-bound `visibleBody` string and let Vue patch that same text again. The retained follow-up
uses a shallow object snapshot instead. Clamped-to-clamped body changes update the snapshot field
without triggering Vue, while transitions between full and rewritten body text still replace the
snapshot so the hidden full-text accessibility sibling appears or disappears correctly.

A simpler `onUpdated` guard experiment was rejected first. It reduced Inline bounding-rect signature
reads, but the focused Inline smoke total moved slightly slower and the extra async recompute state
was not justified on its own.

The retained snapshot version was compared against the pre-snapshot current package by building both
local package directories and running them as two targets in one Chromium benchmark process. Across
the nine Inline package scenarios, it preserved scroll/search reads and reduced the structural work:

| Metric              | Pre-snapshot |  Snapshot |  Delta |
| ------------------- | -----------: | --------: | -----: |
| Median active sum   |    1817.6 ms | 1615.2 ms | -11.1% |
| Bounding-rect reads |        45106 |     36480 | -19.1% |
| Mutation records    |        76034 |     67324 | -11.5% |

The largest scenario wins in that same-process A/B were
`inline-path-middle-batch-continuous` active `457.1 ms -> 360.0 ms` and
`inline-path-middle-batch-jitter` active `489.4 ms -> 395.0 ms`; both also removed the redundant
Vue text-patch mutation records while keeping `scrollWidth` reads unchanged.

## Shared entry-signature helper

After Line/Rich, Inline, and Wrap all adopted subpixel border-box signatures, the remaining
ResizeObserver entry comparison loop was identical in three places. The helper now lives in
`layout.ts`, alongside `borderBoxSizeSignature`, so each component owns only the mapping from an
observed element to its last settled signature.

This is a maintainability change, not a new solver branch. A filtered package smoke covering
Line/Rich/Inline/Wrap hotspot rows kept the expected structural counters unchanged after the
extraction: Line CTA rows stayed at `15904` / `15680` bounding-rect reads and `5840` / `10727`
client-rect reads, Rich metadata rows stayed at `19360` / `20416` bounding-rect reads and `5024` /
`7472` client-rect reads, Inline middle rows stayed at `9120` / `9600` bounding-rect reads and
`14588` / `15687` mutation records, and the Wrap table/dynamic-before rows stayed at `19000` /
`42300` bounding-rect reads with unchanged item slot calls.

## Final hotspot polish

The last optimization loop kept three small, targeted changes and rejected broader speculative
paths that did not move counters.

RichLineClamp now uses the shared rect-count fit shortcut for candidate checks when `maxHeight` is
absent. This is conservative because `getClientRects().length <= maxLines` proves the candidate
does not exceed the line limit; `maxHeight` still takes the full visible-bounds path. In the focused
metadata smoke, this was timing-only but positive: metadata continuous moved about `428.7 ms ->
423.2 ms`, and metadata jitter moved about `484.5 ms -> 480.1 ms`, with client-rect and mutation
counts unchanged.

WrapClamp grow now has a uniform-width count hint before the existing materialized/live settlement.
The hint is gated to no-`after`, no-`maxHeight`, `maxLines` solves, and only uses a fallback width
when already measured visible item widths are positive, finite, and uniform within layout
tolerance. A deliberately mixed-width grow row kept the old structural counters (`12060`
bounding-rect reads, `8700` mutation records, `7980` item slot calls), while uniform grow rows
dropped expensive work. The local no-affix hidden grow A/B moved `25000 -> 16600` bounding-rect
reads, `16100 -> 9700` mutation records, and median active time about `251.6 ms -> 206.3 ms`; the
item slot count rose from `22300 -> 24300` because the hint jumps to a larger public prefix before
the final solve.

The same uniform fallback now seeds before-only grow estimates by measuring the current `before`
box and simulating `before + items`. This is only a starting point; if the final `before` geometry
or live layout disagrees, the existing settlement path still finishes the solve. The
`wrap-dynamic-before-grow` row moved from `42300 -> 16700` bounding-rect reads, `19100 -> 8300`
mutation records, `1800 -> 1200` before slot calls, `25200 -> 14200` item slot calls, and about
`305 ms -> 183-194 ms` median active time across focused smokes. `wrap-before-max-height-grow`
remained on the old structural path (`18000` bounding-rect reads, `1600` client-height reads,
`15000` mutation records), confirming the max-height guard.

LineClamp's native multiline style object is now cached per normalized line limit. This does not
change DOM-read counters, but it avoids equivalent style-object churn in native multiline width
sweeps. A temporary A/B on `line-summary-batch-continuous` measured the cached version at
`124.5 ms` median active versus `129.8 ms` after reverting the cache, with the same structural
counters.

InlineClamp now applies the same conservative full-fit skip pattern as LineClamp for warm clamped
resizes. It still restores the full body before measuring the inline-block width, but when the
previous result was clamped and the root has not grown beyond the local-search window it skips the
separate full-body `scrollWidth` probe and lets the warm search include the full candidate. A small
browser contract verifies that a narrow clamped inline value restores the full source after a small
width grow. The retained implementation also guards local `textContent` writes so repeated
candidates do not create no-op DOM mutations. Focused smoke rows moved as follows versus the
pre-change full-smoke baseline:

| Scenario                              | Scroll reads | Mutation records |
| ------------------------------------- | -----------: | ---------------: |
| `inline-path-end-batch-continuous`    | 6336 -> 4512 |   14512 -> 14064 |
| `inline-path-middle-batch-continuous` | 6380 -> 4556 |   14588 -> 14129 |
| `inline-path-middle-batch-jitter`     | 6930 -> 5010 |   15687 -> 15004 |
| `inline-path-end-batch-jumps`         | 2832 -> 2688 |     4256 -> 4112 |
| `inline-split-file-path-batch-jumps`  |   576 -> 432 |     1728 -> 1440 |

RichLineClamp's hidden-probe affix clone cache no longer serializes `outerHTML` on every affix
reclamp. The cache now uses source wrapper identity plus measured size signature. This keeps the
measurement contract focused on the box that can affect rich fit: if slot content changes but the
wrapper's measured box is identical, the old hidden clone is still a valid fit participant; if the
box changes, the signature invalidates the clone. Focused metadata affix smoke kept the same
structural counts (`5024` / `7472` / `2064` client-rect reads and `38016` / `44928` / `10752`
mutation records for continuous / jitter / jumps) while removing the hot-path HTML serialization.

## Late Line/Rich/Inline polish

Three small changes were retained after the next hotspot loop.

RichLineClamp now checks full-fit before rendered-layout inspection. Unsupported rich layout only
matters when the component needs to search and truncate; if the complete source already fits, the
unclamped result is correct without walking the connected probe tree for computed layout support.
Focused package smoke after the change moved `rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous` from about
`492 ms` to `410-428 ms` median active time. The metadata affix rows kept the same structural
counters but edged down from about `493.5 ms -> 466-484 ms` for continuous and `575.3 ms -> 530-567
ms` for jitter across focused smokes.

InlineClamp now avoids the pre-measure full-body restore when the root has an inline
content-independent `width` and the previous DOM already contains a clamped body. Content-sized
roots still restore the full body before reading the subpixel border box, preserving the grow
correctness contract. The fixed-width package rows benefited directly: `inline-path-end` continuous
mutation records moved `14064 -> 10416` and median active time moved roughly `486 ms -> 339-365
ms`; `inline-path-middle` continuous moved `14129 -> 10481` mutations and roughly `461 ms -> 348-366
ms`; middle jitter moved `15004 -> 11164` mutations and roughly `467 ms -> 371-402 ms`.

The shared text candidate renderer now specializes start/end truncation before slicing and trimming
the unused side of the source text. This is a pure helper simplification that leaves middle
truncation unchanged. Focused Line CTA rows kept the same fit-read shape but improved timing after
the extra string work was removed: continuous settled around `399-436 ms` versus the previous
`470 ms` focused baseline, and jitter settled around `517-552 ms` versus `569 ms`.

One nearby experiment was rejected: increasing the multiline text warm-search expansion window from
`2` to `3`. It slightly reduced continuous Line CTA client-rect reads (`5840 -> 5719`) but worsened
jitter (`10727 -> 11112`) and raised mutation records (`17654 -> 18076`), so the shared text search
window stays at the earlier value.

A final full package smoke after these changes reported zero offset-box reads, `419660` total
mutation records, and the expected top remaining hotspots: Line CTA jitter (`583.6 ms` median
active, `10727` client-rect reads), Rich metadata jitter (`537.9 ms`, `7472` client-rect reads),
Rich metadata continuous (`481.6 ms`, `5024` client-rect reads), Line CTA continuous (`425.6 ms`,
`5840` client-rect reads), and Rich inline markup continuous (`424.7 ms`, `4784` client-rect
reads). These are now dominated by real candidate fit probes, hidden-probe DOM patching, and
externally callable slot rendering; no further low-risk optimization was retained in this loop.

The next loop kept one tiny Rich patching polish: the trailing-whitespace regular expressions used
by `patchRich` are now module-level constants instead of being recreated during candidate suffix
patches. Focused Rich package smoke kept structural counters unchanged and measured
`rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` around `424-454 ms`, metadata jitter around `488-535 ms`, and
inline markup continuous around `396-410 ms` median active time across filtered runs. The current
full package smoke after this polish reported zero offset-box reads, `419660` total mutation
records, and `8499.6 ms` summed median active time.

A shared `fitsContent` line-grouping rewrite was measured and rejected. Replacing the readable
`LineBox + Array.some` code with parallel numeric arrays preserved structural counters, but package
timing was too noisy and not consistently better in the full matrix; keeping the original code is
the simpler maintainability choice until a same-process A/B proves otherwise.

A later text-candidate experiment that branched directly on normalized ratio `0` and `1` was also
rejected. It kept DOM counters unchanged but made the Line CTA focused rows slower than the current
straightforward `prefix/suffix` split shape, while Inline movement stayed within normal smoke drift.
The existing candidate builder remains the simpler measured form.

A WrapClamp render micro-optimization that skipped `resolveItemKey` when `itemKey` was `undefined`
was measured and rejected. It preserved item slot and rect counters, but focused Wrap package
smokes were mixed and made the table/no-affix hidden grow rows slower in repeat runs. The uniform
`resolveItemKey` call remains the clearer render path.

Two final Line/Rich structural probes were rejected after the retained regex polish.

First, the multiline shell tried reusing the layout signature captured by `onUpdated` for the
recompute that `onUpdated` immediately schedules. This cut bounding-rect signature reads in focused
package rows, but it reused a pre-clamp signature as the settled baseline. ResizeObserver then
observed the post-clamp geometry as a fresh change and scheduled duplicate work. The focused rows
showed the bad trade-off clearly: `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous` moved bbox reads
`15904 -> 10688` but client rects `5840 -> 6640` and mutation records `12123 -> 12923`;
`line-cta-affix-batch-jitter` moved bbox `15680 -> 12800` but client rects
`10727 -> 12647` and mutations `17654 -> 19574`; `rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous` moved bbox
`8800 -> 6288` but client rects `4784 -> 5456` and mutations `37312 -> 42256`. The final
post-recompute signature read is therefore necessary because it records the settled clamp geometry,
not merely the geometry that triggered the pass.

Second, a Line-only rect-count reject shortcut was tested for no-affix text candidates. The browser
probe confirmed ordinary Line content emits one `getClientRects()` fragment per visible line, but
the source benchmark did not improve: direct Line DOM-read counts stayed identical while
`direct-line-continuous-cold` slowed from the nearby `108.7 ms` baseline to `114.0 ms`, warm
continuous `41.7 ms -> 43.2 ms`, jitter cold `51.1 ms -> 53.5 ms`, and jumps cold
`20.4 ms -> 21.1 ms`. The extra parameter and branch were removed; the existing conservative
line-box grouping remains both clearer and faster in measurement.

A no-affix render fast path for Line/Rich was also rejected. It skipped affix-slot probing and the
children array when neither slot existed, but it made the render functions longer and did not show a
measured win. Source component Line continuous moved from the nearby `7.6 ms` shape to `9.4 ms`
with unchanged structural counters, so the straightforward children-array render shape remains.

A WrapClamp measured-width allocation cleanup was rejected as well. Mutating `measuredItemWidths`
in place during `measureCurrentSequence` avoided a per-measurement array copy, but same-process
focused package smoke kept every structural counter unchanged and moved the tested Wrap rows
slightly slower: `wrap-table-demo-width-sweep` `269.2 ms -> 275.7 ms`,
`wrap-no-affix-hidden-grow` `193.1 ms -> 199.1 ms`, and `wrap-dynamic-before-grow`
`172.9 ms -> 174.2 ms`. The copy-and-replace shape remains because it is simple and did not
measure worse.

One benchmark-tooling fix was retained from this pass. `BENCH_SCENARIO` lines now include the target
specifier, and the report renderer uses unique target-column keys instead of version-only lookups.
This matters for local same-version A/B runs such as a temporary package directory versus
`current`: both targets may report `1.5.1`, but the rendered matrix now keeps separate columns like
`1.5.1 vue-clamp-wrap-before.FPNCDw` and `1.5.1 current` instead of resolving both cells through the
same version key.

Those scenario lines now also include the core structural counters and compact `extra` counters
when present. A focused smoke over `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jumps`
(`/tmp/vue-clamp-bench-scenario-structural-line.log`) emitted
`bboxReads=1440.0`, `clientRectReads=2064.0`, `clientRectEntries=6048.0`,
`mutationRecords=9792.0`, and an `extra` payload with `resizeObserverCallbacks: 288`,
`afterSlotCalls: 288`, `beforeSlotCalls: 288`, and `componentInstances: 16`. This keeps useful
structural evidence in the streaming log even when the final package summary is not available.

The renderer also now warns and skips unrelated `.log` files that do not contain a package
benchmark marker. This keeps local verification loops from failing when renderer stdout/stderr is
written beside the benchmark log, while making a missing or crashed benchmark payload visible in the
terminal. Logs that do contain a benchmark marker but invalid JSON still fail loudly. It also now
uses the final benchmark marker in a log, matching the report contract when a captured file contains
more than one payload.

A text candidate micro-branch for `kept <= 0` was measured and rejected. It made the return value
more direct by skipping the empty suffix slice/trim, but source text benchmark movement was mixed:
some Inline warm rows improved slightly while direct Line cold rows moved slower with unchanged DOM
read counters. The existing shared candidate builder remains because it is already simple and did
not measure worse.

A WrapClamp root-style identity cleanup was also rejected. Reusing a stable `{ overflow: "hidden" }`
object when no `maxHeight` style is active kept every Wrap source benchmark structural counter
unchanged, but timing moved both ways: some grow/churn rows improved while `table-demo-width-sweep`
and several no-affix grow rows slowed. The inline root-style object remains because there is no
clear measured win.

A later RichLineClamp pass kept one structural improvement after the precision fix. The multiline
shell now updates its cached subpixel border-box signatures from ResizeObserver entries, and
RichLineClamp uses that observed affix signature when deciding whether a hidden-probe affix clone is
still valid. This avoids rereading stable affix wrapper bounding rects during width-only rich probe
rebuilds while preserving the conservative fallback when ResizeObserver cannot provide a border-box
size. A browser test now covers the important edge: a rich after slot keeps the same component-owned
wrapper but changes rendered width, and the component reclamps within the line limit.

Focused same-process smokes kept Line CTA structural counters unchanged (`15904` / `15680`
bounding-rect reads, `5840` / `10727` client-rect reads, and the same mutation records for
continuous / jitter). Rich metadata affix rows kept client-rect, mutation, clone, replace, and slot
counters unchanged while reducing bounding-rect reads: continuous `19360 -> 15840`, jitter
`20416 -> 16704`. No-affix `rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous` stayed at `8800` bounding-rect
reads, as expected because it has no affix clone to validate.

A following Line/Rich shell pass kept another structural improvement. The shell now passes the
subpixel root width captured by `onUpdated` layout snapshots or root ResizeObserver entries into the
component recompute callback. LineClamp and RichLineClamp use that fresh width snapshot for measured
search/probe sizing and still fall back to a direct root bounding-rect read for mount, font, or
semantic-prop requests that do not carry a fresh layout snapshot.

Focused smoke counters show the expected one-root-read-per-hot-pass drop with no change to search
shape: `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous` bounding-rect reads `15904 -> 13632`, CTA jitter
`15680 -> 13440`, `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` `15840 -> 14080`, metadata jitter
`16704 -> 14848`, and no-affix `rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous` `8800 -> 7040`.
Client-rect reads, mutation records, clone calls, and `replaceChildren` calls stayed unchanged in
the focused rows. Because the local machine had visible CPU contention during the run, these
conclusions are based on structural counters rather than active-time deltas.

A smaller follow-up kept the same settled-signature rule but narrowed the `onUpdated` pre-check
when the root border-box signature changes. In that case the shell schedules the same-flush pass
from the root snapshot and lets the post-recompute snapshot refresh content size. RichLineClamp
opts into same-flush affix signature refresh because hidden-probe clone validation needs fresh
affix box signatures; LineClamp does not, because its measured search reads the visible DOM
directly.

Focused smoke confirmed the narrower pre-check shape: `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous`
`13632 -> 9120`, CTA jitter `13440 -> 8960`, `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous`
`14080 -> 12320`, metadata jitter `14848 -> 12992`, and no-affix
`rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous` `7040 -> 5280` bounding-rect reads. Client-rect reads,
mutation records, clone calls, and `replaceChildren` calls again stayed unchanged.

A helper cleanup then split plain border-box signature formatting from signature-plus-width
snapshots. The hot `borderBoxSizeSignature` path no longer allocates a snapshot object when callers
only need the signature string, while root-width handoff still uses the explicit snapshot helper.
Focused counters stayed unchanged, as expected; this was kept as a low-risk JS allocation and
readability cleanup rather than a DOM-read reduction.

The multiline recompute callback shape was also simplified from a one-field context object to a
direct optional root-width parameter. This keeps the internal API matched to the single value the
shell actually provides and avoids allocating `{ rootWidth }` in hot root-change passes. The shell's
settled layout-signature reader now likewise returns only the signature string; the root
signature-plus-width snapshot is used only in the `onUpdated` root-change branch that needs the
width handoff. Focused structural counters stayed unchanged for the Line/Rich hotspot rows.
ResizeObserver entry handling now follows the same split: only root entries build a
signature-plus-width snapshot, while content and affix entries read just the signature string.

A follow-up WrapClamp experiment tried removing `onUpdated`'s synchronous layout-signature check and
always invalidating measured item widths on non-recompute Vue updates. Correctness held, but the
focused package smoke showed this was the wrong trade-off: `wrap-dynamic-before-grow` jumped from
the retained `16700` bounding-rect reads, `8300` mutation records, `1200` before slot calls, and
`14200` item slot calls to `45000`, `22700`, `1800`, and `26400` respectively. No-affix grow rows
also regressed structurally. The conditional geometry check remains because it prevents premature
live settlement while leaving real geometry changes to ResizeObserver.

The earlier current-only Line/Rich smoke after the precision and renderer checks did not expose a
new low-risk optimization target from timing alone. The dominant rows stayed in the same range as
the prior hotspot notes: Line CTA continuous/jitter measured about `401 ms` / `519 ms`, Rich
metadata continuous/jitter about `416 ms` / `506 ms`, and Rich inline markup continuous about
`379 ms`. The retained affix-signature change above came from the structural bbox-read breakdown,
not from treating a noisy timing cell as evidence by itself.

After a later local run was visibly skewed by VS Code CPU contention, the focused Line/Rich hotspot
rows were remeasured with two same-process five-sample package smokes. Structural counters were
identical across both runs, confirming the retained shape: CTA continuous/jitter stayed at `9120` /
`8960` bounding-rect reads and `5840` / `10727` client-rect reads; Rich metadata
continuous/jitter stayed at `12320` / `12992` bounding-rect reads and `5024` / `7472`
client-rect reads; no-affix Rich inline markup stayed at `5280` bounding-rect reads and `4784`
client-rect reads. Offset-box reads remained zero in all five rows. The two median active-time
ranges were: Line CTA continuous `429.4-460.2 ms`, Line CTA jitter `564.2-565.5 ms`, Rich metadata
continuous `436.5-437.4 ms`, Rich metadata jitter `494.3-536.0 ms`, and Rich inline markup
`421.4-464.6 ms`. CV values were mostly `4-8%`, with Rich inline still showing higher timing
noise, so structural counters remain the primary evidence.

Two additional Line/Rich cleanup experiments were rejected in that pass. Replacing
`Array.some(sameLineBox)` inside `fitsContent` with a tiny explicit helper kept every DOM-read and
mutation counter unchanged and did not improve active time in the focused package rows. Temporarily
disabling RichLineClamp's same-flush affix-signature refresh on root signature changes cut Rich
metadata affix bounding-rect reads sharply (`12320 -> 8800` continuous, `12992 -> 9280` jitter),
but it failed the browser contract where an after-slot wrapper keeps identity while its rendered
width changes. The component over-kept rich text because the hidden probe reused a stale affix
clone, so the conservative same-flush affix refresh remains necessary.

The next retained change targets the lower-cost native multiline LineClamp rows rather than the
measured CTA/Rich hotspots. Native multiline only used `clientWidth` as an unmeasurable-layout
guard before comparing `scrollHeight` and `clientHeight`; in root-width update paths the multiline
shell has already captured a fresh subpixel root width. `LineClamp` now passes that width into the
native multiline measurement guard, while native single-line still reads the text cell's own
client width because before/after affixes can shrink that cell independently of the root.

A same-process Line/Rich scan confirmed the structural effect was narrow. The hot measured CTA and
Rich rows kept identical bounding-rect, client-rect, and mutation counters. Native multiline rows
dropped their client-width reads without changing client-height, bounding-rect, or mutation counts:
`line-summary-batch-continuous` `1152 -> 0` client-width reads, and
`line-prefixed-summary-batch-jumps` `576 -> 0`. Native single-line rows stayed at `256`
client-width and `256` scroll-width reads, as expected.

Rich layout inspection now uses `Element.localName` instead of `tagName.toLowerCase()` for internal
HTML tag checks, including the `wbr` trimming path. This is a small JS-hot-path cleanup rather than
a DOM-read change: source Rich benchmark counters stayed identical, while median totals improved in
most rows in a same-process run, including direct continuous cold `50.20 -> 48.25 ms`, direct
continuous warm `18.10 -> 17.45 ms`, direct jitter warm `15.80 -> 15.20 ms`, dense warm
`38.40 -> 36.15 ms`, and component continuous `9.35 -> 8.80 ms`. A focused package smoke kept
Rich metadata and inline markup structural counters unchanged. Active-time movement in package rows
was still noisy, so the retained evidence is the source-level same-counter timing improvement plus
the simpler no-allocation tag check.

A related boundary-point identity fast path was measured and rejected. Checking `current === point`
before structural boundary comparison looked useful because warm hints often originate from the
prepared cut arrays, but the source Rich benchmark moved slower in most rows with unchanged
counters: direct continuous warm `17.45 -> 18.10 ms`, direct jitter warm `15.20 -> 15.75 ms`, and
component continuous `8.80 -> 8.95 ms`. The original structural-only comparison remains.

The shared fit helper's line grouping was revisited with a flatter `[top, bottom]` number array
instead of `LineBox` objects and `Array.some`. Focused package counters again stayed unchanged, and
the timing did not support the extra code: Line CTA continuous was flat/slower (`460.2 -> 464.3 ms`
against the nearby baseline), Rich metadata continuous moved `437.4 -> 447.7 ms`, and Rich metadata
jitter moved `494.3 -> 520.5 ms`. The original object form remains because it is shorter and
benchmarked better in the relevant package rows.

DOMParser reuse for `prepareRich` was also rejected. A browser microbenchmark comparing a fresh
`new DOMParser().parseFromString(...)` per parse against reusing one parser showed the cached parser
was not faster in Chromium: the interleaved median was about `195.4 ms` cached versus `179.0 ms`
fresh for the same HTML corpus. The current local parser allocation remains because it is simpler
and measured no worse for the browser engine used by the benchmark suite.

One tiny shared cleanup was retained: the border-box `ResizeObserver` options object is now a
module-level constant in `layout.ts` and is reused by Line/Rich, Inline, and Wrap observer
registration. This does not change layout counters, but it removes repeated same-shape option
allocation at every observer registration point and keeps the border-box observation contract in
one place.

After VS Code CPU contention skewed one local timing run, the hotspot timings were rechecked before
using them as evidence. Two source Rich benchmark reruns kept every DOM counter identical. The
measured medians moved within a narrow but visible wall-clock band: direct continuous cold
`49.9/51.5 ms`, direct continuous warm `17.9/18.6 ms`, direct jitter warm `15.2/15.3 ms`, dense
warm `38.1/37.6 ms`, and component continuous `9.8/9.1 ms`. This weakens any single-run timing
claim but reinforces that the retained Rich changes did not alter search shape.

The package hotspot rows were also rerun from the built package with fixed five-sample smoke
sampling. The stable rows were `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous` at `437.7 ms` active with `5.8%`
CV, `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` at `459.7 ms` with `6.4%` CV,
`rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter` at `530.5 ms` with `3.2%` CV, and
`rich-dense-batch-jumps` at `64.0 ms` with `0.9%` CV. The lighter native Line rows stayed noisier:
`line-summary-batch-continuous` measured `113.9 ms` with `23.1%` CV in the five-sample scan, then
`132.3 ms` with `17.8%` CV in a nine-sample rerun; `line-prefixed-summary-batch-jumps` measured
`40.4 ms` with `29.1%` CV, then `45.8 ms` with `26.6%` CV. All structural counters were identical
across reruns, including zero `clientWidth`, `offsetWidth`, and `offsetHeight` reads in those
native multiline rows. Future decisions should keep treating structural counters as the primary
signal for these light Line scenarios.

Two further Rich micro-optimizations were rejected after this timing recheck. First, skipping empty
text nodes earlier in `buildPreparedRichNodes` and sharing an empty child array made the preparation
path longer and did not change DOM counters; the source Rich benchmark moved flat to slower, so the
original straightforward preparation shape remains. Second, returning the shared `ROOT_PATH` from
`sharedPath` when two boundary paths have no common prefix looked like a cheap allocation win, but
it slowed the source Rich benchmark in the relevant rows, including direct continuous warm
`17.45 -> 17.85 ms` and dense warm `36.15 -> 39.90 ms` in the comparison run. The original
always-build-small-array version is both clearer and faster in Chromium.

A later affix-ref simplification experiment was rejected. The idea was to replace Line/Rich affix
function refs with direct ref objects and make the multiline layout signature distinguish missing
affixes from zero-sized affixes. Browser contracts still passed, but focused package counters were
identical in every target row: Line CTA stayed at `9120` bounding-rect reads, Rich metadata stayed
at `12320` / `12992`, slot-call counts stayed fixed, and mutation records did not move. The
repeat timing was mixed rather than convincingly faster: Line CTA continuous measured `436.2` and
`444.7 ms` against the nearby `437.7 ms` baseline, Rich metadata continuous `460.4` and `453.1 ms`
against `459.7 ms`, and Rich metadata jitter `553.7` then `531.2 ms` against `530.5 ms`. Because
the experiment pushed extra presence encoding into the shared shell without reducing work, the
existing function-ref side effect remains the clearer trade-off.

Another Rich preparation cleanup was rejected: carrying an incremental `childPathKey` through
`buildPreparedRichNodes` instead of calling `path.join(".")` for element keys. It removed one local
join call but added another recursive parameter, and the source Rich benchmark moved mostly slower
with unchanged counters: direct continuous warm `18.6 -> 19.0 ms`, direct jitter warm
`15.3 -> 16.5 ms`, jumps warm `6.1 -> 6.8 ms`, and dense cold `33.4 -> 35.9 ms` in the comparison
run. The existing `pathKey(childPath)` remains shorter and faster.

Top-level text candidate specialization for `ratio <= 0` and `ratio >= 1` was rejected. The source
text benchmark had a small mixed movement, with direct Line continuous slightly faster but Inline
and word-fallback rows flat to slower. The focused package Line CTA rows were a stronger negative
signal with unchanged DOM counters: continuous moved from the nearby `437.7 ms` stable baseline to
`596.5 ms`, and jitter moved from the prior `~530-565 ms` band to `698.2 ms`. The generic
prefix/suffix split remains because it is shorter and package-hotspot timing did not support the
branch specialization.

Skipping the multiline shell's settled root-signature read after recompute was also rejected. Source
component benchmarks looked attractive because `component-line-continuous` bounding-rect reads moved
`422 -> 281` and `component-rich-continuous` moved `332 -> 221`, with client-rect counts unchanged.
The package hotspot rows exposed the hidden cost: Line CTA continuous moved from the retained
`9120` bounding-rect / `5840` client-rect / `12123` mutation-record shape to `7648` / `6640` /
`12923`, and jitter moved from `8960` / `10727` / `17654` to `8640` / `12647` / `19574`. The saved
root read made the settled signature stale enough to trigger extra measurement and DOM churn, so
the post-recompute root refresh remains.

Replacing `point.path.at(-1)` in Rich patch positioning with direct index arithmetic was rejected.
The first source Rich run looked mildly positive with unchanged counters, but the repeat run moved
several hot rows flat to slower, including direct jumps warm around `5.9 -> 8.0 ms` in that local
comparison. With no structural counter movement and worse readability, the clearer `at(-1)` form
remains.

A `maxHeight`-only fit shortcut using `content.getBoundingClientRect()` was also rejected. It passed
browser contracts and converted Line height-card package reads from `1536` bounding-rect / `2043`
client-rect reads to `3579` / `0`, but the total layout-read shape stayed effectively the same and
median active time was neutral (`~106.9 ms` nearby baseline versus `105.9 ms` in the five-sample
experiment). Rich height-card did not benefit because that benchmark also has a line limit. The
shared fit predicate keeps the single `getClientRects()` path because it remains simpler and no
measured scenario justified the extra branch.

A final code-simplifier pass kept only local snapshot cleanups in Line/Rich hot-path guards: the
Line visible-text state and the Line/Rich warm full-fit skip checks now read their nullable state
once before branching. Source Line/Rich benchmark counters stayed unchanged and browser contracts
still passed. A fixed five-sample package rerun after the VS Code CPU spike showed higher active
times on the machine but unchanged structural evidence: Line CTA continuous/jitter remained at
`9120` / `8960` bounding-rect reads, `5840` / `10727` client-rect reads, and `12123` / `17654`
mutation records; Rich metadata continuous/jitter remained at `12320` / `12992` bounding-rect
reads, `5024` / `7472` client-rect reads, and `38016` / `44928` mutation records. All four rows
kept `0` offset-width and offset-height reads. The local active medians were `600.6`, `686.4`,
`583.3`, and `641.9 ms` respectively, while the source helper timings stayed in the normal range,
so active time remains environment-sensitive and DOM counters remain the primary regression signal.

Three follow-up micro-cleanups were measured and rejected. Replacing slot-content
`Array.some(hasSlotContent)` with an explicit loop kept all Line/Rich package counters unchanged
and produced mixed active timings; the loop version was longer and did not justify replacing the
compact expression. Switching Rich text-node reads from `textContent` to `Text.data` also kept
source counters unchanged but did not produce a stable timing win when repeated in the same
environment. Finally, cloning rich text nodes with `document.createTextNode(data)` instead of
`cloneNode(true)` failed to reduce the tracked clone counter and slowed most source Rich rows. The
existing slot filter and rich text patching code remain the simpler measured shape.

A later focused five-sample package recheck was run after moving shared Line/Rich affix slot
payload creation into the multiline shell. This pass used the current built package and the six
remaining Line/Rich hotspot rows: `line-summary-batch-continuous`,
`line-cta-affix-batch-continuous`, `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter`,
`rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous`, `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`, and
`rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous`. Active medians were `136.1`, `358.9`, `487.8`, `481.8`,
`549.1`, and `371.9 ms` respectively. Structural counters stayed on the retained shapes:
Line CTA continuous/jitter kept `9120` / `8960` bounding-rect reads, `5840` / `10727` client-rect
reads, and zero offset reads; Rich metadata continuous/jitter kept `12320` / `12992`
bounding-rect reads, `5024` / `7472` client-rect reads, and zero offset reads; Rich inline kept
`5280` bounding-rect reads and `4784` client-rect reads. This confirms the post-cleanup path has no
new structural regression. Remaining active-time hotspots are real but are now the expected
measured-search work rather than an obvious extra render, clone, offset-read, or observer churn.

The warm-search threshold model was revisited from first principles after the fixed `24/32px`
guards proved hard to justify across input scales. The important quantity is not physical pixels by
itself; it is how far the true last-fitting candidate rank moves, and whether starting from the old
rank costs less than a cold binary search. The search helper now exposes exact pure probe-count
estimates for both cold and warm search; unit tests exhaust candidate counts, hints, target ranks,
and expansion limits to prove those estimates match the actual `findLastFittingIndex` probe count.
Text layout hint reuse estimates the next rank from visible-rank density (`kept / rootWidth`),
same-rank width intervals, or an observed rank-per-pixel slope. Because that next rank is still a
prediction rather than the true browser layout boundary, the policy compares warm probes against the
cold binary-search probe upper bound instead of the exact cold cost at the predicted rank. A
target-exact cold comparison was tested and rejected after focused package rows regressed:
`line-cta-affix-batch-jitter` moved `10727 -> 10933` client-rect reads and
`line-word-long-token-batch-jumps` moved `960 -> 1040`; restoring the upper-bound budget returned
those rows to `10727` and `960`. The model also records two guardrails from the input-space scan:
only extrapolate across comparable width scales, and only when the estimated rank move is no larger
than the cold search depth. These guards removed wide-jump cases where a stale rank could cost more
than cold search.

The line-count concern is real, but the retained rule is not a separate hard
`maxLines * warmCoverage` multiplier. The primary signal is still the observed kept rank under the
current line limit: more displayed lines usually produce a larger kept rank, which raises
visible-rank density and makes the same physical width change predict a larger rank movement. The
later package A/B exposed a missing single-line case: regular `boundary="word"` text can grow by
many whole-word ranks in one width jump, so the `+2` patch-locality probe budget is now available
only when the predicted rank movement remains inside warm-search local coverage, or for larger word
movements when the active line capacity is greater than one and the estimated warm search remains
inside the bounded `warm <= cold + 2` probe cap. Single-line large-grow word searches must prove
`warm < cold`. This keeps the long-token and multi-line wins while removing the
`line-word-copy-lines1-batch-jumps` read regression against the fixed-window baseline.

A later line-count-focused same-process package A/B confirms the important distinction: line count
changes the width-to-rank slope, but it does not decide the optimization by itself. Across 14
Line/Rich word rows covering normal copy, long tokens, one-line and five-line limits, jumps, and
step resizes, the current rank-cost model moved total client-rect reads `20816 -> 19440` and
mutation records `138544 -> 136480` against the fixed-window file target. Normal word-copy rows
stayed structurally equal for both one-line and five-line cases:
`line-word-copy-lines1-batch-jumps` stayed `1680` reads / `2960` mutations, and
`line-word-copy-lines5-batch-jumps` stayed `288` / `864`. The wins came from long-token word rows,
where the estimated target rank remained cheap enough for warm search despite the width jump:
default long-token jumps moved `1584 -> 960` reads and `3184 -> 2400` mutations, one-line
long-token jumps moved `1280 -> 960` and `2960 -> 2400`, and five-line long-token jumps moved
`1712 -> 1280` and `3264 -> 2544`. Rich line-count rows stayed structurally equal in that public
matrix; the retained Rich beyond-window guard is therefore justified by the broader direct Rich
input-space scan rather than by current package rows.

The same first-principles review found one max-height-only gap: `maxHeight` creates a visible line
capacity even when `maxLines` is absent. The text helper now accepts a separate `lineCapacity`
identity/risk-budget hint. LineClamp derives it only when the prop max height is a pixel length and
the computed line height is numeric; it is not used for correctness, only to decide whether a warm
search may spend the bounded patch-locality budget. A direct helper A/B over a max-height three-line
grapheme case with fixed before/after affixes reduced actual `clampTextToLayout` work from
`619 -> 607` client-rect reads and `658 -> 639` text writes when `lineCapacity=3` was supplied.
The new public package guard row `line-height-affix-card-batch-jumps` covers the same input family
at component level; in the current package matrix it is structurally neutral versus the fixed-window
target (`6617` client-rect reads and `12850` mutation records on both sides), so this change is
evidence-backed for the helper input space but not claimed as a current package-row win.

A follow-up checked whether non-`px` CSS lengths should also be resolved into `lineCapacity` for
the dynamic policy. A temporary 72-row direct browser diagnostic compared the previous unknown
capacity against resolving `1.25em`, `2.5em`, and `3.75em` max heights for regular word,
long-token word, ASCII grapheme, and dense grapheme text; no-affix and fixed-affix layouts; and
jumps, steps, and return paths. Resolving those lengths was worse overall: total deltas were
`+9` client-rect reads and `+13` text writes. The only positive group was regular word text with a
fixed affix at `1.25em` on step resizes (`-2` reads), while dense/grapheme fixed-affix step groups
regressed by `+11` reads and `+7` writes combined, and regular word no-affix `1.25em` steps added
`+6` writes. The retained implementation therefore keeps `lineCapacity` inference to numeric and
`px` max-height values; arbitrary CSS lengths remain `undefined` for this hint until a broader
model proves lower total work.

The fixed comparable-width scale guard was also challenged directly. Temporarily raising the text
helper's width comparability limit from `2x` to `4x`, and then to no practical limit, did not move
structural counters in the package rows most likely to notice it:
`line-cta-affix-batch-jumps`, `line-word-copy-batch-jumps`,
`line-word-long-token-batch-jumps`, and `line-height-affix-card-batch-jumps` all kept the same total
`11321` client-rect reads and `23874` mutation records across `2x`, `4x`, and unlimited scale. The
source text benchmark, which includes direct helper jumps from `460px` to `180px`, also stayed
structurally identical: total rect reads stayed `16250`, and direct-line warm jump reads stayed
`1087`. The current evidence therefore does not justify widening or removing the scale guard; the
other rank-move and warm/cold probe gates already dominate the tested regions, while the `2x` guard
still documents that slope extrapolation is not trusted across completely different wrapping
regimes.

The word-boundary `front half of candidate space` risk-budget guard was then tested as a separate
hypothesis. Package word rows showed that a word-specific bounded risk budget is needed: disabling
large-move word risk entirely regressed the focused package set from `4416 -> 5056` client-rect
reads and `10656 -> 11536` mutation records, mostly in long-token rows. But the package rows did
not prove the old `hintKept * 2 <= candidateCount` half-space boundary itself: changing word
large-move risk to always allow the bounded `+2` probe budget kept the same `4416` reads and
`10656` mutations. A broader direct word matrix then covered regular, mixed, long-token, and short
word text; line capacities 1/2/3/5; start/middle/end ratios; jumps, wide jumps, step resizes, and
return paths. Against the old half-space rule, always allowing the bounded word budget for
multi-line clamps reduced total helper work from `26682 -> 26660` client-rect reads and
`25317 -> 25266` text writes, while strict no-risk moved worse at `26757` reads and `25764` writes.
The old half-space test has therefore been removed: for `boundary="word"`, line capacity greater
than one may spend the bounded patch-locality budget whenever the estimated warm search stays
within the exact `warm <= cold + 2` probe cap and the rank movement is no larger than cold search
depth. Single-line word clamps remain conservative because the earlier package A/B proved that
large single-line word grows should not spend this budget.

A temporary 1080-row browser diagnostic matrix covered typography and scale combinations that are
broader than the public package benchmark: regular word text, mixed word/code-like text, long-token
word text, ASCII grapheme text, dense grapheme text, and emoji grapheme text; `maxLines` 1/2/3/5 plus
max-height-only; start/middle/end ratios; serif/sans/monospace typography; jumps, wide jumps, steps,
and return paths. Against a pure fixed `32px` search / `24px` full-fit policy, the final rank-cost
model reduced total direct-helper workload from `37683 -> 36649` `getClientRects()` reads and
`36603 -> 34597` text writes. Against cold search, it reduced `39320 -> 36649` reads and
`38306 -> 34597` writes. The scan also found two missing dimensions. First, no-affix grapheme text
does not earn the broader patch-locality budget: dense grapheme moved from a `+19` read regression
to `0` after the budget was limited to strict probe wins unless affix occupancy is present. Second,
fixed affixes do change the trade-off for grapheme text: disabling the budget globally restored the
direct matrix but regressed `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter` to `12254` client-rect reads, so the final
rule kept affix-bearing non-word clamps behind a visible-line guard instead of making all grapheme
text eligible.
An affix-aware 432-row direct matrix then covered regular word, long-token word, ASCII grapheme, and
dense grapheme text across no/before/after/both fixed affix occupancy; line limits 1/2/5; three
ratios; and jumps/steps/return paths. It reduced current-vs-fixed workload from `16917 -> 16039`
client-rect reads and `16854 -> 15086` text writes, while showing that no-affix dense grapheme text
should stay on the strict probe gate. The package
single-line title affix rows also stayed structurally unchanged (`0` client-rect reads, `768`
mutation records, `256` scroll-width reads), while the three-line CTA affix row stayed at `10727`
client-rect reads / `17654` mutation records. By text
family, the final diagnostic deltas versus fixed were: regular word `-92` reads / `-212` writes,
mixed word `-17` / `-103`, long-token word `-929` / `-1693`, ASCII grapheme `+3` / `+2`, dense
grapheme `0` / `0`, and emoji grapheme `+1` / `0`. A same-rank plateau-probe prototype was measured
and rejected earlier: it helped a focused continuous-step example but increased total reads by
adding probes to dense grapheme and high-line-count inputs.

A narrower follow-up tested whether the non-word visible-line guard should start at two lines or
three lines. The 384-row direct browser matrix covered ASCII, dense CJK, emoji, and code-like
grapheme text; no affix versus fixed before/after affixes; line capacities 1/2/3/5; start/middle/end
ratios; and jumps, wide jumps, steps, and return paths. The previous three-line rule totaled
`77053` client-rect reads and `79036` text writes. A strict no-budget policy totaled `76999` reads
but `79340` writes, so it reduced measurement by paying more DOM writes. Allowing all multi-line
non-word text totaled `76901` reads and `78290` writes, but it regressed no-affix groups such as
dense five-line text by `+141` reads / `+69` writes and ASCII five-line text by `+29` / `+17`.
Starting the affix-only budget at two visible lines instead totaled `77007` reads and `78863`
writes, and produced no positive group delta in that matrix. The implementation therefore changed
the non-word affix rule from `lineCapacity >= 3` to `lineCapacity >= 2`, while no-affix non-word
inputs still need the exact warm-versus-cold probe gate.

A later DOM-state diagnostic split the same risk budget by whether the warm pass also skipped the
separate full-source fit probe. This matters because `skipFullFit=true` leaves the DOM at the
previous clamped text, while `skipFullFit=false` first writes the full source before searching, so
the patch-locality benefit is weaker. The 1260-row direct browser matrix covered short/long ASCII
grapheme text, dense CJK, emoji, regular word text, mixed word/code tokens, and long-token word
text; affix widths `0/16/64/160/240`; line capacities `1/2/3/5`; start/middle/end ratios; and
jumps, steps, and return paths. Current totaled `157888` client-rect reads and `152476` text writes.
Restricting the large-move budget to `skipFullFit=true` globally improved totals to `157735` /
`152317`, but regressed high-line long-token word groups because word long-token searches still
benefit from warm rank locality after a full-text probe. The accepted narrower policy keeps word
behavior unchanged and applies the `skipFullFit=true` requirement only to non-word affix budget:
`157713` reads and `152299` writes, with no positive group delta in that matrix. Other candidates
were rejected: search-only budget regressed totals to `159966` / `157472`, affix-width-ratio gating
improved reads but raised writes to `153163`, and all-multi-line budget reduced writes but increased
reads and kept known no-affix dense regressions. The implementation therefore treats DOM starting
state as part of the non-word patch-locality proof.

Focused package smoke rows confirmed the retained model on the public component shape using the
current benchmark matrix against a file target built from the fixed-window HEAD. The 17 Line/Rich
focus rows moved from `40785 -> 39409` client-rect reads and `206560 -> 204496` mutation records.
The risk rows stayed structurally flat: `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter` remained `10727` client-rect
reads / `17654` mutation records, `line-word-copy-batch-jumps` remained `1440` / `3504`, and
`line-word-copy-lines1-batch-jumps` returned to the fixed-window shape at `1680` / `2960`.
Long-token word rows carried the structural win: `line-word-long-token-batch-jumps` moved
`1584 -> 960` client-rect reads and `3184 -> 2400` mutation records,
`line-word-long-token-lines1-batch-jumps` moved `1280 -> 960` and `2960 -> 2400`, and
`line-word-long-token-lines5-batch-jumps` moved `1712 -> 1280` and `3264 -> 2544`. Rich rows stayed
structurally unchanged in the same run, confirming that the rejected Rich cost-model experiment was
not retained.

After the DOM-state guard was applied to non-word affix budget, a focused package smoke kept the
main risk rows structurally unchanged (`line-cta-affix-batch-jitter` at `10727` reads / `17654`
mutations, `line-cta-affix-batch-jumps` at `2304` / `5120`, and the Line long-token rows at
`960` / `2400` and `1280` / `2544`). The max-height affix guard row improved from the previous
current shape to `6569` client-rect reads and `12802` mutations, a `-48` / `-48` structural delta,
because that component path can prove a clamped-to-clamped warm pass and keep the DOM out of the
full-text reset path.

RichLineClamp's beyond-window word hint then received a narrower structural guard after a direct
input-space scan exposed atomic inline regressions. The final 192-row Rich direct matrix reduced
current-vs-fixed workload from `9244 -> 8653` client-rect reads, and cold search was higher at
`9699`. The guard only trusts a previous clamped point when it resolves to meaningful text inside
the prepared source; whitespace-only text points are accepted for normal text separators but
rejected when adjacent to inline-atomic neighbors such as `inline-block` spans. This preserves the
long-token rich cases while avoiding the atomic whitespace false signal. The focused package Rich
rows stayed structurally unchanged after the guard, including `rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps`
at `2160` reads / `33600` mutations and `rich-word-long-token-lines5-batch-jumps` at `2480` /
`27040`.

A stricter Rich variant that reused the text helper's exact warm-versus-cold probe-count gate was
also tested and rejected. On the same machine over eight Rich word package rows, the existing
local-coverage gate totaled `12032` client-rect reads, `130336` mutation records, and `848.0 ms`
active time. The exact probe-count gate totaled `12688` reads, `134640` mutations, and `886.5 ms`.
The losses came from the low-rank long-token rows where the local Rich state still had useful patch
locality even when the pure probe estimator was more conservative:
`rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps` added `+240` reads / `+1520` mutations, one-line long-token added
`+240` / `+1200`, and five-line long-token added `+128` / `+1408`. The retained Rich rule therefore
uses local rank coverage plus the meaningful-text guard instead of a pure probe-count comparison.

A later first-principles pass separated RichLineClamp's search-hint question from its preliminary
full-fit read. `clampRich` must still patch the hidden probe to the full rich tree before layout
inspection, so skipping the full-fit check does not remove DOM patch work; it only removes a
redundant `fitsContent` read when the previous clamped state and observed word-rank slope still
predict a clamped target. The full state remains included as a normal coarse-search candidate when
`skipFullFit=true`, so the rank prediction is a cost hint rather than a correctness shortcut. A
temporary 120-scenario Rich direct matrix covered inline/dense grapheme, regular/long-token/atomic
word HTML, affix widths `0/96`, `maxLines` `1/2/5`, max-height-only, and jumps/steps/return paths.
Against the fixed `32px` full-fit gate, the dynamic full-fit skip reduced total direct work from
`16326 -> 15867` client-rect reads with no increase in clone or `replaceChildren` calls. Grouping
the same diagnostic by visible-line policy showed the expected line-count relationship:
`lines1` improved by `-167` reads, `lines2` by `-118`, `lines5` by `-56`, and max-height `44px` by
`-118` versus fixed. The line count is therefore not ignored; it is represented by the observed
rank-per-pixel slope, where more visible lines usually mean the same width grow moves more rich
boundary ranks and reaches the full candidate sooner.

The public Rich package rows then confirmed that this direct-helper effect reaches user-facing
component scenarios. In a same-machine focused smoke A/B, temporarily restoring the fixed `32px`
Rich full-fit gate produced `23461` client-rect reads and `1278.8 ms` active time across nine Rich
rows. Restoring the dynamic full-fit skip produced `22453` client-rect reads and `1223.0 ms`, a
`-1008` read (`-4.3%`) and `-55.8 ms` (`-4.4%`) focused reduction. The affected rows were all
word-boundary width-jump cases: regular word copy moved `1968 -> 1824` reads, one-line word copy
`1920 -> 1776`, long-token default `2160 -> 1920`, long-token one-line `2160 -> 1920`, and
long-token five-line `2480 -> 2240`. Dense grapheme, metadata-affix, and height-card rows stayed
structurally unchanged, so the retained rule broadens only the input region with direct and public
counter evidence.

The remaining Rich full-fit skip risk is the transition from a clamped result back to a full-fit
result: if rank extrapolation says "still clamped" but the browser can already fit the whole rich
source, skipping the preliminary full-fit read can turn one cheap read into a search. A temporary
54-scenario diagnostic targeted that boundary with short/regular/long-token word HTML, affix widths
`0/96`, line limits `1/2/5`, and grow-to-full, jump-to-full, and wide-return paths. Current dynamic
skip still reduced total direct reads from fixed `32px` (`1437 -> 1337`) with identical full-result
counts, but it exposed two first-transition micro-regressions of `+1` read each. Three alternatives
were tested and rejected: requiring one extra rank of distance from the full candidate totaled
`1340` reads, requiring local-coverage distance totaled `1343`, and remembering previously observed
full-fit widths did not change totals because the regressions happened on first entry into the
full-fit region. The retained rule therefore remains the total-work winner, and the newly discovered
boundary is now covered by public package rows rather than hidden in a temporary diagnostic.

A follow-up atomic-inline variant checked the specific concern that `canSkipFullRichFit` does not
reuse the same meaningful-text guard as Rich search hints. The temporary 36-row direct matrix covered
three word-boundary rich sources with `inline-block` atomic spans, line limits `1/2/5`, and
grow-to-full, return-to-full, step-to-full, and wide-jump-to-full paths. Current dynamic full-fit
skip was still better than fixed `32px` full-fit gating overall: `1231 -> 1203` client-rect reads,
with identical full-result counts (`98`). A fully guarded variant that refused non-meaningful text
points was worse at `1214` reads. The scan did expose one narrow current regression:
`textAtomicText lines5 growFull` moved `33 -> 37` reads; a high-line atomic-only guard fixed that
row and totaled `1202` reads, only one read better than current. That condition was not retained
because it was too narrow relative to the evidence and would add another empirical branch without a
clear physical rule. The durable conclusion is that atomic rich full-fit transitions are now
covered by a rejected-path diagnostic, but not enough evidence exists to change the current rule.

The search-hint side of the Rich atomic guard then exposed a real coverage gap: the component-level
meaningful-text check looked at the parsed source node and inline `style`, while Rich's actual
logical runs are built from computed style. That meant a class-styled `inline-block` atom could be
seen as atomic by `inspectLayout` but invisible to the warm-hint safety check. The fix moves the
safe-text signal into `clampRich`, where the result is computed from the same logical runs that
drive the search. A focused public row,
`rich-word-class-atomic-batch-jumps`, covers two class-styled inline-block tokens separated by
whitespace. With the fixed guard, the row recorded `1440` bounding-rect reads, `1840` client-rect
reads, and `11760` mutation records. Temporarily forcing that safe-text flag to `true`, matching
the old over-trusting behavior for this class-styled atomic shape, kept bounding-rect reads at
`1440` but raised client-rect reads to `2720` and mutation records to `12720`. The accepted guard
therefore removes `880` client-rect reads (`-32.4%`) and `960` mutation records (`-7.5%`) in the
newly covered input family.

The same class-styled atomic row was also used to re-challenge `canSkipFullRichFit`, because that
path still does not use the safe-text flag. Temporarily requiring `textRankSafe` there was worse:
the row moved from the retained `1840` client-rect reads and `11760` mutation records to `2160`
reads and `12800` mutations. The earlier direct-matrix rejection of a fully guarded Rich full-fit
skip therefore still holds for the new class-styled atomic input family; search-hint reuse and
preliminary full-fit skipping have different cost shapes and should not share the same guard.

A later source audit found that this guard had drifted into the wrong branch during iteration:
`textRankSafe` was being applied to Rich full-fit skipping, while beyond-window Rich search-hint
reuse did not check it. Re-running the same-process Rich focus rows made the distinction concrete.
The misplaced version totaled `13968` client-rect reads and `132880` mutation records across seven
Rich word rows, with `rich-word-class-atomic-batch-jumps` alone at `3040` reads and `13760`
mutations. Adding `textRankSafe` only to search-hint reuse improved the focus set to `13088` reads
and `131920` mutations, with the class-atomic row at `2160` / `12800`. Moving the guard to its
intended final shape, search guarded and full-fit unguarded, produced `12768` reads and `130880`
mutations, with the class-atomic row back to `1840` / `11760`; the other Rich word rows stayed
structurally unchanged. This confirms the physical split: an unsafe atomic whitespace rank is a bad
place to start local search, but it is not by itself a reason to pay a separate preliminary
full-source fit read.

The same pass also tested two suspected missing input variables. First, a temporary direct-helper
diagnostic switched `overflow-wrap`, `word-break`, and related text layout rules after an initial
Line clamp. At the same width, stale hints and cold search both totaled `63` client-rect reads and
`66` text writes across eight word/grapheme cases; with a simultaneous width change, both totaled
`61` reads and `66` writes. This gives no current evidence for adding computed text-style identity
to Line warm hints, which would add a style read to the hot path. A follow-up `white-space`
diagnostic covered `normal`, `pre-wrap`, and `nowrap` transitions with hard line breaks, repeated
spaces, word and grapheme boundaries, and simultaneous width changes; stale hints and cold search
again tied at `39` client-rect reads and `38` text writes. Second, allowing Rich
beyond-window search to use first-jump density before any observed slope did not move the seven
Rich focus rows: totals stayed `12768` reads and `130880` mutations. That relaxation was not
retained because it added broader trust without measurable workload reduction.

The shared warm-search expansion limit itself was also re-tested after the line-count critique,
because the expansion window sounds like it might need to scale with visible lines. The measured
result did not support changing it. On the focused Line rows, a global expansion limit of `1`
raised totals to `29228` client-rect reads, `53007` mutation records, and `1304.9 ms`; CTA jitter
alone moved to `13317` reads, and long-token one-line/five-line jumps moved to `1040` / `1760`
reads. A global limit of `3` improved over `1` but still lost to the retained limit `2`, totaling
`26312` reads, `49340` mutations, and `1264.4 ms`, with CTA jitter at `11112` reads. Restoring the
retained limit `2` totaled `25920` reads, `49384` mutations, and `1173.1 ms`. A narrower dynamic
prototype that used `3` only for single-line word text kept reads exactly flat at `25920` and saved
only `480` mutation records (`49384 -> 48904`) by improving
`line-word-copy-lines1-batch-jumps` writes (`2960 -> 2480`), while the active-time sample worsened
to `1290.1 ms`. The conclusion is not that line count is irrelevant; line count already changes
the estimated rank movement and the warm-versus-cold decision. The local expansion limit describes
the search algorithm's locality proof. In the measured space, changing that algorithm budget did
not reduce layout reads, so the dynamic expansion-limit prototype was removed rather than retained
as unproven complexity.

Those new public guard rows are `rich-word-copy-affix-lines1-grow-full` and
