`rich-word-long-token-affix-lines5-grow-full`. On the same machine, fixed `32px` full-fit gating
produced `1232` client-rect reads and `85.9 ms` active time across the two rows. The retained
dynamic full-fit skip produced `1104` reads and `79.1 ms`, a `-128` read (`-10.4%`) and `-6.8 ms`
focused reduction, with mutation records unchanged at `11216`.

The package benchmark now emits a compact `PACKAGE_MATRIX_SUMMARY` alongside the full per-run
payload. This keeps full-matrix structural counters extractable from local smoke runs even when the
complete browser-console JSON is too large for a shell pipeline or terminal transcript. After
adding two high-line-count step-resize guard rows (`line-middle-log-lines5-batch-steps` and
`line-word-copy-lines5-batch-steps`), one max-height affix guard row
(`line-height-affix-card-batch-jumps`), one word-boundary fallback guard row
(`line-word-fallback-batch-continuous`), one word-boundary middle long-token guard row
(`line-word-long-token-middle-batch-jumps`), one word-boundary long-token affix guard row
(`line-word-long-token-affix-batch-jumps`), one Rich class-styled atomic guard row, and the two Rich
clamped-to-full guard rows, the final full smoke matrix has 75 supported scenarios. The latest
75-row current totals were `10565.3 ms` active time, `462136` bounding-rect reads, `94361`
client-rect reads, `603139` mutation records, `27991` scroll-width reads, and zero offset reads.
The two high-line-count step rows are
intentionally small guardrails (`1344` bounding-rect reads, `448` client-rect reads, `1344`
mutation records each), covering input space that was previously only represented in the temporary
helper matrix. The max-height affix row adds a component-level guard for height-only visible-line
capacity (`11088` bounding-rect reads, `6569` client-rect reads, and `12802` mutation records in
current smoke). The word-fallback row adds `3072` bounding-rect reads, `11230` client-rect reads,
and `15941` mutation records in current smoke. The word middle long-token row adds `1440`
bounding-rect reads, `2240` client-rect reads, and `3664` mutation records in current smoke. The
word long-token affix row adds `2400` bounding-rect reads, `2240` client-rect reads, and `3424`
mutation records in current smoke. The Rich class-styled atomic row adds `1440` bounding-rect
reads, `1840` client-rect reads, and `11760` mutation records in current smoke. The two new Rich
clamped-to-full rows add `960` bounding-rect reads, `1104` client-rect reads, and `11216` mutation
records in current smoke.

The compact summary later moved to schema v2 by adding `summary.extra` for median structural
counters outside the fixed counter set, plus target-level `extraTotals`. The fixed fields still
carry active time, layout reads, client-rect entries, mutation records, and scroll/offset reads.
`extra` now preserves counters such as slot calls, clone/image-clone calls, `replaceChildren`
calls, mutation callbacks, ResizeObserver callbacks, component instances, and future diagnostic
`*Calls` counters. A focused smoke over `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jumps`
(`/tmp/vue-clamp-compact-extra-smoke.log`) produced schema `2` with extra counters including
`afterSlotCalls: 288`, `beforeSlotCalls: 288`, `resizeObserverCallbacks: 288`,
`mutationCallbacks: 18`, and `componentInstances: 16`.

A follow-up smoke over `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jumps` and `line-cta-affix-batch-jumps`
(`/tmp/vue-clamp-compact-extra-totals-smoke.log`) verified `extraTotals`: `afterSlotCalls` summed to
`1056`, `beforeSlotCalls` to `288`, `resizeObserverCallbacks` to `672`, `mutationCallbacks` to
`54`, and `componentInstances` to `32`. This keeps local optimization loops from losing non-layout
structural signals when they parse the compact payload instead of the full raw benchmark JSON, and
lets them rank those signals without scanning each scenario by hand.

The final package build after the rank-cost, Rich guard, Rich dynamic full-fit skip,
max-height line-capacity model, and class-styled atomic guard was `101092` bytes for
`dist/index.js` (`21092` gzip) and
`7252` bytes for `dist/index.d.ts`
(`1663` gzip). This is a
larger runtime cost than the earlier dynamic-density prototype, so the retained justification is
the broader input-space workload reduction, exact estimator coverage, and the package long-token
and Rich word-jump counter reductions above.

A later correctness audit changed the optimization contract for skipped full-fit probes. The text
and rich searches can include the full source as the last candidate, but that candidate omits the
ellipsis, so it is not monotonic with the truncated candidates that precede it. The fix keeps
helper-level `includeFullCandidate` safe by verifying the full candidate when search did not probe
it naturally. Component paths then recover part of the cost with a physical proof: when the width
shrinks from a previously clamped state and the layout identity is unchanged, the full source still
cannot fit, so the extra verification is unnecessary. Same-width and grow paths still verify the
full candidate before returning a clamped result. Browser regressions now cover a LineClamp source
change from rewritten text to empty text and a Rich hinted-run case where `abc + ellipsis` overflows
while the bare full text `abci` fits.

That same audit fixed related measurement invalidation holes: LineClamp prop changes now replace
the `shallowRef` render snapshot instead of mutating it silently; multiline font-load events call
the recompute scheduler without passing the event object as a width; ResizeObserver-triggered
multiline widths now use the same `getBoundingClientRect()` unit as other recompute paths and only
write a pending root width after a real root-size change; InlineClamp no longer trusts `%` inline
widths for content-independent current-width measurement; native multiline measurement rejects a
zero-width content element even when an outer root-width snapshot exists; and max-height text/rich
fit checks no longer reuse one cached visible root top across changing candidates.
The same pass also restored the rich fallback invariant that unsupported rendered layouts are
detected before an unclamped result is accepted; a float child under `maxHeight` now falls back to
raw HTML instead of being silently clipped by the collapsed root styles.

The focused smoke after the correctness fix shows the expected trade-off. Compared with the earlier
unsafe baseline rows, `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter` moved from `10727` to `11879` client-rect reads
and from `17654` to `19214` mutation records, `line-word-copy-lines1-batch-jumps` moved from
`1680` to `1824` reads and `2960` to `3104` mutations, and
`line-word-long-token-lines5-batch-jumps` moved from `1280` to `1520` reads and `2544` to `2864`
mutations. Before the shrink-only proof was added, the same CTA row had reached `12967` reads and
`21038` mutations, so the proof recovered about half of the avoidable full-candidate checks while
keeping the non-shrink correctness guard. `rich-word-copy-affix-lines1-grow-full` measured `640`
client-rect reads and `3184` mutations in the same smoke. The package build after these fixes was
`101620` bytes for `dist/index.js` (`21250` gzip) and `7252` bytes for `dist/index.d.ts`
(`1663` gzip).

The next retained Rich change made the skipped-full-fit path actually avoid the full rich patch on
warm passes. `clampRich` now caches the searchable logical runs and word-rank points after the first
full-probe layout inspection for a prepared source. Later warm passes can start from the previous
hidden-probe state and patch directly to the first candidate; they still patch and measure the full
candidate whenever same-width/grow correctness requires it, and unsupported layout still falls back
because the cache is created only after a successful full layout inspection.

Focused Rich package smoke before that cache totaled `7472` client-rect reads and `76080` mutation
records across `rich-word-copy-batch-jumps`, `rich-word-copy-lines1-batch-jumps`,
`rich-word-copy-affix-lines1-grow-full`, `rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps`, and
`rich-word-long-token-affix-lines5-grow-full`. After the cache, the same focused set kept
client-rect reads at `7472` but reduced mutation records to `50832` (`-25248`, `-33.2%`). The
largest structural win was `rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps`, where mutation records moved
`45648 -> 22400`. Median active time in that row moved roughly `176.5 ms -> 135.6 ms` in nearby
smokes, but the normal-copy rows still had high RME, so the durable claim is the mutation-work
reduction rather than a precise timing percentage. The package build after the Rich cache measured
`102290` bytes for `dist/index.js` (`21469` gzip) and `7252` bytes for `dist/index.d.ts`
(`1663` gzip), so the cache adds `670` raw JS bytes and `219` gzip bytes over the preceding
correctness-fix build.

The hinted text-run coarse-search seed was revisited after the search-index cache changed the warm
path shape. The accepted version only moves the coarse-search hint after two facts are already
measured in the same pass: the hinted text run's end fits, and the following atomic run also fits.
The search helper still revalidates that hinted coarse index, so this does not skip a correctness
check; it only avoids restarting local expansion from the previous complete run.

A strict single-diff source benchmark comparison showed the retained shape is narrow but real:
`direct-rich-dense-jumps-warm` moved from `2177` to `2137` client-rect reads and from `120` to `80`
clone calls, while every other Rich source structural counter stayed unchanged. A focused package
smoke over `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous`, `rich-word-copy-batch-jumps`,
`rich-word-class-atomic-batch-jumps`, and `rich-dense-batch-jumps` moved totals from `11706` to
`11690` client-rect reads and from `50858` to `50794` mutation records. The package-level win came
from `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` (`5888 -> 5872` client-rect reads and `25824 -> 25760`
mutation records); the other three rows stayed structurally unchanged. Timing stayed secondary:
these focused smoke runs were used as counter proof, not as a precise active-time claim.

Rich fallback grapheme cuts now publish no word rank instead of rank zero; this fixes a
hint-pollution bug but did not change the focused package counters after the cache.

RichLineClamp's rank-slope state also now survives same-width recomputes. The bug was not in the
layout answer but in the hint state machine: after a resize observed a real rank-per-pixel slope, a
font-load invalidation at the same width refreshed the clamp and reset `rankObserved` to false even
though the stored slope was still the latest measured resize slope. The next beyond-window width
jump therefore fell back to the fixed window/cold path.

The package matrix now includes `rich-word-long-token-font-tick-jumps`, which dispatches a
`loadingdone` font event before each long-token width jump. This makes the input combination
explicit instead of relying on incidental browser font timing. In a focused smoke before preserving
the observed flag, the row measured `5232` client-rect reads, `56800` mutation records, and
`377.4 ms` median active time with `1.98%` active RME. Preserving the observed slope across the
same-width recompute moved the same row to `4160` client-rect reads, `39552` mutation records, and
`292.7 ms` median active time with `1.57%` active RME. Existing Rich smoke rows that do not include
a same-width font tick stayed structurally unchanged: `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` at
`5872` client-rect reads / `25760` mutation records, `rich-word-copy-batch-jumps` at `1968` /
`8160`, `rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps` at `2208` / `22400`, and `rich-dense-batch-jumps` at
`1770` / `5194`.

The matrix now has the matching Line input shape as `line-word-long-token-font-tick-jumps`.
LineClamp already preserved the previous text rank slope on same-width recomputes through
`previousRankSlope`, so this row did not justify a new algorithmic change; it closes the coverage
gap for the same font-invalidation-before-jump pattern that exposed the Rich state bug. A focused
current-only package smoke measured the new row at `2832` client-rect reads, `4272` mutation
records, and `136.7 ms` median active time with `3.76%` active RME. The adjacent risk rows in the
same run were `line-word-long-token-batch-jumps` at `1200` client-rect reads / `2640` mutation
records, `line-word-copy-batch-jumps` at `1584` / `3648`, and
`line-word-copy-lines1-batch-jumps` at `1824` / `3104`; their active-time RMEs were high enough
that the counters are the useful signal.

A subsequent Rich rank-index experiment was also rejected. Replacing the cached word `rankPoints`
array with a `Map` from structural point key to rank kept every source Rich DOM counter unchanged,
but the full source Rich benchmark moved total median time `226.0 ms -> 229.4 ms` in the same local
A/B. The array scan remains simpler and faster for the current input sizes.

LineClamp word-boundary fallback kept one structural win from the same pass. When the previous
result used grapheme fallback boundaries and the next width is narrower, `clampTextToLayout` now
starts directly in the fallback search instead of first re-running the primary word search that
cannot fit at a smaller width. Same-width and growing passes still try word boundaries first. In a
focused package smoke A/B for `line-word-fallback-batch-continuous`, the old path measured `11230`
client-rect reads, `15941` mutation records, and `381.4 ms` active time. The retained fallback
warm-start measured `10206` client-rect reads, `14917` mutation records, and `357.9 ms`, with low
RME in both runs. The package build after this pass measured `102734` bytes for `dist/index.js`
(`21519` gzip) and `7252` bytes for `dist/index.d.ts` (`1663` gzip).

The package matrix now also includes CJK word-boundary guard rows so the warm-search evidence is
not limited to English copy and long ASCII tokens. `line-word-cjk-batch-jitter` uses
`boundary="word"` with non-ASCII text and a non-repeating jitter width list; the focused current
smoke recorded `992` client-rect reads and `2256` mutation records. `rich-word-cjk-batch-jitter`
does the same for trusted inline rich HTML and recorded `1152` client-rect reads and `3680`
mutation records. The active-time RME was high enough that these rows should be read as structural
coverage, not as timing proof.

The word-boundary public matrix also gained ordinary English novel-width jitter rows, because the
older word-copy rows used repeated jump rings and could not prove behavior for resize paths that
mostly visit new widths. Current smoke for `line-word-copy-batch-jitter` recorded `8512`
bounding-rect reads, `6864` client-rect reads, and `12880` mutation records; current smoke for
`rich-word-copy-batch-jitter` recorded `7680` bounding-rect reads, `6112` client-rect reads, and
`25072` mutation records. A `current,current` filtered smoke kept those structural counters
identical across both targets, while same-version timing still drifted: Line active medians were
`417.0 ms` vs `405.8 ms`, and Rich medians were `435.9 ms` vs `429.0 ms`, with one Rich sample set
showing `56.5%` active RME. These rows therefore strengthen input-space coverage and counter-based
proof, but their smoke timing must not be used for small-percentage claims.

A RichLineClamp root-ellipsis reuse experiment was rejected. The idea was to keep the existing
root-level ellipsis during clamped-to-clamped structural patches and make the final append
idempotent, avoiding a remove-and-append pair when the patch anchor stayed inside the source tree.
Focused package smoke over `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous`,
`rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`, and `rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous` showed identical
structural counters before and after: `19968` client-rect reads and `83904` mutation records across
the three rows. The prototype only increased built JS size (`102.73 kB -> 102.86 kB` in that run),
so it was removed.

The remaining generic ResizeObserver signature path was tightened for transformed and logical-axis
layouts. InlineClamp and WrapClamp still use `ResizeObserverEntry.borderBoxSize` for ordinary
horizontal, untransformed elements so normal rows avoid extra layout reads. When an observed element
has a transformed ancestor or vertical/sideways writing mode, the entry's layout-pixel
inline/block size is not comparable to the stored `getBoundingClientRect()` visual signature, so the
helper now falls back to a visual signature only for that element. A browser helper test proves the
fixed case: a `transform:scale(0.5)` element's initial observer entry no longer reports a change
against the current visual signature, while a real width change still reports one. Focused package
smoke over `inline-path-end-batch-continuous`, `inline-path-middle-batch-jitter`, and
`wrap-table-demo-width-sweep` kept ordinary-path structural counters unchanged at `9120`, `9600`,
and `19000` bounding-rect reads respectively. The package build after this fix measured
`103.58 kB` for `dist/index.js` (`21.73 kB` gzip).

The shared `fitsContent` helper no longer exposes the unused `cachedVisibleTop` parameter. No
current caller passed it, and caching one visible root top across candidate checks is unsafe in
layouts where candidate height changes move the root, such as a max-height clamp centered inside a
fixed-height flex parent. The current helper intentionally reads the root's visible bounds for the
candidate being tested. A browser regression test covers that self-moving root shape and asserts
LineClamp still returns real clamped text, not an over-clamped ellipsis-only result, while staying
within the two visible-line `maxHeight` limit. Validation after the cleanup passed
`vp test -c vite.browser.config.ts packages/vue-clamp/tests/clamp.browser.test.ts`, full
`vp run test:browser`, `vp test`, and `vp check`. Focused max-height package smoke recorded the
current structural baseline: `line-height-card-batch-jumps` at `3627` bounding-rect reads /
`2187` client-rect reads / `3825` mutation records, `line-height-affix-card-batch-jumps` at
`17449` / `7065` / `13394`, and `rich-height-card-batch-jumps` at `3435` / `2283` / `11628`.
The package build measured `103.55 kB` for `dist/index.js` (`21.72 kB` gzip), a small size cleanup
from removing the unused parameter path.

The visual-signature fallback then received one dynamic-style correction. The first version cached
both positive and negative `needsVisualBorderBoxSignature` decisions in a `WeakMap`. A negative
cache entry is unsafe: an element can first compare ordinary untransformed `ResizeObserver` entries,
then later acquire a transformed ancestor or vertical/sideways writing mode. In that state, the
old negative cache would keep treating layout-pixel RO entries as comparable to stored visual
`getBoundingClientRect()` signatures, causing repeated false-positive reclamps after the next real
size change. The helper now uses a `WeakSet` and caches only positive fallback decisions. A browser
helper test forces an untransformed mismatch first, then applies `transform:scale(0.5)` and proves
the same layout-size entry is compared against the current visual border box instead of the stale
negative result. Focused normal-path package smoke kept ordinary counters unchanged:
`inline-path-end-batch-continuous` stayed at `9120` bounding-rect reads / `11328` mutation records /
`5424` scroll-width reads, `inline-path-middle-batch-jitter` stayed at `9600` / `12153` / `5922`,
and `wrap-table-demo-width-sweep` stayed at `19000` bounding-rect reads / `5200` mutation records
with `15300` item slot calls. The package build after this correction measured `103.51 kB` for
`dist/index.js` (`21.71 kB` gzip).

The same ordinary-entry / visual-fallback split is now used by the shared Line/Rich multiline
shell. The shell had kept the correctness fix by reading `getBoundingClientRect()` for every
ResizeObserver entry, including ordinary untransformed entries whose `borderBoxSize` was already
comparable. That made the current Line/Rich continuous and jitter hotspots pay one extra bounding
rect read per observed entry. The retained helper returns the entry snapshot for ordinary layout and
only reads a visual snapshot when the target has a transformed ancestor or vertical/sideways writing
mode; transformed behavior is covered by browser helper tests for both unchanged and changed visual
sizes.

A focused package smoke before the shell fast path measured the affected current rows at:
`line-cta-affix-batch-continuous` `11360` bounding-rect reads, `6576` client-rect reads, `12946`
mutation records, `465.2 ms` median active with `14.6%` RME; `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter`
`11200` / `11879` / `19214`, `542.5 ms` with `18.5%` RME;
`line-height-affix-card-batch-jumps` `17449` / `7065` / `13394`, `278.7 ms` with `13.4%` RME;
`rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` `14080` / `5872` / `25760`, `449.9 ms` with `8.5%` RME;
and `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter` `14848` / `8432` / `32624`, `493.3 ms` with `1.9%` RME.
After the fast path, the same focused rows measured `9120`, `8960`, `16313`, `12320`, and `12992`
bounding-rect reads respectively. Client-rect and mutation counts stayed unchanged. Active medians
were `419.0 ms`, `544.3 ms`, `293.0 ms`, `413.0 ms`, and `469.5 ms`; this timing movement is
secondary because the Line rows still have double-digit RME, while the structural bounding-rect
reduction is exact for the affected rows.

The Rich affix signature path then kept one more targeted shell reduction. On a root-size change,
RichLineClamp pre-reads before/after signatures so the hidden probe can validate cloned affix boxes
before measuring. The settled layout signature used to read the same affix boxes again immediately
after recompute. That second read is needed if `clamped` changed, because before/after slots receive
`clamped` in their slot props and may rerender to a different size. If `clamped` is unchanged, the
pre-read signatures are still the committed affix layout and can be reused for the settled
signature.

Focused package smoke after this reuse measured `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` at `8800`
bounding-rect reads, `5872` client-rect reads, and `25760` mutation records; the previous retained
shell shape was `12320` / `5872` / `25760`. `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter` moved from `12992` /
`8432` / `32624` to `9280` / `8432` / `32624`. The clamped/full risk rows also stayed structurally
safe while reducing only redundant bbox reads: `rich-word-copy-affix-lines1-grow-full` moved from
`576` to `384` bounding-rect reads with `640` client-rect reads and `3024` mutation records
unchanged, and `rich-word-long-token-affix-lines5-grow-full` moved from `576` to `384` bbox reads
with `736` client-rect reads and `9088` mutation records unchanged.

A later review-driven proof pass added two browser regressions for correctness invariants that are
easy to break while optimizing skipped full-fit paths. Native multiline LineClamp now has a zero
content-width guard test: the root still has a positive border-box width, but the native content
cell is forced to `clientWidth === 0`, and the component must keep the source text unclamped rather
than treating root width as proof that native line-clamp measurement is valid. RichLineClamp also
has a direct hidden-probe test for `white-space: break-spaces` trailing whitespace: the full rich
text spans more than one visual line, while the clamped candidate with trimmed trailing whitespace
and an ellipsis fits; `clampRich` must return a clamped state after measuring the bare full
candidate, not infer full fit from the hinted text-run end. Focused browser validation passed with
`vp run test:browser -- packages/vue-clamp/tests/clamp.browser.test.ts` (`7` browser files,
`131` tests).

The hinted text-run coarse-search seed was re-tested in the current search-index shape. A temporary
variant set `coarseHint = hintedRunIndex + 1` whenever the hinted text run end fit and any following
run existed, not only when the following atomic run had already been measured as fitting. The
candidate is correct because `findLastFittingIndex` revalidates hints, but it did not reduce
deterministic work in the focused Rich word package rows. Before the variant, smoke totals over
`rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`, `rich-word-copy-batch-jumps`, `rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps`,
`rich-word-long-token-lines5-batch-jumps`, and `rich-word-long-token-font-tick-jumps` were `12576`
bounding-rect reads, `16976` client-rect reads, and `115056` mutation records. After the variant the
same totals were exactly `12576`, `16976`, and `115056`; per-row client-rect and mutation counters
were unchanged. Only timing moved within normal smoke noise (`1148.9 ms` total active before,
`1124.9 ms` after), so the variant was rejected and removed.

LineClamp first kept a smaller same-rank full-candidate skip. The earlier correctness audit proved
that truncated candidates and the bare full-source candidate are not monotonic because the full
source omits the ellipsis. Therefore same-width warm passes still verify the full source; browser
coverage now includes a direct helper case where `abcWWWW` overflows but `abci` fits at the same
root width. The safe skip is narrower: when a growing width remains inside an already observed
same-rank width interval whose wider endpoint also produced a clamped result, the final bare
full-source verification is redundant. A wider clamped measurement has already proved that the
source did not fit under the same text, ellipsis, ratio, spacing, line limit, max-height, and affix
layout key.

A focused package smoke comparison over `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous`,
`line-cta-affix-batch-jitter`, `line-word-fallback-batch-continuous`,
`line-word-copy-batch-jitter`, and `line-word-long-token-font-tick-jumps` showed a small exact
workload reduction: client-rect reads moved from `38357` to `37893`, and mutation records from
`64229` to `63765`; bounding-rect reads stayed `30816`. The affected rows were the jitter and
font-tick rows: `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter` saved `32` client-rect reads and `32` mutation
records, `line-word-copy-batch-jitter` saved `192` / `192`, and
`line-word-long-token-font-tick-jumps` saved `240` / `240`. A broader Line-only smoke run stayed
structurally consistent with the focused result: all Line rows totaled `80468` bounding-rect reads,
`67577` client-rect reads, and `127981` mutation records, with no counter increase in any retained
row. Timing is not used as primary evidence here because the focused rows still include high-RME
jitter cases. The package size cost in the nearby current build was about `+0.33 kB` raw and
`+0.07 kB` gzip (`dist/index.js` `104.59 kB` to `104.92 kB`, gzip `21.88 kB` to `21.95 kB`).

LineClamp then replaced the same-rank-only final-full verification skip with the same wider proof
used by RichLineClamp: each clamped text result records the widest same-context width that the
browser has already proved still cannot fit the bare full source. Later growing passes can skip the
final bare-full verification when the new width is no wider than that observed clamped maximum.
Widths that returned full text do not seed this cache, and same-width passes still verify because a
font or layout metric invalidation can change fit at an unchanged root width.

A fresh focused package smoke comparison over `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous`,
`line-cta-affix-batch-jitter`, `line-word-fallback-batch-continuous`,
`line-word-copy-batch-jitter`, `line-word-long-token-font-tick-jumps`,
`line-word-long-token-batch-jumps`, `line-word-copy-lines1-batch-jumps`, and
`line-word-copy-lines5-batch-jumps` moved total client-rect reads from `40965` to `38773`
(`-2192`, `-5.35%`) and mutation records from `70133` to `67350` (`-2783`, `-3.97%`);
bounding-rect reads stayed `33984`. The rows that moved were the affix and jitter rows:
`line-cta-affix-batch-continuous` (`6576 -> 5856` client rects, `12946 -> 12139` mutations),
`line-cta-affix-batch-jitter` (`11847 -> 10759`, `19182 -> 17702`), and
`line-word-copy-batch-jitter` (`6672 -> 6288`, `12688 -> 12192`). The long-token and fallback rows
were structurally unchanged. A full Line smoke run after the broader proof totaled `80324`
bounding-rect reads, `64841` client-rect reads, and `124398` mutation records, compared with the
prior same-rank-only full Line smoke at `80468`, `67577`, and `127981`. The current build after the
Line proof measured `106.01 kB` raw and `22.16 kB` gzip, about `+0.33 kB` raw and `+0.05 kB` gzip
over the preceding Rich clamped-width build (`105.68 kB` / `22.11 kB`). Timing moved in the same
direction in the focused aggregate (`2113.6 ms -> 2041.4 ms` active), but several row RMEs are high,
so the retained claim remains the exact DOM-work reduction.

A follow-up simplification tested whether the old same-rank warm-search interval still had
independent value now that final-full verification uses the broader clamped-width proof. Disabling
that same-rank search branch kept the focused Line structural totals exactly unchanged at `33984`
bounding-rect reads, `38773` client-rect reads, and `67350` mutation records. After fully removing
the fields, helper, and test fixture data, the full Line smoke still totaled `80324`
bounding-rect reads, `64841` client-rect reads, and `124398` mutation records, while the package
build dropped from `106.01 kB` / `22.16 kB` gzip to `104.13 kB` / `21.91 kB` gzip. Line warm-search
reuse now relies on observed rank-per-pixel slope when available and visible-rank density as the
fallback estimate; the separate clamped-width proof owns final full-source verification skipping.

RichLineClamp also replaced its narrow same-rank proof with a simpler clamped-width proof. The
component records the widest width in the current source / constraint / affix-signature context
where the full rich tree was known not to fit. A later growing pass can skip the final bare-full
verification whenever the new width is no wider than that observed clamped maximum. This proof does
not depend on word rank, so it covers default grapheme rich rows as well as word-boundary rows.
Same-width passes still verify the full tree, and affix signature changes reset the observed
clamped maximum and rank slope so old slot geometry cannot justify new-layout skips.

The full Rich smoke before this broader proof totaled `55424` client-rect reads, `302690` mutation
records, and `49019` bounding-rect reads. After the proof, the same Rich smoke totaled `50336`
client-rect reads, `231794` mutation records, and the same `49019` bounding-rect reads. The largest
row-level reductions were `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` (`5872 -> 4992` client rects,
`25760 -> 17232` mutations), `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter` (`8432 -> 7616`,
`32624 -> 23808`), `rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous` (`5632 -> 4752`, `25392 -> 18016`),
`rich-word-copy-batch-jitter` (`6112 -> 5200`, `25072 -> 21824`), and
`rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps` (`2208 -> 1968`, `22400 -> 10640`). A focused repeat of the
largest affected rows kept the same structural counts. The current build after the broader proof
measured about `105.68 kB` raw and `22.11 kB` gzip in the affix-guarded build, with a prior
same-rank-only build at `105.51 kB` / `22.07 kB`; timing moved favorably in several low-RME rows,
but the retained claim is the deterministic DOM-work reduction.

InlineClamp then moved from its old fixed `24px` full-body skip window to the shared text rank-cost
policy plus the same clamped-width proof used by multiline text. The inline path supplies a
single-line text context with preserved outer body spacing, so the text helper can decide whether a
warm search is cheaper than a cold full-body read without hard-coding a pixel delta in the
component. A same-machine inline package smoke before this change totaled `30215` scroll-width
reads, `54387` mutation records, `36480` bounding-rect reads, and `1665.7 ms` active time, with the
nearby package build at `104.13 kB` / `21.91 kB` gzip. After the change the same inline smoke
totaled `27383` scroll-width reads (`-2832`, `-9.37%`), `51382` mutation records (`-3005`,
`-5.52%`), unchanged `36480` bounding-rect reads, and `1488.9 ms` active time, with the nearby build
at `104.93 kB` / `21.98 kB` gzip. The rows that moved were the path and split/file-path warm rows:
`inline-path-end-batch-continuous` saved `912` scroll-width reads and `912` mutation records,
`inline-path-middle-batch-continuous` saved `912` / `912`,
`inline-path-middle-batch-jitter` saved `912` / `989`,
`inline-split-file-path-batch-jumps` saved `48` / `96`, and
`inline-word-copy-batch-jumps` saved `48` / `96`. Timing moved in the same direction, but the
retained evidence is the exact read/write reduction.

The RichLineClamp dynamic-threshold question was re-opened after the clamped-width proof and search
index cache. The current fixed/gated Rich baseline for that round was `49019` bounding-rect reads,
`50336` client-rect reads, `231794` mutation records, and a nearby build of `104.93 kB` /
`21.98 kB` gzip. A strict run-hint cost model that compared estimated warm probes against cold
probes increased the same smoke to `65737` client-rect reads and `308373` mutations, with a
`106.86 kB` / `22.47 kB` build. A risk-budget version still totaled `59679` client-rect reads and
`236621` mutations at `107.35 kB` / `22.58 kB`. A comparable-width/local-coverage version improved
mutations but still regressed client-rect reads to `51759` and grew to `107.56 kB` /
`22.61 kB`. An observed-slope span guard totaled `59998` client-rect reads and `276514` mutations
at `107.92 kB` / `22.68 kB`. A smaller all-boundary rank-only variant still regressed to `50787`
client-rect reads and `231859` mutations, with a `105.32 kB` / `22.25 kB` build. None proved a net
workload reduction, and the size cost was material compared with the exact counter gains already
available from the retained search-index and clamped-width work.

A final local Rich seed experiment was also removed. Starting the coarse search after a hinted text
run whenever any following run existed is correct because the search helper revalidates hints, but
it produced the same Rich smoke totals as the baseline: `49019` bounding-rect reads, `50336`
client-rect reads, and `231794` mutation records, with a nearby `105.04 kB` / `21.99 kB` build.
The current Rich policy therefore does not claim that the fixed `32px` window is globally optimal.
It says only that the tested dynamic signals, including coarse run rank and all-boundary rank,
failed to prove lower total browser work in the expanded matrix. The retained Rich optimizations are
the correctness-preserving clamped-width full-candidate proof, cached layout/search index reuse, and
the narrower word-boundary dynamic guards that already had direct counter evidence.

The next exact LineClamp hotspot was `line-word-fallback-batch-continuous`, whose current smoke row
still spent `10206` client-rect reads and `14917` mutation records re-proving that no word-boundary
candidate fit before falling back to grapheme cuts. The retained optimization records, only on a
word-boundary result that actually used fallback grapheme offsets, the widest same-context width
where the browser has proved the primary word search failed. Later grows can skip the primary word
search while they remain inside that proved width; same-width recomputes intentionally do not carry
the wider proof so font or layout metric changes can re-test word candidates.

Against the same-machine Line smoke captured immediately before the change, the full Line group
moved from `64841` to `63817` client-rect reads (`-1024`) and from `124398` to `123374` mutation
records (`-1024`), with every other Line row structurally unchanged. The affected row was exactly
`line-word-fallback-batch-continuous`: client-rect reads moved `10206 -> 9182`, mutation records
`14917 -> 13893`, and bounding-rect reads stayed `3072`. The row's active time moved
`356.1 ms -> 325.3 ms` in the Line-group smoke, but the retained claim is again the exact
read/write reduction. A focused repeat of just that row measured the same structural counters
(`9182` client rects, `13893` mutations) and `338.5 ms` active time with `1.7%` RME. The package
build after this proof measured `105.74 kB` raw and `22.10 kB` gzip, about `+0.74 kB` raw and
`+0.11 kB` gzip over the immediately preceding `105.00 kB` / `21.99 kB` build.

The next visible Line hotspot, `line-height-affix-card-batch-jumps`, was inspected but did not yet
produce a retained optimization. A line-capacity early-rejection prototype used the already
estimated pixel `maxHeight / line-height` capacity as a fit predicate line limit, but the focused
row kept the exact same structural counters: `16169` bounding-rect reads, `6921` client-rect reads,
`6921` client-height reads, `6921` client-top reads, and `13154` mutation records. A second
maxHeight-only prototype replaced `getClientRects()` with the content union
`getBoundingClientRect()` when no explicit line limit was active. It removed the `6921`
client-rect reads but added the same number of bounding-rect reads (`16169 -> 23090`), kept
client-height/client-top/mutations unchanged, and did not improve the focused active time against
the previous no-counter-change run (`285.3 ms` before, `289.0 ms` after). Both prototypes were
removed: the first had no workload effect, and the second only changed the kind of synchronous
layout read without proving lower browser work.

The multiline shell's affix-signature reuse option was also tested on LineClamp after it had helped
RichLineClamp avoid hidden-probe clone reads. Enabling `syncAffixSignaturesOnRootChange` for
LineClamp did not reduce the focused affix rows. Across `line-title-single-affix-batch-sweep`,
`line-cta-affix-batch-continuous`, `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter`, `line-cta-affix-batch-jumps`,
`line-word-long-token-affix-batch-jumps`, and `line-height-affix-card-batch-jumps`, bounding-rect
reads increased from `41001` to `42825` (`+1824`) while client-rect reads, client-height reads,
client-top reads, and mutations were unchanged. Some active times moved down, but without structural
support and with mixed RME, so the option was removed for LineClamp. The result confirms that the
Rich reuse path is tied to hidden-probe clone validation; Line's visible affix layout key does not
benefit from the same root-change pre-read.

InlineClamp then removed a duplicate root-width read from Vue-driven style updates. The component
already reads parent/root border-box signatures in `onUpdated` to decide whether it must reclamp.
For content-independent root widths, that same subpixel root width is a valid clamp limit, so the
recompute pass can reuse it instead of calling `getBoundingClientRect()` again. Content-sized and
percentage-width layouts keep the old behavior: they restore the full body first and measure after
that restore, so the earlier shrink-to-fit correctness invariant remains intact.

Against the same-machine Inline smoke before this change, all Inline rows moved from `36480` to
`29184` bounding-rect reads (`-7296`, `-20.0%`) while scroll-width reads stayed `27383` and mutation
records stayed `51382`. The largest row deltas were `inline-path-middle-batch-jitter`
(`9600 -> 7680` bounding rects), `inline-path-end-batch-continuous` (`9120 -> 7296`), and
`inline-path-middle-batch-continuous` (`9120 -> 7296`). Active time moved in the same direction for
the focused smoke (`1784.3 ms -> 1490.6 ms` total), but the retained proof is the exact duplicate
root-read reduction. The package build after the change measured `106.31 kB` raw and `22.20 kB`
gzip, about `+0.57 kB` raw and `+0.10 kB` gzip over the preceding `105.74 kB` / `22.10 kB` build.

A fresh single-diff repeat was then run by temporarily removing only that Inline root-width snapshot
reuse and immediately restoring it. The before log
`/tmp/vue-clamp-inline-width-snapshot-fresh-before.log` kept the dynamic text policy and percentage
width safety guards, but always reread `getBoundingClientRect()` inside `clampBody`. The after log
`/tmp/vue-clamp-inline-width-snapshot-fresh-after.log` restored the snapshot reuse. The total Inline
smoke counters repeated the same structural result: bounding-rect reads moved `36480 -> 29184`
(`-7296`, `-20.0%`), while scroll-width reads stayed `27383` and mutation records stayed `51382`.
Every Inline row saved one root rect read per component step: the continuous rows saved `-1824` or
`-1920` bounding-rect reads, and each jump row saved `-288`. Median active time moved
`1508.1 ms -> 1488.2 ms` (`-1.3%`), but several row RMEs were high, so timing remains supporting
only. A browser regression now covers the correctness side of the same optimization boundary:
`InlineClamp` with inline `width:100%` inside a shrink-to-fit parent reclamps after a font-load
event and restores the full body when the outer width grows, proving percentage widths still take
the full-body measurement path.

The package matrix then gained one missing RichLineClamp coverage row:
`rich-height-affix-card-batch-jumps`. Line already had a maxHeight + before/after affix card row,
but Rich only had maxHeight without affixes, leaving the combination of hidden-probe affix clones,
affix signatures, rich layout inspection, and maxHeight visible-bounds fitting uncovered. A current
focused smoke for the new row measured `3504` bounding-rect reads, `2064` client-rect reads, `2064`
client-height reads, `2064` client-top reads, and `10128` mutation records. The total layout-read
shape (`9696`) is close to `rich-height-card-batch-jumps` (`9996`) and
`line-height-card-batch-jumps` (`9900`), and far below the existing Line maxHeight-affix hotspot
(`36932`). The row therefore extends matrix coverage without changing the current optimization
target: Rich maxHeight affixes do not currently show the same structural amplification as Line's
height-affix card row. Its smoke timing had high RME, so no timing claim is retained.

One more maxHeight candidate-order experiment was rejected after that coverage pass. The temporary
variant used the already inferred `lineCapacity` as the `fitsContent` line limit for maxHeight-only
LineClamp searches and checked line count before reading the root visible bounds. This is correct
for the covered pixel-line-height cases, but it did not reduce deterministic work. A focused A/B
over `line-height-card-batch-jumps`, `line-height-affix-card-batch-jumps`,
`rich-height-card-batch-jumps`, and `rich-height-affix-card-batch-jumps` kept every structural
counter unchanged: the Line height-affix row stayed at `16169` bounding-rect reads, `6921`
client-rect reads, `6921` client-height reads, `6921` client-top reads, and `13154` mutation
records; the other three rows were also identical. The variant was removed because it added another
fit-path branch without proving any workload reduction.

The package matrix then gained Line/Rich word-boundary + maxHeight coverage. Earlier rows covered
word-boundary behavior and height-constrained behavior separately, but not their combination, which
matters for the dynamic-threshold question because displayed line capacity changes the amount of
rank movement a width change can usefully search. A current focused smoke for the new
`line-word-height-card-batch-jumps` row measured `2832` bounding-rect reads, `1968`
client-rect reads, `1968` client-height reads, `1968` client-top reads, and `3104` mutation
records. The new `rich-word-height-card-batch-jumps` row measured `2688` bounding-rect reads,
`1824` client-rect reads, `1824` client-height reads, `1824` client-top reads, and `7728`
mutation records. The structural counters are stable and give the matrix direct coverage for
ordinary word-boundary text under browser height fitting. The smoke timings are not retained as
evidence because the Rich row's active-time RME was `25.3%`.

The Line text warm-search expansion budget was then tested from the input-space side instead of
being treated as a fixed magic value. Disabling cross-width text hints was rejected first: on the
same focused Line rows it increased `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter` by `+7411` layout reads and
`+11154` mutation records, `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous` by `+7004` / `+8908`, and
`line-word-copy-batch-jitter` by `+4640` / `+6400`. That proves the current warm hint path is
removing substantial cold-search work.

Raising the global local expansion limit from `2` to `3` found the useful shape but was not retained
globally. It reduced word rows, especially `line-word-fallback-batch-continuous`
(`-2686` layout reads, `-2805` mutation records), but it also regressed non-word rows such as
`line-cta-affix-batch-jitter` (`+385` / `+422`) and `line-height-affix-card-batch-jumps`
(`+28` / `+14`). The retained version therefore keeps the default expansion limit at `2` and uses
`3` only for LineClamp layout searches whose original boundary is `word`, including their grapheme
fallback search. A full Line smoke compared against the immediately preceding same-machine baseline
showed total Line structural counters move by `-3982` layout reads and `-4389` mutation records.
Only word rows changed: `line-word-fallback-batch-continuous` saved `2686` client-rect reads and
`2805` mutation records, `line-word-copy-batch-jitter` saved `608` / `656`,
`line-word-long-token-middle-batch-jumps` saved `320` / `480`,
`line-word-long-token-affix-batch-jumps` saved `320` / `400`, and
`line-word-cjk-batch-jitter` saved `48` / `48`. No non-word row had structural counter changes in
the targeted variant. The package build after retaining this change measured `106.50 kB` raw and
`22.23 kB` gzip, about `+0.19 kB` raw and `+0.03 kB` gzip over the preceding
`106.31 kB` / `22.20 kB` build.

A similar RichLineClamp expansion experiment was rejected. Raising both Rich warm-search constants
from `3` to `4` reduced mutation records but increased full Rich smoke layout reads by `+1632`,
mostly from word-boundary jump and word+height rows. A narrower non-word-only variant avoided that
regression and saved `256` layout reads plus `960` mutation records across the full Rich group, but
the gain was tiny, affected only three current rows, and added another fixed threshold split without
a stronger input-space explanation. It was removed rather than retained as a likely overfit
micro-optimization.

The font-invalidation coverage was strengthened after that. The older font-tick rows dispatch a
`loadingdone` event before each large width jump, which validates that font events reclamp and that
same-width invalidations preserve rank-slope information, but those rows do not actually change
font metrics. Two new rows now toggle a CSS `--bench-font-size` between `18px` and `16px` before the
same large width jumps and dispatch the font event, so the browser really changes text metrics
before the resize. Current focused smoke baselines are
`line-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` at `7264` layout reads, `4178` mutation records,
`162.9 ms` active time, `2.3%` RME, and `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` at `9648`
layout reads, `53058` mutation records, `437.9 ms` active time, `2.3%` RME.

Those rows also tested whether same-width font invalidations should clear rank-slope hints. The
temporary variant had no structural effect on Line font rows, but it made Rich much worse: the
synthetic `rich-word-long-token-font-tick-jumps` row regressed by `+1312` layout reads and
`+24688` mutation records, while the real-metric
`rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` row regressed by `+464` layout reads and `+16672`
mutation records. The existing Rich behavior, preserving an already observed slope across same-width
font invalidations, is therefore retained with evidence from both synthetic and real font-metric
coverage.

A Rich word-rank index micro-optimization was also tested and removed. The idea was to replace
`rankForState`'s linear search through word rank points with a `WeakMap` built beside the cached
search index. Because this changes no DOM work, it was evaluated with focused report-mode timing
instead of structural counters. The before run had low RME on the target rows:
`rich-word-copy-batch-jitter` `440.2 ms` median / `3.0%` RME,
`rich-word-long-token-font-tick-jumps` `255.3 ms` / `0.8%`,
`rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` `429.1 ms` / `3.9%`, and
`rich-word-long-token-lines5-batch-jumps` `151.8 ms` / `0.9%`. The indexed variant left all
layout and mutation counters unchanged, improved the ordinary word jitter row, but regressed the
low-RME long-token rows: font tick moved `255.3 -> 260.9 ms` median and lines5 moved
`151.8 -> 156.5 ms`. Since the workload proof was mixed and the change added another data
structure, it was rejected as an unstable JS-only micro-optimization.

The next retained maxHeight optimization reintroduced bounds reuse with a stricter invalidation
rule. The earlier removed `cachedVisibleTop` parameter was unsafe because a candidate can change the
root height and move a centered or anchored root. The retained version caches visible top/bottom
only within one clamp pass and only while `root.clientHeight` stays unchanged; every height change
forces a fresh visible-root read. Focused same-machine smoke over all current Line/Rich height rows
showed exact structural savings with no mutation changes:
`line-height-card-batch-jumps` `9900 -> 8118` layout reads,
`line-word-height-card-batch-jumps` `8736 -> 7392`,
`line-height-affix-card-batch-jumps` `36932 -> 31904`,
`rich-height-card-batch-jumps` `9996 -> 8502`,
`rich-word-height-card-batch-jumps` `8160 -> 6720`, and
`rich-height-affix-card-batch-jumps` `9696 -> 8352`. Across those six rows, total layout reads
moved by `-12432`; the savings were exactly `-6216` bounding-rect reads and `-6216` client-top
reads, while client-rect reads, client-height reads, and mutation records stayed unchanged. The
existing browser regression for a maxHeight clamp centered in a fixed-height flex parent still
passed with this cache, confirming that height-changing candidates do not reuse stale root bounds.
The package build after retaining this change measured `107.16 kB` raw and `22.40 kB` gzip, about
`+0.66 kB` raw and `+0.17 kB` gzip over the preceding `106.50 kB` / `22.23 kB` build.

A follow-up maxHeight fit-order experiment was rejected. Moving the line-count check ahead of the
visible-bounds check inside `fitsContent` looked like it could avoid root visible-bound reads when a
candidate already exceeded `maxLines`, but the focused height-row smoke proved no workload change.
Against the retained bounds-cache baseline, all six Line/Rich height rows kept identical counters:
total bounding-rect reads stayed `25463`, client-rect reads stayed `17247`, client-top reads stayed
`11031`, and mutation records stayed `49567`. The temporary branch was removed because the only
movement was noisy high-RME timing with no DOM-work reduction.

The suggested Rich hinted-run coarse-start variant was also tested and removed. The proposed shape
assumed that once a hinted text run's last cut fits, the next logical run may be another text run and
coarse search could start there. In the current implementation adjacent searchable text across
inline wrappers is deliberately merged into one logical text run; text runs are split only by
atomic inline units or breaks. A temporary hit log over `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter` produced no
`fineIndex === runEndIndex` hits, and a broader before/after smoke over eleven Rich word rows kept
all structural counters identical: `21408` bounding-rect reads, `29712` client-rect reads, and
`175074` mutation records before and after. The existing atomic-following-run start remains the
only retained form because it matches the logical-run invariant and already has benchmark support.

Rich structural patching then gained one retained grow-only fast path. When the previous clamped
point is exactly at the end of a source text node, and climbing through ancestors proves that the
visible prefix already contains complete source subtrees, a later clamped point can be reached by
removing the root ellipsis and appending only the missing source fragment. This preserves the live
prefix nodes and avoids deleting/recloning stable rich wrappers while keeping the generic patcher
for partial text cuts, shrinks, and unsupported shapes. A browser regression asserts that growing
from `<span>alpha</span>…` to `<span>alpha</span> <span>beta</span>…` preserves the original first
`span` node identity.

Fresh same-process RichLineClamp smoke with the fast path disabled/enabled showed deterministic DOM
work reduction across the full Rich group. Total mutation records moved `302708 -> 294561`
(`-8147`), bounding-rect reads moved `56144 -> 56117`, and client-rect reads moved
`60800 -> 60580`. The main mutation savings were `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`
`53058 -> 50722`, `rich-word-long-token-font-tick-jumps` `32112 -> 31184`,
`rich-word-long-token-lines5-batch-jumps` `12432 -> 11504`, `rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps`
`10640 -> 9920`, `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` `17232 -> 16720`, and
`rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous` `18016 -> 17456`. A simplified follow-up kept the same
structural deltas and moved aggregate active time by only `-3.5 ms`, but timing remains secondary
because several affected rows still have high RME; the proof is the reduced DOM mutation workload.
The package build after simplification measured `109.04 kB` raw and `22.90 kB` gzip, about
`+1.88 kB` raw and `+0.50 kB` gzip over the prior `107.16 kB` / `22.40 kB` build.

A later text-write micro-optimization was tested and removed. The variant updated a single existing
text child via `Text.data` instead of assigning `element.textContent` during Line/Inline search
candidate probes. Focused Line rows with high mutation volume showed no structural change:
`line-cta-affix-batch-continuous` stayed `5856` client-rect reads / `12139` mutation records,
`line-cta-affix-batch-jitter` stayed `10759` / `17702`, `line-word-copy-batch-jitter` stayed
`5680` / `11536`, and `line-word-fallback-batch-continuous` stayed `6496` / `11088`. The noisy
active-time movement was therefore ignored and the variant was removed rather than adding code for
an unproved browser-work reduction.

The benchmark harness then gained a `clientRectEntries` counter in addition to
`clientRectReads`. The earlier counter only showed how often `getClientRects()` was called, but not
how many inline fragments each call materialized. This matters for Line/Rich maxHeight and affix
rows: the same call count can hide very different browser work when a content element has many
fragmented inline boxes. A focused current smoke over eight height/affix rows produced
`35643` client-rect calls and `115822` client-rect entries, an average of `3.25` returned rects per
call. The highest ratios were `rich-word-height-card-batch-jumps` at `1824` calls / `10176` entries
(`5.58x`), `line-height-affix-card-batch-jumps` at `6921` / `26573` (`3.84x`), and
`line-cta-affix-batch-jitter` at `10759` / `37090` (`3.45x`). This is a benchmark credibility
improvement, not a retained runtime optimization by itself: previous maxHeight-only experiments
that replaced client rect reads with bounding rect reads removed the client rect calls but did not
prove lower active time. Future fit-predicate changes should report both call and entry movement so
they do not mistake a call-count-neutral change for unchanged browser work, or a read-type swap for
a proven workload reduction.

Rich structural patching then gained the matching shrink-side whole-prefix fast path. The earlier
retained fast path handled growth from a complete source-prefix boundary by appending only the newly
visible suffix. The shrink-side path handles the opposite direction: when the next clamped point is
an earlier complete source-prefix boundary, it removes only the live DOM suffix and re-appends the
root ellipsis. Partial text cuts, non-prefix boundaries, and unsupported shapes still use the
generic patcher. A browser regression now asserts that shrinking from
`<span>alpha</span> <span>beta</span> <span>gamma</span>...` to
`<span>alpha</span>...` preserves the original first `span` node identity.

A fresh same-machine focused A/B was run by disabling only this shrink-side path, then restoring it.
The focused rows were `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous`,
`rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`, `rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous`,
`rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps`, `rich-word-long-token-lines5-batch-jumps`,
`rich-word-long-token-font-tick-jumps`, and
`rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`. The retained path moved total mutation records
`160914 -> 150738` (`-10176`, `-6.32%`) while leaving `clientRectReads` unchanged at `31856`,
`clientRectEntries` unchanged at `423348`, and bounding-rect reads unchanged at `32384`. Per-row
mutation savings were:
`rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` `16720 -> 15808` (`-912`),
`rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter` `23408 -> 22640` (`-768`),
`rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous` `17456 -> 16320` (`-1136`),
`rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps` `9920 -> 8928` (`-992`),
`rich-word-long-token-lines5-batch-jumps` `11504 -> 10224` (`-1280`),
`rich-word-long-token-font-tick-jumps` `31184 -> 29904` (`-1280`), and
`rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` `50722 -> 46914` (`-3808`). Active time was mixed
across repeats (`2178.6 -> 2126.1 ms` in one run, `2178.6 -> 2183.9 ms` after simplification), so
the retained proof is the deterministic DOM mutation reduction, not a timing claim.

A full Rich smoke after the shrink path measured `281133` mutation records with the same
`60580` client-rect reads and `56117` bounding-rect reads as the preceding append-only Rich
baseline. The immediately preceding full Rich smoke after the grow-only fast path had `294561`
mutation records, so the additional shrink path accounts for another `-13428` mutation records on
the full Rich group. After simplification, the package build measured `110.60 kB` raw and
`23.18 kB` gzip, about `+1.56 kB` raw and `+0.28 kB` gzip over the preceding
`109.04 kB` / `22.90 kB` build.

The whole-prefix grow path then gained a small clamped-to-full extension: if a clamped point is a
complete source prefix and the next state is full, the patcher can remove the root ellipsis and
append the remaining source suffix instead of rebuilding from the root. The same pass also tightened
the correctness guard for complete-prefix growth. A clamped render trims trailing whitespace and
trailing `wbr` nodes before appending the root ellipsis; if a later grow simply appends from such a
boundary, it can lose source spacing or break opportunities. The fast path therefore falls back to
generic rebuild when the complete source prefix is not byte-for-byte present in the live clamped DOM.
Browser regressions now cover both sides: `<span>alpha</span>...` can grow to full content while
preserving the first `span`, while `<span>alpha </span><span>beta</span>` must grow from `alpha...`
to `alpha beta...` rather than `alphabeta...`.

A focused A/B isolated the clamped-to-full extension by disabling only that branch while keeping the
guard. The rows were `rich-word-copy-affix-lines1-grow-full`,
`rich-word-long-token-affix-lines5-grow-full`, `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous`, and
`rich-inline-markup-batch-continuous`. The retained branch changed only one current row:
`rich-word-long-token-affix-lines5-grow-full` mutation records moved `8256 -> 8240` (`-16`).
The focused total moved `45088 -> 45072` mutation records, while bounding-rect reads stayed
`14848`, client-rect reads stayed `11056`, and `clientRectEntries` stayed `31806`. This is a real
structural reduction but too small to present as a meaningful standalone performance win in the
current matrix. The retained value is mostly correctness-complete patch coverage; the current matrix
just proves it does not add read work.

The matrix then gained `rich-trailing-space-markup-batch-continuous` to cover rich HTML where spaces
live inside inline wrappers rather than between them. That row currently measures `5280`
bounding-rect reads, `5248` client-rect reads, `30592` client-rect entries, and `16352` mutation
records. A more aggressive fast path that restored a trimmed trailing text node in place was tested
against this row and rejected: before and after both measured exactly `16352` mutation records,
`5280` bounding-rect reads, `5248` client-rect reads, and `30592` client-rect entries. The rejected
branch also raised the nearby package build to `112.06 kB` raw and `23.48 kB` gzip, so the final
retained code keeps the simpler correctness guard. The package build after reverting that branch
measured `111.60 kB` raw and `23.37 kB` gzip.

The package report renderer then promoted mutation records to the human-readable report surface.
Recent Rich optimizations were proved primarily by mutation-record reductions, but the Markdown
version summary, adjacent summary, top-movers table, and SVG adjacent-delta tooltip previously
showed layout, client-rect-entry, offset, and slot counters without mutation totals. The renderer now
includes mutation-record totals and adjacent deltas in those places while preserving the existing
CV/MOE low-confidence timing markers. A smoke render against
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-trailing-space-after.log` wrote Markdown, SVG, and raw JSON reports and
confirmed the new `Mutation records`, `Mutation delta`, `mutationRecordsDelta`, and SVG
`mutation records` tooltip fields are present.

The renderer then added a separate `Top structural movers by adjacent release` section. Active-time
top movers are still useful for triage, but they are intentionally noisy and often low confidence;
the new section ranks the largest structural counter deltas directly across layout reads,
client-rect entries, mutation records, slot calls, clone/replacement calls, scroll reads, and
ResizeObserver callbacks. A smoke render using the clamped-to-full before/after logs produced the
new section and surfaced `rich-word-long-token-affix-lines5-grow-full` under `Mutation records`,
proving that a small DOM-work change can now be found without relying on active-time ordering.

A fresh current-only LineClamp/RichLineClamp smoke was then used to search for the next retained
optimization target. The absolute totals were `143575` bounding-rect reads, `132043`
client-rect calls, `815197` client-rect entries, and `426379` mutation records. The largest
low-RME structural hotspot was `RichLineClamp` long-token font-size ticks:
`rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` measured `176768` client-rect entries and `46914`
mutation records at `421.3 ms` median active / `1.5%` RME; the related font-tick row measured
`118096` entries and `29360` mutation records at `253.9 ms` / `1.8%` RME. The highest LineClamp
affix rows remained visible too: `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter` had `37090` client-rect entries and
`17702` mutation records, while `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous` had lower timing noise but fewer
entries (`19874`) and mutations (`12139`). High-active jitter rows with RME around `40-55%` were
not used as timing proof, but their structural counters remain useful for hotspot ranking.

One candidate was tested and rejected: giving Rich word-boundary fallback grapheme cuts their own
rank point space so large-width long-token jumps could potentially keep using warm hinted text-run
search. The implementation deliberately kept word rank and fallback rank separate to avoid the
older bug where fallback cuts masqueraded as rank `0`. Focused smoke over the six Rich long-token
rows showed exact structural parity with the current baseline:
`rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps` stayed at `1968` client-rect calls / `24672` entries /
`8928` mutations, `rich-word-long-token-font-tick-jumps` stayed at `3920` / `118096` / `29360`,
`rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` stayed at `6576` / `176768` / `46914`, and
`rich-word-long-token-lines5-batch-jumps` stayed at `2288` / `61248` / `10224`. The variant also
increased the package build from `111.60 kB` / `23.37 kB` gzip to `112.36 kB` / `23.79 kB` gzip.
Because it did not reduce any browser-work counter, the experiment was removed.

The `clientRectEntries` investigation also clarified a tempting but invalid fit-predicate
optimization. In the benchmark harness, entries are counted as the length of the `DOMRectList`
returned by each `getClientRects()` call. Stopping the JavaScript loop after the line limit is
exceeded would not reduce this counter, because the browser has already materialized the whole
rect list. Any future attempt to lower these hotspots must reduce the number of `getClientRects()`
calls or replace the measurement with a correct predicate that does not enumerate all inline
fragments; simply breaking the loop earlier is not a proved workload reduction.

Finally, the package report renderer gained `Top structural hotspots by version` and
`Top structural hotspots by component` sections, with matching compact `structuralHotspots` and
`structuralHotspotsByComponent` JSON fields. This complements the adjacent-version structural
movers: movers explain what changed between versions, while hotspots show which current
scenario/counter pairs are absolutely heaviest and therefore worth investigating next. The
per-component view keeps LineClamp and RichLineClamp browser-work candidates visible when another
component family dominates the global structural top rows.

The renderer now also emits `Top low-noise active hotspots by version` plus compact
`activeHotspots` and `activeHotspotsByComponent` JSON fields. The lists are deliberately narrower
than the raw active-time matrix: they keep only rows with active RME at or below 5% and sort them by
median active time. The per-component view prevents LineClamp or RichLineClamp candidates from
being hidden when another component family dominates the global top rows. Structural columns still
render as `N/A` when counter tracking is disabled, so a counters-off probe-overhead run can be read
for timing without pretending that zero counters mean zero browser work.

The next retained RichLineClamp fit-predicate optimization targets those `clientRectEntries`
hotspots directly. Because `clientRectEntries` is counted as the full `DOMRectList.length` returned
by `getClientRects()`, a loop-level early break cannot reduce this work; the only useful shape is to
avoid the rect-list call for inputs where a cheaper predicate is equivalent. For simple inline-rich
content with no affixes and no `maxHeight`, the measured content bounding height is enough to decide
whether the candidate fits within `maxLines`, provided the rendered tree is only transparent inline
wrappers and the current font metrics leave enough leading for browser inline text rects to stay
within the CSS line box.

The first naive version used the height predicate whenever layout inspection had proved a simple
inline tree. It was rejected in that form: the `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` row uses
`18px` text on a `20px` line height during part of the run, and Chrome can report inline text boxes
taller than the CSS line height in that regime. The naive predicate falsely rejected some fitting
candidates and increased mutation records on that row from `46914` to `57794`. The retained version
therefore requires `fontSize <= lineHeight * 0.8`; tight font metrics fall back to exact
`getClientRects()` line counting. A browser regression also covers the cached-index hazard: after a
simple rich search index is built, child spans are changed to a larger font size, and the second
clamp must re-enter exact rect-list counting instead of trusting the old index.

Fresh focused smoke before the optimization, using
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-heightfit-before.log`, totaled `450640` client-rect entries,
`31712` client-rect calls, `29824` bounding-rect reads, and `154754` mutation records across the
eight affected/guard rows. The retained, current-DOM-rechecked version in
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-heightfit-after-reinspect.log` moved those totals to `113072` entries,
`13328` calls, `48208` bounding-rect reads, and the same `154754` mutations. This is a deliberate
read-type swap: `18384` expensive rect-list calls are replaced by the same number of bounding-rect
height reads, reducing returned rect entries by `337568` (`-74.91%`) while preserving DOM write
work.

The full RichLineClamp smoke comparison confirms that the focused result generalizes to the whole
current Rich scenario set. Rich-only totals from `/tmp/vue-clamp-line-rich-current-hotspots.log`
to `/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-heightfit-full-after-reinspect.log` moved `clientRectEntries`
`581127 -> 183943` (`-397184`, `-68.35%`) and `clientRectReads` `66048 -> 36384`
(`-29664`, `-44.91%`). Bounding-rect reads rose `61424 -> 91088` (`+29664`) by design, while
client-height reads, client-top reads, and mutation records stayed unchanged. Active time moved
`4055.0 -> 3674.2 ms` in that smoke, but several rows still have wide RME, so the retained proof is
the structural reduction in rect-list materialization rather than the timing delta. The package
build after this optimization measured `113.26 kB` raw and `24.10 kB` gzip, about `+1.66 kB` raw
and `+0.73 kB` gzip over the preceding `111.60 kB` / `23.37 kB` build.

The same predicate was then tested for non-native LineClamp text searches. The retained gate is
narrower than the shared text helper: LineClamp passes a simple line-height only when the rendered
path has no before/after affix, no `maxHeight`, and a concrete `maxLines` line limit. Native
single-line and native multi-line cases remain on the CSS/native overflow path, while affix and
height-clipped rows keep exact rect-list or visible-bounds measurement.

A same-machine focused A/B disabled only the LineClamp height-fit hint, then restored it for the
same scenario list. The disabled run `/tmp/vue-clamp-line-heightfit-disabled.log` totaled
`146999` client-rect entries, `38775` client-rect calls, `38208` bounding-rect reads, and
`68019` mutation records. The enabled run `/tmp/vue-clamp-line-heightfit-after.log` moved those
totals to `68592` entries, `19031` calls, `57952` bounding-rect reads, and the same `68019`
mutations. That is `-78407` client-rect entries (`-53.34%`) and `-19744` rect-list calls
(`-50.92%`), traded for `+19744` bounding-rect height reads. Affix guard rows stayed structurally
unchanged. Active time moved `2481.4 -> 2457.8 ms` (`-0.95%`) in the focused smoke; this is
supporting only, because the proof is the deterministic reduction in rect-list materialization.

The full LineClamp smoke after enabling the hint measured Line-only totals of `122179`
client-rect entries and `34523` client-rect calls, compared with `234070` entries and `65995`
calls in the earlier current Line/Rich hotspot scan. Bounding-rect reads rose `82151 -> 113623`,
while client-height reads, client-top reads, client-width reads, and mutation records stayed flat.
Those full-run active totals were not used for timing proof because the before and after full scans
were not a fresh same-process A/B. The additional package size for the LineClamp connection was
small relative to the Rich height-fit change: disabling only the Line hint built at `113.31 kB` raw
and `24.09 kB` gzip, while enabling it built at `113.64 kB` raw and `24.16 kB` gzip.

The tight-font-metric branch of the same predicate was then retained after a correctness audit. The
roomy guard (`fontSize <= lineHeight * 0.8`) avoids rect-list counting from the first probe, but
`18px` text on `20px` line height still had to exact-count every candidate. The improved version
keeps the first exact `getClientRects()` result in the current clamp pass, records the observed
per-line box height, and then applies the same bounding-height formula to later candidates in that
pass. The proof obligation was correctness, not just fewer counter reads: a temporary browser probe
measured plain text, bold text, emoji fallback, explicit `Apple Color Emoji`, CJK, and mixed-font
inline children under `font-size:18px; line-height:20px`. Chrome reported a stable `21px` rect
height, with multi-line bounding height following `21 + (lineCount - 1) * 20`; a durable browser
regression now checks calibrated tight line-box fitting against exact rect-list fitting for mixed
emoji/CJK content.

The full LineClamp/RichLineClamp smoke comparison from
`/tmp/vue-clamp-line-rich-after-heightfit.log` to
`/tmp/vue-clamp-line-rich-tight-linefit-after.log` changed structure only in the two font-size tick
rows targeted by this calibration. Combined Line/Rich totals moved `clientRectEntries`
`306122 -> 220270` (`-85852`, `-28.05%`) and `clientRectReads` `70907 -> 65931`
(`-4976`, `-7.02%`), traded for `boundingRectReads` `204711 -> 209687` (`+4976`). Mutation records,
client-height reads, client-top reads, client-width reads, and scroll reads were unchanged. Split by
component, LineClamp moved `122179 -> 112423` entries (`-7.99%`) and RichLineClamp moved
`183943 -> 107847` entries (`-41.37%`).

The target rows show where the work disappeared. `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` moved
`clientRectReads` `3584 -> 512` and `clientRectEntries` `88912 -> 12816`, with active time
`425.2 -> 409.5 ms` at similarly low RME (`3.4% -> 3.1%`). The Line counterpart moved
`clientRectReads` `2416 -> 512` and `clientRectEntries` `11628 -> 1872`; its active time moved
`155.0 -> 157.2 ms` with low but overlapping RME (`4.0% -> 5.8%`). The full-smoke aggregate active
time moved unfavorably (`6670.6 -> 7919.9 ms`), but many rows with identical structural counters
also shifted by large amounts, so that aggregate is treated as run-to-run timing drift rather than a
performance claim. The retained evidence is the deterministic removal of rect-list materialization
on the two affected rows. The package build after this calibration measured `114.24 kB` raw and
`24.31 kB` gzip, about `+0.60 kB` raw and `+0.15 kB` gzip over the prior simple-height-fit build.

LineClamp affix rows then reused the same calibrated line-fit predicate under a stricter gate. A
temporary direct shortcut that allowed affix rows to use text line-height immediately was rejected:
a browser helper with a `strong` prefix and `button` suffix showed that affix inline boxes can make
the true line box taller than the text line-height. The retained version therefore passes only the
line-height seed for affix-bearing `maxLines` searches, forcing the first exact rect-list count to
calibrate the observed line-box height before later candidates use bounding-height checks. The
durable browser regression compares the calibrated affix predicate with exact rect-list fitting for
two- and three-line limits.

A focused before/after smoke around the affected LineClamp rows first established the exact work
shape. Before the calibrated affix path, the seven-row focus totaled `110551` client-rect entries,
`32107` client-rect calls, and `41815` bounding-rect reads. Afterward it totaled `56755` entries,
`16836` calls, and `57086` bounding-rect reads. That is `-53796` client-rect entries (`-48.66%`)
and `-15271` rect-list calls (`-47.56%`), traded for the same `+15271` bounding-rect reads.
Mutation records stayed exactly `58260`, and the `maxHeight` guard rows stayed structurally
unchanged as intended.

A full LineClamp smoke then confirmed that the structural movement was isolated to four no-`maxHeight`
affix rows. Compared with `/tmp/vue-clamp-line-rich-tight-linefit-after.log`, the LineClamp totals
moved from `112423` to `58627` client-rect entries (`-53796`, `-47.85%`) and from `32619` to
`17348` client-rect calls (`-15271`, `-46.82%`), traded for `115527 -> 130798` bounding-rect reads
(`+15271`). Client-height reads, client-top reads, client-width reads, scroll reads, and mutation
records were unchanged. The rows that moved were:

| Scenario                                 | Client-rect calls | Client-rect entries | Active time / RME                         |
| ---------------------------------------- | ----------------: | ------------------: | ----------------------------------------- |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous`        |    `5856 -> 2272` |     `19874 -> 7232` | `428.5 -> 249.1 ms`, RME `3.9% -> 6.3%`   |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter`            |   `10759 -> 2240` |     `37090 -> 7680` | `535.5 -> 401.5 ms`, RME `29.8% -> 12.3%` |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-jumps`             |     `2496 -> 768` |      `9792 -> 3008` | `111.1 -> 88.1 ms`, RME `12.3% -> 1.3%`   |
| `line-word-long-token-affix-batch-jumps` |     `1920 -> 480` |      `6560 -> 1600` | `116.4 -> 91.0 ms`, RME `17.8% -> 60.5%`  |

Only the continuous and CTA-jumps rows have timing precision strong enough to treat the active-time
movement as supporting evidence. The retained proof is still structural: the same search candidates
use one exact calibration per pass, then avoid repeated inline-fragment materialization. The package
build after this affix calibration measured `114.36 kB` raw and `24.34 kB` gzip, about `+0.12 kB`
raw and `+0.03 kB` gzip over the prior tight-line-fit build.

The next LineClamp hotspot was max-height-only fitting. This path does not need visual line
grouping: with no `maxLines` limit, the question is only whether all rendered content is inside the
root's clipped visible box. The content `getBoundingClientRect()` is the union of those child
fragments, so if that union is inside the root bounds, every child fragment is inside as well. Rows
that also have `maxLines` keep exact `getClientRects()` grouping because they still need the
browser's visual line count.

A browser helper regression now compares the new max-height-only bounding-box predicate with the
old per-rect visible-bounds loop for both short and overflowing affix content, and asserts that the
new path does not call `getClientRects()`. The same test suite still covers the centered/anchored
max-height correctness case through the existing visible-bounds cache tests.

For benchmark proof, two temporary local package targets were built and compared in one browser
process: `/tmp/vue-clamp-maxheight-before.Du0Fms` with the bbox branch disabled, and
`/tmp/vue-clamp-maxheight-after.g7jaFP` with it enabled. The focused same-process A/B over
`line-height-card-batch-jumps`, `line-word-height-card-batch-jumps`, and
`line-height-affix-card-batch-jumps` moved totals as follows:

| Metric              |  Before |   After |    Delta |
| ------------------- | ------: | ------: | -------: |
| `clientRectReads`   | `11076` |     `0` | `-11076` |
| `clientRectEntries` | `37235` |     `0` | `-37235` |
| `boundingRectReads` | `18263` | `29339` | `+11076` |
| `clientHeightReads` | `11076` | `11076` |      `0` |
| `clientTopReads`    |  `6999` |  `6999` |      `0` |
| `mutationRecords`   | `20083` | `20083` |      `0` |

This is a read-type swap with the same number of layout-read calls, but it removes all
fragment-list materialization from the current largest LineClamp `clientRectEntries` hotspot. The
low-RME affix row also moved in the expected timing direction in that same-process A/B:
`line-height-affix-card-batch-jumps` went from `331.4 ms` / `4.3%` RME to `315.9 ms` / `2.3%` RME.
The two smaller height rows had high timing RME, so their active-time movement is not used as proof.

A full LineClamp smoke after retaining the branch confirmed isolation. Compared with the preceding
full Line smoke, only those three max-height-only rows changed structurally. Line totals moved
`clientRectEntries` `58627 -> 21392` (`-37235`, `-63.51%`) and `clientRectReads` `17348 -> 6272`
