(`-11076`, `-63.85%`), traded for `boundingRectReads` `130798 -> 141874` (`+11076`). Mutation
records, client-height reads, client-top reads, client-width reads, and scroll reads were
unchanged. The full-smoke active total moved unfavorably, but many structurally unchanged rows also
shifted substantially in that run, so the retained evidence is the same-process A/B counters plus
the low-RME affix-row timing support. The package build moved from the temporary before target's
`114.44 kB` raw / `24.36 kB` gzip to `114.76 kB` raw / `24.40 kB` gzip.

A follow-up RichLineClamp experiment tried to extend the same simple-line-fit idea to compatible
atomic inline boxes and affix wrappers by measuring each atomic/affix box with
`getBoundingClientRect()` before allowing the cached line-height predicate. The correctness proof
was possible, but the workload proof failed. Same-process package targets
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-atomic-before-clean.tylLKq` and
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-atomic-after-clean.fMZ4qZ` showed that the change removed all rect-list reads
in the focused rows, but replaced them with more total bbox reads and worse active time:

| Metric              |      Before |       After |      Delta |
| ------------------- | ----------: | ----------: | ---------: |
| `clientRectReads`   |     `25317` |         `0` |   `-25317` |
| `clientRectEntries` |     `64963` |         `0` |   `-64963` |
| `boundingRectReads` |     `27824` |     `62397` |   `+34573` |
| `mutationRecords`   |     `93740` |     `93740` |        `0` |
| Active time total   | `1919.6 ms` | `1967.9 ms` | `+48.3 ms` |

The low-RME rows did not support retention: `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous` regressed
`503.3 -> 512.3 ms` with RME `5.1% -> 5.5%`, `rich-word-class-atomic-batch-jumps` regressed
`151.7 -> 162.9 ms` with RME `9.2% -> 8.3%`, and `rich-dense-batch-jumps` regressed
`59.0 -> 64.6 ms` with RME `0.6% -> 3.2%`. One low-RME row improved
(`rich-custom-marker-batch-jumps`, `93.6 -> 90.4 ms`), but the focused total and most stable rows
moved the other way. The experiment was reverted. The current retained Rich simple-line path stays
limited to body-only text runs where it does not need per-atomic or affix bbox checks.

Another rejected experiment tried to persist calibrated tight line-box heights across clamp passes.
The theory was that fixed `18px` text on a `20px` line height pays one exact `getClientRects()`
calibration per pass even though the measured line box is stable across width-only reclamps. Two
fixed tight-font benchmark rows were added to make this input explicit:
`line-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` and
`rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps`.

The cache implementation keyed calibration by computed style, cleared on semantic content changes,
and was narrowed after an initial control-row regression showed that collecting signatures for
roomy metrics added unnecessary RichLineClamp overhead. The narrowed same-process A/B in
`/tmp/vue-clamp-linefit-cache-full-only-ab.log` still failed the timing gate. It reduced
`clientRectReads` `1984 -> 336` and `clientRectEntries` `31776 -> 9152`, traded for
`boundingRectReads` `36560 -> 38208`, with mutation records unchanged at `110244`; active time
moved `1305.6 -> 1337.4 ms`. The Line rows were timing-neutral (`+0.4 ms` and `+0.3 ms`), but
Rich low-RME rows still moved the wrong way: `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`
`410.0 -> 433.3 ms`, and the unchanged-counter `rich-word-long-token-font-tick-jumps`
`253.7 -> 260.0 ms`.

An 8-run Line-only check in `/tmp/vue-clamp-linefit-cache-line-8runs.log` also did not prove a
LineClamp win: the cache reduced `clientRectReads` `992 -> 16` and entries `3552 -> 48`, but active
time moved `294.5 -> 298.25 ms`. The cache code and its direct tests were removed. The fixed
tight-font benchmark rows remain because they cover a real input class that is distinct from the
font-size-tick rows and helped disprove an otherwise plausible optimization.

A narrower LineClamp affix cache was then tested against the remaining `line-cta-affix-*`
rect-list hotspot. The cache key used the measured affix geometry signature plus the text font
metrics and only applied to affix-bearing `maxLines` searches, leaving max-height rows as guards.
The focused smoke in `/tmp/vue-clamp-line-affix-cache-ab.log` removed all target rect-list work:
`clientRectReads` `5760 -> 0` and `clientRectEntries` `19520 -> 0`, traded for
`boundingRectReads` `59399 -> 65159`, with mutation records unchanged. The 3-run active total moved
`1418.1 -> 1303.6 ms`, but the CTA rows had high RME.

The stricter 8-run check in `/tmp/vue-clamp-line-affix-cache-8runs.log` did not confirm a timing
win. It reduced `clientRectReads` `3520 -> 0` and entries `11840 -> 0`, again with unchanged
mutation records, but active time moved `630.15 -> 637.45 ms`; the main continuous row moved
`425.05 -> 444.50 ms` with RME around `18-20%`. Because the timing result did not prove an
improvement, the affix cache was removed too.

An external correctness/performance review against an earlier intermediate branch was reconciled
against the current worktree before continuing optimization. Several cited risks are now covered by
direct browser or helper tests: non-monotonic full candidates for text and rich, percentage-width
InlineClamp shrink-to-fit recovery, rich fallback for unsupported inline flow including `maxHeight`,
fallback grapheme rich rank suppression, transformed ResizeObserver signature comparison, native
multiline zero-width content guards, and max-height fitting while candidate height moves a centered
root. One remaining timing-sensitive concern was same-flush invalidation: an external container
width change and a Vue content prop change could theoretically consume a stale root-width snapshot
before a later ResizeObserver correction. Two browser tests now cover that case for LineClamp and
RichLineClamp by growing an externally sized container and changing the text/html in the same flush;
both must recover the full source at the new wide width rather than keeping an ellipsis from the old
narrow width.

The visible-bounds cache behind the retained max-height-only bounding-box predicate was checked
directly after the external review questioned stale `root.top` reuse. The current implementation is
not a one-time top cache: it keys cached visible bounds by `root.clientHeight`. A new browser helper
regression runs multiple candidates through the same cache in centered flex and bottom-anchored
layouts, asserts that the root top actually moves during the sequence, compares every cached
`fitsContent` result with an uncached exact visible-bounds check, and verifies that the path still
does not call `getClientRects()`. The targeted browser test file passed with 19 tests. This keeps
the max-height-only bbox optimization in place while making its safety boundary explicit.

The next retained shell optimization targets font invalidations that are immediately followed by a
width update. Real font-only changes still need to reclamp, but a font event and a Vue/RO width
change in the same frame should not pay two full text/rich searches. The multiline shell now
schedules font-load reclamps for the next animation frame and records a recompute epoch; if any
reclamp has already run before the scheduled font pass, the delayed font-only pass is skipped
because that earlier pass measured the current font metrics. LineClamp and RichLineClamp browser
regressions cover font-only metric changes by increasing a CSS font-size variable, dispatching
`loadingdone`, and verifying that both components reclamp to shorter two-line output.

A same-process package A/B compared the pre-change package copied to
`/tmp/vue-clamp-font-coalesce-before.BxlXC9` against the current build on four font rows plus four
guard rows. The no-font guards stayed structurally unchanged:
`line-word-long-token-batch-jumps`, `rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps`,
`rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`, and `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter` had identical layout reads
and mutation records. The four font rows moved:

| Scenario                                    | BBox reads     | Client rects            | Mutations        | Active time / RME                         |
| ------------------------------------------- | -------------- | ----------------------- | ---------------- | ----------------------------------------- |
| `line-word-long-token-font-tick-jumps`      | `5664 -> 2784` | unchanged `0 / 0`       | `4032 -> 2592`   | `128.7 -> 140.5 ms`, high RME             |
| `line-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` | `6752 -> 3472` | `512/1872 -> 272/1056`  | `4178 -> 2322`   | `157.1 -> 122.4 ms`, RME `15.4% -> 20.8%` |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-tick-jumps`      | `6992 -> 4112` | unchanged `0 / 0`       | `29360 -> 12400` | `260.0 -> 203.5 ms`, RME `6.8% -> 5.3%`   |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` | `9136 -> 4096` | `512/12816 -> 272/9408` | `46914 -> 22130` | `413.3 -> 245.7 ms`, RME `9.5% -> 0.3%`   |

Across those four target rows, bounding-rect reads moved `28544 -> 14464` (`-49.3%`),
client-rect reads/entries moved `1024/14688 -> 544/10464`, and mutation records moved
`84484 -> 39444` (`-53.3%`). The trade-off is more MutationObserver callback deliveries in the
font rows (`256 -> 444` callbacks) and one row with extra ResizeObserver callbacks, but the
record count and DOM/layout work both drop sharply. Package size moved from the copied before build
at `115.22 kB` / `24.51 kB` gzip to `115.92 kB` / `24.66 kB` gzip. The shared font listener also
now suppresses both `document.fonts.ready` and `loadingdone` callbacks after stop, so an unmounted
component cannot schedule the delayed font rAF from the uncancellable ready promise.

A full current Line/Rich smoke after this change
(`/tmp/vue-clamp-line-rich-current-after-font-coalesce.log`) confirmed the isolation. Compared with
the previous full-current locator, total mutation records moved `504397 -> 459357` (`-8.9%`),
bounding-rect reads `274269 -> 260189` (`-5.1%`), client-rect reads `40544 -> 40064`, and
client-rect entries `146327 -> 142103`. The only structural movers were the four font rows listed
above; all no-font rows were structurally unchanged. The remaining top structural hotspots are now:

| Hotspot family                   | Current state                                                                                                                                                                          |
| -------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Rich affix/atomic rect-list rows | Still large, but extending the bbox/simple-line predicate to affixes and atomic boxes was rejected by same-process A/B because total bbox reads and low-RME active time regressed.     |
| Tight-font long-token rows       | The broad Rich reuse path was rejected, but LineClamp now keeps a narrower style-keyed line-fit cache that removes repeat rect-list line counts without caching clamp results.         |
| Line maxHeight affix card row    | Still large in bbox/mutations; earlier line-capacity and maxHeight-only candidate-order prototypes either had no counter effect or only swapped read kinds without proving lower work. |
| Word-fallback Line row           | Already optimized by fallback-width proof and word-only expansion limit; later fallback full-fit skip attempts regressed this row.                                                     |

This means the next useful runtime change needs a new algorithmic idea or a new input-space hole.
Repeating the rejected affix bbox, line-fit cache, maxHeight line-capacity, or fallback full-fit
experiments would add complexity without new evidence.

The benchmark matrix also gained two long-token novel-width jitter rows:
`line-word-long-token-batch-novel-jitter` and `rich-word-long-token-batch-novel-jitter`. The older
long-token rows remain useful jump-pattern probes, but they repeat the same small width set; the new
rows force every measured width transition to visit a fresh pixel width inside the row. They also
use large jitter rather than ordinary local jitter: in the generated 34 transitions, Line has 18
steps wider than the old 32px physical warm window and Rich has 19, with max deltas of `81px` and
`77px`. This is specifically meant to keep warm-search evidence from depending only on revisiting
previously seen widths or staying inside the fixed local threshold.

The first attempt used novel widths but kept `maxDelta` near 32px. That row validated freshness but
did not test the dynamic-threshold question: fixed-window search already covered almost every step,
so the isolated Line comparison showed no structural change. The row was corrected to large jitter
before drawing conclusions.

A same-process isolated A/B compared package builds from `44cbcab` and `3840b2d` with the current
benchmark harness. The result distinguishes repeated-width wins from novel-width wins:

| Scenario                                  | Structural result from `44cbcab` to `3840b2d`                                          |
| ----------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `line-word-long-token-batch-jumps`        | client-rect reads `3120 -> 1584`, entries `15360 -> 8000`, mutations `4560 -> 3184`    |
| `line-word-long-token-batch-novel-jitter` | client-rect reads `2464 -> 2416`, entries `11056 -> 10656`, mutations `4272 -> 4208`   |
| `rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps`        | client-rect reads `3600 -> 2160`, entries `76960 -> 35280`, mutations `42480 -> 33600` |
| `rich-word-long-token-batch-novel-jitter` | client-rect reads `2992 -> 2208`, entries `56128 -> 34208`, mutations `42816 -> 38352` |

This means the latest committed warm-rank change still has a clear RichLineClamp novel-width
benefit, but its LineClamp benefit is much smaller once repeated-width revisits are removed. The
Line repeated-jump row remains a real workload, but it should not be used alone as proof that the
Line dynamic threshold generalizes across large novel width changes. Timing followed the structural
direction for Rich with usable RME; the Line novel timing moved against the small structural win, so
Line timing is not retained as proof there.

The current dirty worktree was then compared against the same `44cbcab` before target on the same
four rows. This captures the later retained line-fit / rich-probe work rather than isolating the
single committed warm-rank change. It removed all client-rect list reads in the four rows:
`line-word-long-token-batch-jumps` entries `15360 -> 0`, mutations `4560 -> 2400`;
`line-word-long-token-batch-novel-jitter` entries `11056 -> 0`, mutations `4272 -> 3360`;
`rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps` entries `76960 -> 0`, mutations `42480 -> 8928`; and
`rich-word-long-token-batch-novel-jitter` entries `56128 -> 0`, mutations `42816 -> 13648`.
Those rows trade rect-list materialization for bounding-box reads, so future reports should read
the total layout-read mix rather than only client-rect counters.

The large-novel coverage was then extended from long-token text to ordinary word text and CJK word
text: `line-word-copy-batch-novel-jitter`, `line-word-cjk-batch-novel-jitter`,
`rich-word-copy-batch-novel-jitter`, and `rich-word-cjk-batch-novel-jitter`. These rows are guard
rails for dynamic-threshold overreach: long-token text is low rank density, while ordinary word and
CJK inputs can move many more candidate ranks for the same width delta.

A same-process isolated `44cbcab` to `3840b2d` A/B on those four rows showed why the retained
claim must stay narrow. Line ordinary large-novel moved slightly the wrong way structurally:
client-rect reads `1456 -> 1472`, entries `4720 -> 4768`, and mutations `2960 -> 2976`. Line CJK
large-novel was unchanged (`544` client-rect reads, `1196` entries, `1632` mutations). Rich ordinary
large-novel improved (`2704 -> 2224` client-rect reads, `13104 -> 9984` entries,
`13056 -> 11664` mutations), while Rich CJK large-novel was unchanged (`544` client-rect reads,
`3408` entries, `2176` mutations). Timing on the Line/CJK rows is not used as proof because RME was
wide or directions were mixed. The conclusion is that the committed warm-rank change has strong
evidence for Rich ordinary/long-token large-novel inputs, strong evidence for Line repeated
long-token jumps, but no broad Line proof for ordinary or CJK novel large-jump input. The current
dirty worktree's later line-fit path changes the final workload shape for these rows, but it should
not retroactively widen the claim about the isolated warm-rank commit.

## RichLineClamp beyond-window probe-count gate

The RichLineClamp beyond-window hint gate was then refined from a fixed rank-movement cap to the
same probe-count model used by the search helper. The retained version keeps same-width and small
local width changes on the old warm path, but for `boundary="word"` jumps beyond the local pixel
window it now estimates the warm-start probe count from the observed text rank slope and compares it
with the cold binary-search probe count. It accepts the warm hint only when warm is cheaper, or when
it is within one extra probe and the current line limit still gives a patch-locality reason to keep
the probe near the previous structural state.

The same-process smoke pair used the local fixed-rank gate as before
(`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-dynamic-probe-before-rerun.log`) and the probe-count gate as after
(`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-dynamic-probe-after-rerun.log`). Structural counters, not timing, are the
retained evidence:

| Scenario                                   | Structural result from fixed rank cap to probe-count gate                      |
| ------------------------------------------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| `rich-word-copy-lines1-batch-jumps`        | mutations `7296 -> 6864` (`-5.9%`); layout-read counters unchanged             |
| `rich-word-long-token-batch-novel-jitter`  | bbox reads `3792 -> 3712` (`-2.1%`), mutations `13648 -> 12624` (`-7.5%`)      |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`              | unchanged (`10960` bbox reads, `21824` mutations)                              |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-novel-jitter`        | unchanged (`3872` bbox reads, `8640` mutations)                                |
| `rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps`         | unchanged (`3408` bbox reads, `8928` mutations)                                |
| `rich-word-copy-lines5-batch-jumps`        | unchanged (`2112` bbox reads, `5232` mutations)                                |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter` control | unchanged (`9280` bbox, `7616` rect reads, `18964` entries, `22960` mutations) |

The focused totals moved by only `36064 -> 35984` bbox reads (`-0.2%`) and
`88528 -> 87072` mutations (`-1.6%`) because most rows are unchanged; the value is in removing
avoidable work from the two input shapes where the fixed rank cap was too narrow. Active-time
numbers were noisy in this pair and are not used as proof.

A stricter variant made the same probe-count model replace the local `<=32px` warm rule whenever a
word-rank slope was available. That was rejected. In
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-dynamic-probe-allwidth-after.log`, compared with the same fixed-gate before,
`rich-word-copy-batch-jitter` regressed structurally: bbox reads `10960 -> 11120` (`+1.5%`) and
mutations `21824 -> 22272` (`+2.1%`). CJK rows were structurally unchanged, and the two retained
improvements above stayed, but the ordinary word jitter regression proves the all-width rank model
is missing an important cost: small local resizes let the rich patcher mutate a short suffix from
the current probe state, and that DOM patch locality is not fully captured by candidate rank probe
counts. The final design therefore treats the pixel window as a local patching/bootstrap rule, not
as the global threshold for all input scales; beyond that window, the dynamic probe-count model must
prove the hint is worth using.

A full Rich group smoke with the retained gate
(`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-group-dynamic-probe.log`) found no additional structural regressions against
available pre-patch logs. The only changed rows were the two retained wins above; all other
comparable Rich rows had unchanged layout-read and mutation counters.

## Rich height-only benchmark coverage correction

The Rich package matrix had one benchmark semantics bug: `richLineClampBatch` always supplied
`maxLines: 2`, so rows named `rich-height-card-batch-jumps` and
`rich-height-affix-card-batch-jumps` were actually mixed `maxLines + maxHeight` rows. Line batch
fixtures already defaulted `maxLines` only when neither `maxLines` nor `maxHeight` was provided.
Rich now follows the same rule.

To preserve the old mixed-limit logic space, the matrix gained explicit
`rich-lines-height-card-batch-jumps` and `rich-lines-height-affix-card-batch-jumps` rows. A focused
smoke in `/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-height-coverage.log` confirms that the split exercises distinct fit
paths:

| Scenario                                   | Layout counter shape                                                  |
| ------------------------------------------ | --------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `rich-height-card-batch-jumps`             | bbox `4683`, client-rect reads/entries `0/0`, mutations `11202`       |
| `rich-lines-height-card-batch-jumps`       | bbox `2400`, client-rect reads/entries `2283/6198`, mutations `11202` |
| `rich-word-height-card-batch-jumps`        | bbox `1968`, client-rect reads/entries `1824/10176`, mutations `7728` |
| `rich-height-affix-card-batch-jumps`       | bbox `6720`, client-rect reads/entries `0/0`, mutations `10224`       |
| `rich-lines-height-affix-card-batch-jumps` | bbox `2832`, client-rect reads/entries `2064/6048`, mutations `9792`  |

This is a benchmark coverage correction, not a runtime optimization claim. The renamed semantics
make the height-only rows cover the visible-bounds bounding-box predicate directly, while the new
mixed rows keep the exact line-counting path that the previous height rows were accidentally
measuring.

## Style-read counter and Rich max-height guard

The benchmark harness now counts `getComputedStyle` calls on tracked component roots as
`styleReads`. This closes a blind spot in the structural counters: Rich layout inspection can spend
work in computed-style reads even when rect and mutation counters are unchanged.

The first use of that counter found one narrow Rich waste path. `clampRich` previously refreshed
the simple-line fit inspection whenever a cached search index had a `simpleLineFit`, even when the
current fit predicate could not use it because `maxHeight` was present. The runtime now asks for that
inspection only when `lineLimit !== undefined && maxHeight === undefined`, matching the
`fitsContent` fast-path precondition.

Focused A/B used the same current workspace and only toggled this guard, with `styleReads` tracking
enabled in both runs:

- before: `/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-style-before.log`
- after: `/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-style-after.log`

The only structural movement was the intended computed-style work:
`rich-word-height-card-batch-jumps` moved `styleReads 576 -> 0`. The five focused Rich height rows
kept the same bounding-rect, client-rect, client-rect-entry, and mutation counters; total median
active time moved `519.9 ms -> 522.2 ms`, which is within the row RME noise and is not claimed as a
timing improvement. This is retained as a small workload reduction plus a benchmark-observability
improvement, not as elapsed-time proof.

The broader `styleReads` hotspot scan then showed that the largest remaining computed-style work was
not in height-only rows, but in Rich simple-line reinspection during width churn:
`rich-word-long-token-font-tick-jumps` `8928`, `rich-trailing-space-markup-batch-continuous` `8800`,
`rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` `8496`, `rich-word-long-token-lines5-batch-jumps`
`7840`, `rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` `6880`, and
`rich-word-copy-batch-jitter` `3840`.

An aggressive follow-up tested whether Rich simple-line fit reinspection could be reused on
width-driven recomputes. The prototype passed a "no pending font event" signal from the multiline
shell, let `RichLineClamp` opt into `reuseSimpleLineFit`, and validated the body font/style
signature plus a cheap visible descendant `class` / `id` / `style` attribute signature before
skipping `inspectLayout(body)`.

Focused A/B toggled only that prototype:

- before: `/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-simpleline-reuse-before.log`
- after: `/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-simpleline-reuse-after-slim.log`

The six focused Rich rows moved:

| Scenario                                      | Style reads      | Client rects           | BBox reads        | Mutations         |
| --------------------------------------------- | ---------------- | ---------------------- | ----------------- | ----------------- |
| `rich-trailing-space-markup-batch-continuous` | `8800 -> 1760`   | unchanged `0 / 0`      | unchanged `10528` | unchanged `16352` |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`                 | `3840 -> 1920`   | unchanged `0 / 0`      | unchanged `10960` | unchanged `21824` |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-tick-jumps`        | unchanged `8928` | unchanged `0 / 0`      | unchanged `4112`  | unchanged `12400` |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`   | unchanged `8496` | unchanged `272 / 9408` | unchanged `4096`  | unchanged `22130` |
| `rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` | `6880 -> 480`    | `480 / 15408 -> 0 / 0` | `4496 -> 4976`    | unchanged `23216` |
| `rich-word-long-token-lines5-batch-jumps`     | `7840 -> 480`    | unchanged `0 / 0`      | unchanged `3728`  | unchanged `10224` |

Across those rows, `styleReads` moved `44784 -> 22064` (`-50.7%`), client-rect
reads/entries moved `752 / 24816 -> 272 / 9408`, bounding-rect reads moved `37920 -> 38400`, and
mutation records stayed `106146`. A full Line/Rich smoke showed the same structural direction:
`styleReads 81856 -> 47008`, client-rect entries `142103 -> 126695`, bounding-rect reads
`260189 -> 260669`, and mutation records unchanged.

The prototype was rejected on correctness. A stronger browser regression showed that stylesheet- and
CSS-variable-driven child font metrics can change while the body computed-style signature and cheap
visible descendant attribute signature stay unchanged. In that case reusing the cached
`simpleLineFit` skips the exact rect-list line count that proves whether height-based line counting
is still valid. The retained code therefore keeps the narrow max-height guard and the `styleReads`
counter, but still reinspects current Rich child line metrics before using cached search-index
metadata. The rejected experiment is preserved here as evidence that the counter found real work,
but the current implementation deliberately pays that work until a stricter invalidation proof
exists.

That reinspection also exposed a correctness hole in the cached search metadata itself. If the first
rich pass saw a transparent inline wrapper and cached text cuts inside it, then CSS later changed the
same wrapper to `inline-block`, the stale index could keep slicing inside what had become an atomic
inline box. A browser regression now covers this by first caching `<span>observabilityPlatform1</span>`
as searchable text, then changing the live span to `display:inline-block;width:180px` under a
`120px` one-line probe. Before the fix the second clamp produced a partial span
`observabilityPl…`; after the fix the current layout inspection rebuilds the search index and the
atomic span is dropped as a unit. Focused Rich smoke over the six style-read hotspot rows kept the
same structural totals as before this correctness fix: `styleReads 44784`, client-rect
reads/entries `752 / 24816`, bounding-rect reads `37920`, and mutation records `106146`. The package
build moved from `115.92 kB` / `24.66 kB` gzip to `116.45 kB` / `24.76 kB` gzip.

A later LineClamp-only pass kept the same idea in a narrower form. The earlier rejected prototype
tried to reuse rich simple-line inspection across child style changes; the retained Line change only
reuses the calibrated `maxLineBoxHeight` for plain text when the text computed-style key and the
before/after affix layout key are unchanged. It still reads current computed style, still recalibrates
when font-size or affix geometry changes, and font-load notifications clear the cache before the next
reclamp.

Focused Line smoke over the affected affix rows showed the intended structural trade-off:

| Scenario                                      | Client rects           | BBox reads       | Mutations         | Style reads      |
| --------------------------------------------- | ---------------------- | ---------------- | ----------------- | ---------------- |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous`             | `2272 / 7232 -> 0 / 0` | `12704 -> 14976` | unchanged `12139` | unchanged `2272` |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter`                 | `2240 / 7680 -> 0 / 0` | `17479 -> 19719` | unchanged `17702` | unchanged `2240` |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-jumps`                  | `768 / 3008 -> 0 / 0`  | `4800 -> 5568`   | unchanged `5312`  | unchanged `768`  |
| `line-word-long-token-affix-batch-jumps`      | `480 / 1600 -> 0 / 0`  | `3840 -> 4320`   | unchanged `3024`  | unchanged `480`  |
| `line-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` | `480 / 1680 -> 0 / 0`  | `3520 -> 4000`   | unchanged `2544`  | unchanged `480`  |

The guard rows behaved as designed: ordinary no-affix rows were structurally unchanged, and
`line-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` kept its exact calibration path
(`272 / 1056` client rects unchanged) because the font-size key changed.

The full current Line/Rich smoke after this change
(`/tmp/vue-clamp-current-line-rich-linefit-cache-full.log`) compared with the previous current smoke
(`/tmp/vue-clamp-current-line-rich-smoke-latest.log`) moved total client-rect reads
`40064 -> 33824` (`-15.6%`) and client-rect entries `142103 -> 120903` (`-14.9%`). Bounding-rect
reads increased `260189 -> 266429` (`+2.4%`) because the cached fit path still measures the current
root/candidate boxes instead of collecting line fragments. Mutation records and style reads stayed
unchanged at `459357` and `81856`. Median active-time totals moved `9223.8 ms -> 8041.6 ms`, but this
is secondary evidence only; the retained proof is the deterministic replacement of repeated
rect-list line counting with cheaper current-box reads under an explicit style and affix key.

One additional Rich mutation experiment was rejected. `patchRich` removes source suffixes one child
at a time, so a prototype replaced that loop with `Range.deleteContents()` to test whether Chromium
would coalesce MutationObserver records. Focused smoke over twelve Rich mutation-heavy rows
(`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-range-delete-smoke.log`) showed no structural counter movement at all:
mutation records, client-rect reads/entries, bbox reads, and style reads were unchanged on every row.
Several low-RME rows got slower instead, for example `rich-height-card-batch-jumps`
`88.4 ms -> 161.4 ms` and `rich-custom-marker-batch-jumps` `77.2 ms -> 146.8 ms`. The code therefore
keeps the simpler per-child removal loop.

## Counter-tracking overhead check

Claude's review correctly identified one benchmark validity risk: the structural probes themselves
add work inside the active timing window. The harness now has an explicit switch for that question.
By default it still tracks layout/style/DOM counters, because those counters are the primary proof
for workload reduction. With `VUE_CLAMP_BENCH_COUNTERS=0`, the benchmark keeps the same
ResizeObserver-based stability wait but disables the monkey-patched layout, style, clone,
replacement, and mutation counters. Reports include `counterTracking`; when it is `false`,
structural summaries and structural deltas are rendered as `N/A` instead of zero.

A focused same-worktree report compared current Line/Rich hotspots with counters off and on:

- counters on: `/tmp/vue-clamp-probe-overhead-counters-on.log`
- counters off: `/tmp/vue-clamp-probe-overhead-counters-off.log`

| Scenario                                      | Counters on | Counters off |   Delta | Active RME on/off |
| --------------------------------------------- | ----------: | -----------: | ------: | ----------------: |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter`                 |  `633.1 ms` |   `629.9 ms` | `+0.5%` |     `1.0% / 4.0%` |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`                 |  `486.2 ms` |   `455.0 ms` | `+6.9%` |   `16.3% / 15.2%` |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`   |  `239.2 ms` |   `235.5 ms` | `+1.6%` |     `3.6% / 1.6%` |
| `rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` |  `189.7 ms` |   `188.0 ms` | `+0.9%` |     `2.0% / 0.2%` |

The four-row total moved `1548.2 -> 1508.4 ms` (`+2.6%` with counters enabled). The low-RME rows put
the probe overhead in the low single digits, while the `rich-word-copy` delta is inside high timing
variance and should not be interpreted. This does not prove an optimization by itself. It proves the
benchmark needs both modes: the default counter-tracked mode remains necessary to show reduced
browser work, while counters-off runs are useful when a small active-time delta might be dominated
by the measurement probes.

## Rejected max-height visible-window fast accept

The next low-RME Line hotspot was `line-height-affix-card-batch-jumps`: in the current full
Line/Rich smoke it had `20576` bounding-rect reads, `6921` client-height reads, `4407` client-top
reads, `13154` mutation records, and `311.2 ms` active time at `12.0%` RME. A candidate optimization
tried to let max-height-only probes accept a candidate from a cached visible window before rereading
the root's `clientHeight` / `clientTop`, but only when the new content rect was still inside the
cached window and was not shorter than that cached window. The height guard was intended to avoid
the known correctness pitfall where centered or bottom-anchored roots move when a shorter candidate
shrinks the root.

Browser tests over the Line/Rich clamp suites passed, but the focused same-process package A/B
showed no structural benefit:

- before: `/tmp/vue-clamp-layout-before`
- after: `/tmp/vue-clamp-layout-after`
- benchmark log: `/tmp/vue-clamp-layout-visible-cache-ab.log`

| Scenario                             | Structural result      | Active time / RME                        |
| ------------------------------------ | ---------------------- | ---------------------------------------- |
| `line-height-card-batch-jumps`       | all counters unchanged | `76.0 -> 73.9 ms`, RME `22.0% -> 5.9%`   |
| `line-height-affix-card-batch-jumps` | all counters unchanged | `278.7 -> 258.8 ms`, RME `17.8% -> 3.3%` |
| `rich-height-card-batch-jumps`       | all counters unchanged | `79.4 -> 79.3 ms`, RME `4.9% -> 7.4%`    |
| `rich-height-affix-card-batch-jumps` | all counters unchanged | `87.9 -> 87.5 ms`, RME `4.4% -> 2.7%`    |

The package build also grew from `117.37 kB` / `25.02 kB` gzip to `117.72 kB` / `25.08 kB` gzip.
Because the exact root-read counters did not move, the active-time movement is not accepted as an
optimization signal. The experiment was removed.

## Mutation breakdown counter

The mutation counter was then split by MutationObserver record type. The benchmark still reports
total `mutationRecords`, but it now also records child-list, character-data, and attribute records,
plus added-node and removed-node totals. This is a benchmark-observability change only; it does not
change runtime behavior, and `VUE_CLAMP_BENCH_COUNTERS=0` still disables these counters together
with the other structural probes.

A focused current smoke (`/tmp/vue-clamp-mutation-breakdown-smoke.log`) over three mutation-heavy
rows showed why the split is useful:

| Scenario                                    | Mutation breakdown                                                                             |
| ------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `line-height-affix-card-batch-jumps`        | `13154` total = `7634` child-list + `5520` attribute; added/removed nodes `7282/7282`          |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jumps`           | `9792` total = `7632` child-list + `1008` character-data + `1152` attribute; nodes `4800/4800` |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` | `22130` total = `21136` child-list + `994` attribute; nodes `16736/16736`                      |

The generated report at `/tmp/vue-clamp-mutation-breakdown-report/out/310-package-benchmark-matrix.md`
lists these as structural hotspots, so future DOM-patch experiments can prove whether they remove
node churn, text rewrites, or Vue attribute churn instead of relying on the single aggregate
MutationObserver count.

## Text-node data writes for text clamps

The mutation split exposed a concrete Line/Inline hotspot: text-only candidate probes were replacing
the sole text child with `textContent`, producing child-list records and added/removed text nodes
for every candidate. The runtime now updates an existing sole `Text` child through `Text.data` and
falls back to `textContent` only when the target has a different child structure. This is a runtime
workload reduction, not a search-algorithm change: the same candidate texts are still measured.

Two temporary local package targets were built and compared in one browser process:

- before: `/tmp/vue-clamp-textdata-before`
- after: `/tmp/vue-clamp-textdata-after`
- jump log: `/tmp/vue-clamp-textdata-ab.log`
- continuous/jitter log: `/tmp/vue-clamp-textdata-continuous-ab.log`

Across five Line/Inline jump rows, structural node churn moved as follows:

| Metric                         |     Before |      After |    Delta |
| ------------------------------ | ---------: | ---------: | -------: |
| `childListMutationRecords`     |    `24647` |     `4016` | `-83.7%` |
| `characterDataMutationRecords` |        `0` |    `20631` |      `+` |
| `addedNodes`                   |    `24103` |     `3472` | `-85.6%` |
| `removedNodes`                 |    `24103` |     `3472` | `-85.6%` |
| `mutationRecords`              |    `37271` |    `37271` |   `0.0%` |
| active time                    | `916.3 ms` | `906.9 ms` |  `-1.0%` |

The per-row structural movement was consistent:

| Scenario                              | Child-list records |    Added nodes | Active time / RME                         |
| ------------------------------------- | -----------------: | -------------: | ----------------------------------------- |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-jumps`          |      `3008 -> 768` |  `2816 -> 576` | `120.6 -> 120.6 ms`, RME `0.9% -> 11.6%`  |
| `line-word-fallback-batch-continuous` |     `8016 -> 1008` | `8016 -> 1008` | `290.4 -> 281.7 ms`, RME `2.3% -> 1.6%`   |
| `line-height-affix-card-batch-jumps`  |     `7634 -> 1696` | `7282 -> 1344` | `312.3 -> 313.5 ms`, RME `12.2% -> 15.8%` |
| `inline-path-end-batch-jumps`         |      `2960 -> 272` |  `2960 -> 272` | `93.5 -> 96.5 ms`, RME `4.8% -> 18.7%`    |
| `inline-path-middle-batch-jumps`      |      `3029 -> 272` |  `3029 -> 272` | `99.5 -> 94.6 ms`, RME `13.2% -> 7.1%`    |

Across four continuous/jitter rows, the same node-churn pattern held:
`childListMutationRecords` moved `20332 -> 3440` (`-83.1%`), `addedNodes` moved
`20204 -> 3312` (`-83.6%`), and `removedNodes` moved `20188 -> 3296` (`-83.7%`). Total mutation
records again stayed unchanged because child-list records were replaced by character-data records.
Active time moved `1930.4 -> 1963.4 ms` (`+1.7%`) across that noisy smoke set, so timing is not
used as the proof.

The retained claim is therefore narrow: LineClamp and InlineClamp now do much less DOM node
allocation/removal during text-only candidate probes. The current benchmark evidence does not prove
a general active-time improvement for this change. The package build moved from the temporary
before target's `117.37 kB` / `25.02 kB` gzip to `117.58 kB` / `25.09 kB` gzip, so the measured
size cost is about `+0.21 kB` raw and `+0.07 kB` gzip.

## Rejected rich partial-text patching

The next tempting follow-up was to apply the same idea to RichLineClamp. The hypothesis was that
rich long-token rows still rebuilt too many nodes because `patchRich` only updated `Text.data` when
both the previous and next clamped points were inside the same source text node. A prototype added
two more partial-text fast paths:

- growing from a partial text cut restored that live text node to its full source text and appended
  only the following source fragment
- shrinking to a partial text cut updated the live text node and removed later siblings/ancestors

Browser identity tests for those local transitions passed, but the package smoke did not support
retaining the code. The before data is from `/tmp/vue-clamp-after-textdata-hotspots.log`; the after
data is from `/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-partial-text-patch-after.log`.

| Scenario                                      | Structural result                                                                                         | Active time / RME                        |
| --------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------- |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`            | child-list `9392 -> 8288` (`-11.8%`), added/removed `5312 -> 4592` (`-13.6%`), mutations `22960 -> 22784` | `306.5 -> 553.4 ms`, RME `4.3% -> 3.3%`  |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`                 | child-list `11664 -> 11584` (`-0.7%`), mutations unchanged `21824`                                        | `540.7 -> 547.7 ms`, RME `14.0% -> 3.1%` |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`   | child-list unchanged `21136`, character-data `0 -> 704`, mutations `22130 -> 22834` (`+3.2%`)             | `243.9 -> 251.3 ms`, RME `5.0% -> 2.5%`  |
| `rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` | child-list unchanged `22256`, character-data `0 -> 1280`, mutations `23216 -> 24496` (`+5.5%`)            | `206.4 -> 207.0 ms`, RME `4.0% -> 3.6%`  |

The long-token target rows did not reduce child-list records or node add/remove counts at all; they
only added extra character-data records, increasing total mutation records. The one row with a real
child-list reduction, `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`, got much slower in the same smoke with
low RME. The code size also moved from `117.58 kB` / `25.09 kB` gzip to `120.88 kB` / `25.40 kB`
gzip. The experiment was removed. The practical conclusion is that RichLineClamp's remaining
long-token node churn is dominated by moving across many wrapper spans and hidden-probe candidate
states, not by repeated partial cuts inside one stable text node.

## Max-height clientTop cache

The remaining `line-height-affix-card-batch-jumps` height-only hotspot still reread `clientTop`
inside max-height candidate checks. The previous visible-window cache correctly rereads the root
visual top whenever candidate height changes, because centered and bottom-anchored roots can move
as text grows or shrinks. However, the root border-top offset itself does not change during a clamp
pass. The runtime now keeps `clientTop` inside the pass-local visible-bounds cache while still
refreshing the visual root top for every changed height.

The before data is the mutation-breakdown report
`/tmp/vue-clamp-mutation-breakdown-report/out/310-package-benchmark-matrix.local.json`; the after
data is a focused current smoke in `/tmp/vue-clamp-clienttop-cache-rerun.log`.

| Scenario                             |        `clientTopReads` | Other structural counters                                       | Active time / RME                       |
| ------------------------------------ | ----------------------: | --------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------- |
| `line-height-affix-card-batch-jumps` | `4407 -> 1840` `-58.2%` | bbox `20576`, client-height `6921`, mutations `13154` unchanged | `321.2 -> 347.7 ms`, RME `4.9% -> 4.8%` |

The timing moved the wrong way in this smoke, so it is not an elapsed-time optimization claim. The
retained claim is narrower and structural: the target row performs fewer `clientTop` getter reads
without changing candidate search shape, bounding-rect reads, client-height reads, or mutation
records. A browser regression in `text-layout.browser.test.ts` compares cached max-height results
against exact fitting while the root moves and asserts that `clientTop` is read once across the
candidate sequence. The package build moved from the Text.data baseline's `117.58 kB` /
`25.09 kB` gzip to `117.74 kB` / `25.12 kB` gzip, about `+0.16 kB` raw and `+0.03 kB` gzip.

## Remaining hotspot scan after clientTop caching

A full current smoke after the `clientTop` cache is in
`/tmp/vue-clamp-current-full-smoke-after-clienttop.log`. The retained next-step conclusion is not
that there is no work left; it is that the highest Line/Rich/Inline rows no longer show an obvious
single redundant getter like the previous `clientTop` case.

The largest Line/Inline active rows are still real candidate-search work:

| Scenario                           | Main structural shape                                                                      |
| ---------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous`  | bbox `14976`, mutations `12139`, style reads `2272`, active `540.4 ms` / RME `4.5%`        |
| `line-word-copy-batch-jitter`      | bbox `12272`, mutations `11536`, style reads `2160`, active `489.7 ms` / RME `4.7%`        |
| `inline-path-middle-batch-jitter`  | scroll-width reads `5010`, bbox `7680`, mutations `11164`, active `500.7 ms` / RME `13.9%` |
| `inline-path-end-batch-continuous` | scroll-width reads `4512`, bbox `7296`, mutations `10416`, active `465.4 ms` / RME `11.8%` |

For LineClamp, the remaining style reads come from validating text metrics before using the
simple-line fit predicate. Skipping those reads would require a stronger proof that width changes
cannot change computed text metrics; earlier Rich simple-line reuse experiments showed that
stylesheet and CSS-variable changes can invalidate that assumption. For InlineClamp, the high
`scrollWidth` rows are the actual one-line fit probes; the Text.data change already converted most
node replacement into character-data writes without reducing candidate count.

The largest Rich rows are dominated by structural node churn:

| Scenario                                      | Main structural shape                                                                              |
| --------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` | child-list `22256`, added nodes `16832`, style reads `6880`, active `208.7 ms` / RME `1.9%`        |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`   | child-list `21136`, added nodes `16736`, style reads `8496`, active `252.5 ms` / RME `4.0%`        |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`                 | child-list `11664`, added nodes `5888`, mutations `21824`, active `518.2 ms` / RME `7.3%`          |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`            | client-rect entries `18964`, child-list `9392`, mutations `22960`, active `530.9 ms` / RME `10.7%` |

The just-rejected Rich partial-text patch did not reduce child-list churn in the long-token target
rows, so repeating that direction is not justified. The likely remaining Rich opportunity, if any,
would need to reduce whole-wrapper prefix churn across search candidates, not merely update text
inside one existing node. That is a larger structural-patching problem and should be proved with a
same-process A/B on the rows above before being retained.

One temporary browser diagnostic directly exercised `patchRich` on a long-token span sequence and
counted mutation records for structural transitions. It confirmed the current whole-prefix fast
paths are already active: applying the same clamped state produced zero mutations, growing kept the
existing prefix and mostly appended wrapper suffixes, and shrinking removed wrapper suffixes before
adding the ellipsis. The useful numbers were:

| Transition      | Added nodes | Removed nodes | Child-list records | Character-data records |
| --------------- | ----------: | ------------: | -----------------: | ---------------------: |
| Initial token 3 |           8 |             0 |                  2 |                      0 |
| Grow token 8    |          11 |             1 |                  3 |                      0 |
| Shrink token 4  |           1 |             9 |                 10 |                      0 |
| Grow token 12   |          17 |             1 |                  3 |                      0 |
| Same token 12   |           0 |             0 |                  0 |                      0 |
| Full            |           8 |             1 |                  2 |                      0 |

That diagnostic was intentionally not retained as a test fixture because it only explains the
current hotspot shape. The durable conclusion is that RichLineClamp's high long-token mutation rows
come from wrapper add/remove work between candidate states. A future optimization must change how
the hidden probe represents or patches those wrapper suffixes, and it must keep the unsupported
layout fallback, trailing-whitespace full-candidate verification, and full-candidate recovery tests
green while proving fewer child-list records in a same-process A/B.

## Current-state reconciliation of the external review

The external review remains useful as an audit list, but several findings targeted an earlier
intermediate branch and have been absorbed by the current worktree. Current code and tests now cover
the high-risk correctness class: skipped full-fit probes no longer skip the full-candidate
correctness check on same-width or growing text/rich passes; InlineClamp no longer trusts percentage
root widths, including `calc(var(...))` forms that can resolve to percentages, in shrink-to-fit
parents; LineClamp replaces the shallow visible-text state on semantic prop changes; font-load
callbacks no longer pass event objects into width parameters; transformed ResizeObserver entries are
compared against visual snapshots when layout and visual pixels are not comparable; unsupported rich
layouts still fall back before reporting `clamped=false`; fallback grapheme rich cuts do not publish
a fake word rank; and native multiline measurement still refuses zero-width content elements.

The benchmark criticism should still shape how results are reported. Counter-tracked timing is fair
for A/B work but not strong enough for small timing claims by itself, because probes run inside the
active timing window and RME can be much larger than a few percentage points. The current retained
standard is therefore: use structural counters as the main proof that browser work changed, mark
active-time deltas as low confidence when mean MOE intervals overlap or median/mean directions
disagree, and use counters-off timing only as a separate check when claiming small elapsed-time
movement. This keeps the latest dynamic-threshold conclusion narrow: the retained Rich
beyond-window gate has structural evidence on specific word-boundary inputs, while the fixed local
width window remains part of the cost model because it captures cheap DOM patch locality that rank
probe counts do not describe.

Some benchmark-harness findings from that review also targeted an earlier state. The current report
renderer warns when a log file has no final `PACKAGE_MATRIX_BENCHMARK` marker instead of silently
dropping it, and the package matrix already includes CJK word-boundary and novel-width jitter rows
for both LineClamp and RichLineClamp. Those rows are guard coverage for input-space shape, not proof
that every dynamic warm-search gate improves every text distribution.

## Rich dynamic atomic benchmark coverage

The package matrix now includes `rich-word-dynamic-atomic-batch-jumps`, a RichLineClamp word-boundary
row whose inline token wrappers switch `display` between `inline` and `inline-block` through a CSS
variable before each measured width step. This is coverage, not an optimization claim. It protects
the correctness boundary behind Rich `inspectLayout`: a cached search index is valid only while
transparent inline wrappers remain transparent. If CSS turns those wrappers atomic, the logical runs
must be rebuilt and later candidate searches must drop atomic spans as units instead of slicing text
inside them.

Current report-mode baseline: `/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-dynamic-atomic-report.log`. The row ran with
5 samples at `3.6%` active RME and fixed structural counters: `1440` bounding-rect reads,
`2400` client-rect reads, `6480` client-rect entries, `5314` mutation records,
`2640` child-list records, `1680/1680` added/removed nodes, and `48` style reads. The important
signal is the shape: the row exercises both rect-list fitting and the style reinspection path that
would disappear under an unsafe Rich simple-line/search-index cache.

## Rich root ellipsis stability

The next retained Rich optimization reduces wrapper churn without changing candidate search. In
clamped-to-clamped whole-prefix patches, the root-level ellipsis text node is now kept stable and
source suffix nodes are inserted or removed before it. The fallback path still removes and
re-appends the ellipsis when the boundary needs trailing-whitespace trimming or when the target state
is full, so the existing whitespace and full-candidate correctness tests remain the safety boundary.

The focused same-process package A/B used the pre-change package copy
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-ellipsis-before` and the retained implementation copy
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-ellipsis-after-simplified`; log:
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-ellipsis-simplified-ab.log`.

| Scenario                                      | Structural result                                                                                     | Active time / RME                        |
| --------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------- |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`            | child-list `9392 -> 8528` (`-9.2%`), mutations `22960 -> 22096` (`-3.8%`)                             | `521.6 -> 526.6 ms`, RME `1.7% -> 6.8%`  |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`                 | unchanged child-list `11664`, unchanged mutations `21824`                                             | timing noisy, not used                   |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`   | child-list `21136 -> 18256` (`-13.6%`), mutations `22130 -> 19250` (`-13.0%`)                         | `246.8 -> 243.2 ms`, RME `4.1% -> 13.4%` |
| `rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` | child-list `22256 -> 16944` (`-23.9%`), mutations `23216 -> 17904` (`-22.9%`), nodes `16832 -> 14176` | `204.3 -> 188.3 ms`, RME `10.7% -> 5.3%` |

Focused totals moved child-list records `64448 -> 55392` (`-14.1%`), total mutation records
`90130 -> 81074` (`-10.0%`), and added/removed nodes `44768 -> 40240` (`-10.1%`). Layout-read
counters were unchanged, which is expected: this optimization changes DOM patch churn per candidate,
not the number of fit probes. Active-time totals moved `1442.4 -> 1452.5 ms` in this smoke, so the
retained claim is structural workload reduction rather than elapsed-time reduction.

A smaller forward-only variant was tested in
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-ellipsis-forward-only-ab.log`. It reduced the same focused total child-list
records only to `59776` (`-7.3%`) and mutation records to `85458` (`-5.2%`). Its build was smaller
(`118.17 kB` / `25.20 kB` gzip), but the complete grow+shrink implementation doubled the structural
reduction for the actual high-churn rows. The retained build is `118.81 kB` / `25.32 kB` gzip
against the pre-change `117.73 kB` / `25.12 kB` gzip, so the incremental cost is about `+1.08 kB`
raw and `+0.20 kB` gzip.

A follow-up `Range.deleteContents()` variant was tested on top of the retained root-ellipsis
implementation (`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-range-delete-ab.log`). It did not reduce any structural
counters: focused totals stayed exactly flat at `81074` mutation records, `55392` child-list records,
and `40240` added/removed nodes. Active time moved `1463.9 -> 1591.9 ms` (`+8.7%`), with the
low-RME long-token rows regressing clearly (`rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`
`243.8 -> 284.6 ms`, `rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` `199.9 -> 254.2 ms`). Because the
bulk-delete form adds code and build cost without reducing observer-visible work, the retained patch
keeps the simple child-removal loop.

A current-only focused smoke after the root-ellipsis optimization
(`/tmp/vue-clamp-current-focused-hotspots-after-ellipsis.log`) is the latest local hotspot baseline
for the next loop:

| Scenario                                      | Main structural shape                                                                       | Active time / RME       |
| --------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------- |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter`                 | bbox `19719`, mutations `17702`, child-list `1824`, style reads `2240`                      | `465.1 ms`, RME `37.5%` |
| `line-height-affix-card-batch-jumps`          | bbox `20576`, client-height `6921`, client-top `1840`, mutations `13154`                    | `247.6 ms`, RME `5.1%`  |
| `inline-path-middle-batch-jitter`             | scroll-width `5010`, bbox `7680`, mutations `11164`, child-list `1077`                      | `203.5 ms`, RME `12.7%` |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`            | bbox `9280`, rects `7616 / 18964`, mutations `22096`, child-list `8528`                     | `378.1 ms`, RME `58.1%` |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`                 | bbox `10960`, style reads `3840`, mutations `21824`, child-list `11664`                     | `489.9 ms`, RME `4.1%`  |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`   | bbox `4096`, rects `272 / 9408`, style reads `8496`, mutations `19250`, child-list `18256`  | `236.7 ms`, RME `4.1%`  |
| `rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` | bbox `4496`, rects `480 / 15408`, style reads `6880`, mutations `17904`, child-list `16944` | `190.3 ms`, RME `5.9%`  |

Two tempting follow-ups remain unimplemented because the current evidence is not strong enough.
First, same-width/font reclamps still verify the full rich candidate before returning a clamped
result. Skipping that verification would save the full->clamped probe churn in synthetic font rows,
but a real font load or CSS metric change can make the full source fit at the same width, so the
optimization needs a stricter "font metrics unchanged" proof before it is safe. Browser regressions
now cover that exact boundary for both LineClamp and RichLineClamp: start clamped at `24px`, shrink
the same-width font metrics to `12px`, dispatch `loadingdone`, and require the full text/rich HTML
to be restored with `clamped=false`. Second, retaining Rich probe suffix nodes and hiding them would
trade child-list records for attribute/style state and cannot hide intervening text-node spaces with
a single CSS marker. Any future attempt in that direction must prove both DOM visibility correctness
and lower total mutation work in a same-process A/B before replacing the current structural patcher.

The public package matrix now has matching coverage rows:
`line-word-font-size-recover-full-same-width` and
`rich-word-font-size-recover-full-same-width`. They keep width fixed at `420px` and alternate
`--bench-font-size` between `12px` and `24px` through `loadingdone`, so the matrix covers both the
same-width recovery to full content and the return to clamped output. A smoke run
(`/tmp/vue-clamp-font-recovery-coverage-smoke.log`) recorded stable structural work:

| Scenario                                      | Structural shape                                                  | Active time / RME      |
| --------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------- |
| `line-word-font-size-recover-full-same-width` | bbox `1152`, rects `48 / 144`, mutations `822`, child-list `192`  | `48.2 ms`, RME `4.2%`  |
| `rich-word-font-size-recover-full-same-width` | bbox `720`, rects `48 / 336`, mutations `1782`, child-list `1680` | `56.4 ms`, RME `21.7%` |

These rows are coverage, not an optimization claim. They make future font-invalidation changes pay
for the exact correctness boundary that prevents blindly skipping same-width full-candidate probes.

## Line affix height-fit verification

The demo-page narrow-width regression exposed a LineClamp correctness boundary in the simple
line-height predicate. At `315-321px`, the first website `LineClamp` example could keep a two-line
prefix such as:

`Vue (pronounced /vjuː/, like view) is a progressive framework for building user interfaces.…`

while a browser-fit clone showed a three-line candidate around

`Vue (pronounced /vjuː/, like view) is a progressive framework for building user interfaces. Unlike other monolithic fra…`

still fit with the after-slot button. The root cause is that an affix-calibrated content
`getBoundingClientRect().height` can be slightly above the cached three-line threshold even when
exact `getClientRects()` line grouping is still within `maxLines`. Treating that height overflow as
a hard rejection made the search settle on a shorter two-line candidate.

The retained fix marks LineClamp affix line-fit caches as requiring exact verification near the
overflow boundary. The height shortcut still accepts candidates below the threshold and still
rejects candidates that are clearly at least one extra line over the limit; only the narrow
threshold band falls back to exact rect line counting. Browser evidence:

- `vp test -c vite.browser.config.ts packages/vue-clamp/tests/text-layout.browser.test.ts -t "affix"`
  passes the helper regression for the near-boundary verification control flow.
- `vp test -c vite.browser.config.ts packages/vue-clamp/tests/demo-page.browser.test.ts -t "narrow edge"`
  passed 10/10 runs with the full verification fallback and 5/5 runs after narrowing the fallback to
  the near-boundary band.

Focused smoke A/B for the guard used the same current worktree, first with the LineClamp
`verifyOverflow` marker removed (`/tmp/vue-clamp-affix-overflow-before-smoke.log`), then with the
retained near-boundary marker (`/tmp/vue-clamp-affix-overflow-after-smoke.log`). This is a
correctness guard with a measured structural cost:

| Scenario                          | Pre-guard rect reads | Retained rect reads | Active time / RME                         |
| --------------------------------- | -------------------: | ------------------: | ----------------------------------------- |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-jumps`      |                  `0` |               `896` | `100.5 -> 91.1 ms`, RME `28.5% -> 1.6%`   |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous` |                  `0` |              `2370` | `355.3 -> 323.1 ms`, RME `47.2% -> 48.4%` |

The active-time deltas are not an optimization claim because the pre-guard timing is low-confidence
and the retained path adds exact rect work. The useful conclusion is narrower: the broad
"always verify affix overflow" variant read `1344` rect lists in `line-cta-affix-batch-jumps`,
whereas the retained near-boundary band reads `896`, so the final guard preserves the correctness
fix while avoiding some far-overflow exact counting. Build size for the retained smoke was
`119.08 kB` / `25.37 kB` gzip.

### Line affix overflow-height cache

Follow-up diagnostics on `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter` showed that the retained near-boundary guard
was still paying exact rect-list reads only to reject overflow candidates:

- `fitHeightVerifyRectCalls`: `5101`
- `fitHeightVerifyRejectCalls`: `5101`
- `fitHeightVerifyFitCalls`: `0`
- reject height buckets: one bucket, `79px`

The retained optimization caches the minimum exact-rejected content height per `SimpleLineFit` and
line limit. Later candidates at that height or above can reject from `getBoundingClientRect().height`
without another `getClientRects()` pass. The cache is invalidated whenever exact rects increase the
known single-line box height, which keeps the earlier near-boundary fit guard intact.

Same-machine six-run A/B toggled only this fast reject. Logs:
`/tmp/vue-clamp-line-affix-overflow-cache-ab-before.log` and
`/tmp/vue-clamp-line-affix-overflow-cache-ab-after.log`.

| Metric               |           Before |            After |
| -------------------- | ---------------: | ---------------: |
| `clientRectReads`    |           `5101` |              `0` |
| `clientRectEntries`  |          `20404` |              `0` |
| `medianActiveMs`     |          `630.0` |         `621.45` |
| `sampleMeanActiveMs` | `625.30 ± 12.14` | `619.52 ± 16.59` |

The active-time intervals overlap, so this is not a proved timing win. The retained claim is
structural: the row's repeated rect-list verification work is removed without a measured timing
regression.

A broader smoke A/B toggled the same fast reject across LineClamp affix rows. Logs:
`/tmp/vue-clamp-line-affix-overflow-cache-broader-before.log` and
`/tmp/vue-clamp-line-affix-overflow-cache-broader-after.log`.

| Scenario                              | `clientRectReads` | `clientRectEntries` |
| ------------------------------------- | ----------------: | ------------------: |
| `line-title-single-affix-batch-sweep` |          `0 -> 0` |            `0 -> 0` |
| `line-prefixed-summary-batch-jumps`   |          `0 -> 0` |            `0 -> 0` |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous`     |      `2370 -> 16` |        `9480 -> 64` |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-novel-jitter`   |        `660 -> 0` |         `2640 -> 0` |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-jumps`          |       `896 -> 16` |        `3584 -> 64` |

This narrows the effect: it helps CTA after-affix rows where `verifyOverflow` is the rect-list
source, and it leaves affix rows that already avoided that path unchanged.

## Rich metadata forward text-prefix patch

After the Line affix round, the next focused Rich baseline was
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-next-round-baseline-smoke.log`. The remaining metadata-affix rows showed no
style-read hotspot; their costs were rect-list reads plus DOM churn:

| Scenario                                 | Structural shape                                                                              |
| ---------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`       | bbox `9280`, rects `7616 / 18964`, mutations `18464`, child-list `4768`, added/removed `3120` |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-novel-jitter` | bbox `2720`, rects `3312 / 8512`, mutations `10544`, child-list `7104`, added/removed `4944`  |

Temporary branch diagnostics showed that existing fast paths were already doing useful work, but
generic root-level patches remained high. Logs:
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-patch-branch-diagnostic-smoke.log`,
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-patch-generic-diagnostic-smoke.log`, and
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-patch-anchor-diagnostic-smoke.log`.

| Scenario                                 | Same-text cuts | Generic patches | Main generic source                                               |
| ---------------------------------------- | -------------: | --------------: | ----------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`       |         `6560` |          `1232` | probe clamped-to-clamped `720`, visible clamped-to-clamped `272`  |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-novel-jitter` |         `1296` |          `2000` | probe clamped-to-clamped `1424`, visible clamped-to-clamped `352` |

All generic patches used the rich body root as the anchor. The retained path handles a narrower
forward-grow case: when the previous clamped point cuts through the middle of a source text node and
the next point is after that text node's whole-prefix boundary, the patcher restores the existing
live text node to the full source text and appends only the newly visible suffix. It preserves the
existing prefix wrapper and root ellipsis instead of deleting and recreating that prefix.

Same-process six-run A/B toggled only this path. Logs:
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-forward-text-prefix-ab-before.log`,
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-forward-text-prefix-ab-after.log`,
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-forward-text-prefix-reverse-after.log`, and
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-forward-text-prefix-reverse-before.log`.

| Scenario                                 | Child-list records | Added/removed nodes | Character-data records | Active timing                                            |
| ---------------------------------------- | -----------------: | ------------------: | ---------------------: | -------------------------------------------------------- |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`       |     `4768 -> 4368` |      `3120 -> 2720` |         `6272 -> 6672` | `545.6 -> 541.0 ms`, MOE overlaps                        |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-novel-jitter` |     `7104 -> 6400` |      `4944 -> 4240` |         `1264 -> 2000` | mixed: first order slower, reverse order flat within MOE |

This is retained as a structural DOM-churn optimization only. It trades some text-node data updates
for fewer child-list mutations and fewer node allocations/removals. It does not change layout reads
or prove an active-time win.

## Rejected Rich simple-line disable experiment

After the CSS-variable InlineClamp correctness pass, the next Rich hotspot audit revisited
`rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`, whose current retained shape still has high style reads from
per-width rich layout reinspection. A temporary experiment disabled RichLineClamp's cached
simple-line height fit so rich probes would stop re-reading computed styles for transparent inline
wrappers. Focused smoke log: `/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-no-simple-line-smoke.log`.

The experiment confirmed the trade-off but did not improve the retained workload:

| Scenario                                      | Style reads   | Client rect reads / entries   | Active time / RME                      |
| --------------------------------------------- | ------------- | ----------------------------- | -------------------------------------- |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`                 | `3840 -> 0`   | `0 / 0 -> 5200 / 23488`       | `489.9 -> 431.1 ms`, after RME `46.2%` |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`   | `8496 -> 128` | `272 / 9408 -> 2768 / 76080`  | `236.7 -> 241.1 ms`, after RME `6.0%`  |
| `rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` | `6880 -> 0`   | `480 / 15408 -> 3536 / 84048` | `190.3 -> 205.0 ms`, after RME `3.2%`  |

The `rich-word-copy` timing movement is unusable because the after-run RME was high. The low-noise
long-token rows show the important structural result: dropping the style reinspection removes style
reads but forces far more rect-list allocation and line grouping. The experiment was reverted.
RichLineClamp should keep the simple-line path until a stricter invalidation signal can avoid
repeated style reads without falling back to full rect lists.

## Current CJK and novel-width guard smoke

A current-only smoke over the CJK and novel-width guard rows confirms that those rows are coverage,
not the next dominant optimization target. Log:
`/tmp/vue-clamp-current-cjk-novel-guard-smoke.log`.

| Scenario                            | Structural shape                                                     | Active time / RME      |
| ----------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------- |
| `line-word-cjk-batch-jitter`        | bbox `2512`, style reads `512`, mutations `2208`, child-list `160`   | `82.5 ms`, RME `5.5%`  |
| `line-word-cjk-batch-novel-jitter`  | bbox `2176`, style reads `544`, mutations `1632`, child-list `0`     | `77.2 ms`, RME `8.4%`  |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-novel-jitter` | bbox `3872`, style reads `1088`, mutations `8640`, child-list `5328` | `155.9 ms`, RME `7.4%` |
| `rich-word-cjk-batch-jitter`        | bbox `2256`, style reads `1408`, mutations `3296`, child-list `1072` | `88.9 ms`, RME `13.6%` |
| `rich-word-cjk-batch-novel-jitter`  | bbox `2176`, style reads `2176`, mutations `2176`, child-list `0`    | `99.3 ms`, RME `16.1%` |

The useful reading is structural. CJK novel rows have no child-list churn, and the remaining Rich
cost is mostly width-step layout/style validation. That validation is intentionally conservative:
container queries, external CSS, font changes, or class-driven display changes can make an inline
wrapper atomic or change simple-line metrics without changing the trusted HTML source. Without a
stricter invalidation signal, caching those style reads would be a correctness trade rather than a
proved optimization.

## Rich patch-path diagnostic

A temporary non-retained diagnostic counted which `patchRich` path handled candidate transitions in
the current Rich hotspots. Logs:
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-word-copy-patch-debug.log` and
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-long-token-patch-debug.log`.

Per measured run, `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter` produced:

| Patch path                    | Count |
| ----------------------------- | ----: |
| same-state clamped -> clamped |  3616 |
| same-text clamped -> clamped  |  2480 |
| generic clamped -> clamped    |  2720 |
| generic clamped -> full       |   112 |
| generic full -> clamped       |   112 |

The long-token rows had a different shape:

| Scenario                                      | Generic c->c | Backward prefix c->c | Forward prefix c->c | Same-state c->c | Full transitions |
| --------------------------------------------- | -----------: | -------------------: | ------------------: | --------------: | ---------------: |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`   |          752 |                 1520 |                 736 |             720 |        `64 + 64` |
| `rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` |          656 |                 1680 |                1376 |             784 |              `0` |

This narrows the remaining Rich opportunity. The cheap same-state and same-text paths are already
heavily used, and the retained whole-prefix grow/shrink paths handle most long-token transitions.
The still-expensive part is generic clamped-to-clamped movement across rich wrapper or text-node
boundaries. A prior partial-text patch experiment already showed that adding more local text-node
updates does not materially reduce long-token child-list churn. The next credible Rich optimization
would need a different representation for hidden-probe suffixes or a stronger structural patch that
keeps wrapper chains stable across cross-node boundaries; small extra `Text.data` patches are not
enough evidence-wise.

## Retained Rich same-node whitespace patch

One small structural patch improvement was still available inside the already-proven same-text
patch path. Before this change, clamped-to-clamped movement inside the same source `Text` node fell
back to generic subtree replacement whenever the target cut ended after whitespace, because the
generic rich render trims trailing whitespace before appending the root ellipsis. The retained patch
applies that same trimming directly to the live text node, preserving the wrapper/text/ellipsis
nodes and avoiding the child-list replacement.

Same-process package A/B used fresh before/after tarballs in one browser run. Log:
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-trimmed-same-text-ab-report.log`. Package size was neutral to slightly lower in
this build (`dist/index.js` `119.17 -> 119.16 kB`, gzip `25.40 -> 25.39 kB`). Timing is not claimed
because several rows have noisy active-time samples; the proof is structural:

| Scenario                                      |                   Mutations |                Child-list |   Text records |                Added/removed |
| --------------------------------------------- | --------------------------: | ------------------------: | -------------: | ---------------------------: |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jumps`                  |   `7728 -> 5424` (`-29.8%`) | `5664 -> 2592` (`-54.2%`) |  `912 -> 1680` |     `2976/2976 -> 1440/1440` |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`                 | `21824 -> 13664` (`-37.4%`) | `11664 -> 784` (`-93.3%`) | `2480 -> 5200` |       `5888/5888 -> 448/448` |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-novel-jitter`           |   `8640 -> 5376` (`-37.8%`) |  `5328 -> 976` (`-81.7%`) | `1136 -> 2224` |       `2720/2720 -> 544/544` |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`   |   `19250 -> 19250` (`0.0%`) | `18256 -> 18256` (`0.0%`) |       `0 -> 0` | `15296/15296 -> 15296/15296` |
| `rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` |   `17904 -> 17904` (`0.0%`) | `16944 -> 16944` (`0.0%`) |       `0 -> 0` | `14176/14176 -> 14176/14176` |

Across the five focused rows, total mutation records moved `75346 -> 61618` (`-18.2%`),
child-list records `57856 -> 39552` (`-31.6%`), and added/removed nodes both
`41056 -> 31904` (`-22.3%`). Character-data records increased (`4528 -> 9104`) because subtree
replacement became direct `Text.data` mutation. Bounding-rect reads, client-rect reads/entries, and
style reads were unchanged, which is expected: this patch changes DOM mutation shape, not search
probe count or layout validation.

The browser regression `preserves rich text nodes when reclamping to a same-node whitespace cut`
checks the exact invariant: output remains `alpha…`, and the live wrapper, text node, and root
ellipsis node are preserved when the next cut lands after a trailing space.

## Retained Rich same-node equal-write guard

The retained same-text patch opened one smaller follow-up optimization: when a word-boundary cut
moves from the end of a word to the following whitespace, trailing-whitespace trimming can make the
visible text identical. Reassigning `Text.data` in that case does not change output but can still
emit a `characterData` mutation. The retained guard skips the assignment when the live text already
matches the trimmed target.

Focused current-run evidence used `/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-same-text-equal-write-guard-report.log`,
compared against the earlier retained same-node whitespace A/B counters. Layout/search counters
were unchanged; only text mutation records moved:

| Scenario                            | Mutation records           | Character-data records    |
| ----------------------------------- | -------------------------- | ------------------------- |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jumps`        | `5424 -> 5328` (`-1.8%`)   | `1680 -> 1584` (`-5.7%`)  |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`       | `13664 -> 13184` (`-3.5%`) | `5200 -> 4720` (`-9.2%`)  |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-novel-jitter` | `5376 -> 5088` (`-5.4%`)   | `2224 -> 1936` (`-12.9%`) |
