Across those three rows, mutation records moved `24464 -> 23600` (`-3.5%`) and character-data
records `9104 -> 8240` (`-9.5%`). Child-list, added/removed node, bounding-rect, client-rect, and
style-read counters stayed unchanged. Active time is not claimed because the run had visible sample
noise unrelated to this small mutation-only change. The browser regression now also observes the
same reclamp with a `MutationObserver` and expects zero mutation records when the trimmed text is
unchanged.

## Retained Rich generic ellipsis reuse

After the same-text patch improvements, the next Rich mutation hotspot was generic
clamped-to-clamped patching across source nodes. The generic path still removed the root-level
ellipsis before rebuilding the source suffix and then appended a new ellipsis, even though that
ellipsis is not part of the source tree. The retained patch reuses the existing root ellipsis and,
when the patch anchor is the rich body root, inserts the rebuilt source fragment before it.

Same-process package A/B used fresh tarballs:
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-generic-ellipsis-before.tgz` and
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-generic-ellipsis-after.tgz`; log
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-generic-ellipsis-ab-report.log`. Package size grew from
`119.19 kB / gzip 25.40 kB` to `119.47 kB / gzip 25.41 kB`. The retained benefit is structural:
layout/search counters were unchanged in every row.

| Scenario                                  | Mutation records           | Child-list records        | Added/removed nodes      |
| ----------------------------------------- | -------------------------- | ------------------------- | ------------------------ |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`        | `20032 -> 18368` (`-8.3%`) | `6160 -> 4496` (`-27.0%`) | `3696/3696 -> 2864/2864` |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jumps`              | `5328 -> 4176` (`-21.6%`)  | `2592 -> 1440` (`-44.4%`) | `1440/1440 -> 864/864`   |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`             | `13184 -> 13184` (`0.0%`)  | `784 -> 784` (`0.0%`)     | `448/448 -> 448/448`     |
| `rich-word-long-token-lines5-batch-jumps` | `7568 -> 6576` (`-13.1%`)  | `5648 -> 4656` (`-17.6%`) | `3728/3728 -> 3232/3232` |
| `rich-height-affix-card-batch-jumps`      | `10032 -> 8976` (`-10.5%`) | `7536 -> 6480` (`-14.0%`) | `5280/5280 -> 4752/4752` |

Across those five rows, mutation records moved `56144 -> 51280` (`-8.7%`), child-list records
`22720 -> 17856` (`-21.4%`), and added/removed nodes both `14592 -> 12160` (`-16.7%`). Active time
is not claimed for the full set because `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter` had high RME and moved
in the wrong direction in that noisy run. The low-noise rows were consistent with the structural
change but small: `rich-word-long-token-lines5-batch-jumps` moved `139.2 -> 138.9 ms`
(`2.0% / 1.5%` RME), and `rich-height-affix-card-batch-jumps` moved `85.9 -> 85.4 ms`
(`2.3% / 2.3%` RME).

The browser regression `preserves the rich root ellipsis across generic clamped patches` covers a
cross-node patch from `<span>al</span>…` to `<span>alpha</span> <span>be</span>…` and asserts that
the root ellipsis node identity is preserved.

## Retained Rich root-space prefix patch

The next retained Rich patch keeps complete wrapper prefixes stable when a clamped logical boundary
ends at a root-level whitespace text node or root-level `wbr` that the renderer trims before the
root ellipsis. This matters for long-token rich HTML such as
`<span>token1</span> <span>token2</span>`: the word boundary can land at the end of the root space,
but the rendered clamped DOM is `<span>token1</span>…`. The whole-prefix fast path previously
rejected that state because the source boundary included the space while the live DOM did not, so
later growth or shrinkage fell back to generic subtree rebuilding.

The retained rule normalizes only that root-level trimmed suffix. For a grow, the live prefix is
matched before the trimmed root child, and the cloned source suffix starts from that same rendered
boundary so the space is restored before later content. For a shrink, the suffix is removed after
the rendered boundary while the existing root ellipsis can stay in place. This deliberately does
not revive the broader partial-text patch experiment: trailing whitespace inside a text node still
uses the generic path unless the same-node fast path can handle it safely.

Same-process package A/B used a fresh before tarball and the final guarded current build:
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rootspace-before.tgz` and `current`; log
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rootspace-guard-ab-report.log`. Package size moved from
`119.24 kB / gzip 25.39 kB` to `120.30 kB / gzip 25.55 kB` after adding the safety guard that
refuses to reuse a clamped prefix when the normalized root-space boundary would hide whitespace
trimmed inside the previous source leaf. Layout/search counters were unchanged in every row; the
retained benefit is reduced DOM node churn in root-space rich rows, primarily long-token inputs.

| Scenario                                      | Mutation records           | Child-list records         | Added/removed nodes          | Active time / RME                       |
| --------------------------------------------- | -------------------------- | -------------------------- | ---------------------------- | --------------------------------------- |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`            | `18368 -> 18464` (`+0.5%`) | `4496 -> 4768` (`+6.0%`)   | `2864/2864 -> 3120/3120`     | `517.7 -> 521.9 ms`, RME `4.4% / 14.1%` |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`                 | `13184 -> 13184` (`0.0%`)  | `784 -> 784` (`0.0%`)      | `448/448 -> 448/448`         | `491.7 -> 482.1 ms`, RME `11.9% / 5.1%` |
| `rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps`            | `5952 -> 4960` (`-16.7%`)  | `4032 -> 3040` (`-24.6%`)  | `2768/2768 -> 2272/2272`     | `94.0 -> 96.8 ms`, RME `4.8% / 7.8%`    |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`   | `17746 -> 16114` (`-9.2%`) | `16752 -> 15120` (`-9.7%`) | `14544/14544 -> 13728/13728` | `238.7 -> 237.5 ms`, RME `2.7% / 1.5%`  |
| `rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` | `16592 -> 15792` (`-4.8%`) | `15632 -> 14832` (`-5.1%`) | `13520/13520 -> 13120/13120` | `192.8 -> 193.5 ms`, RME `3.5% / 0.6%`  |
| `rich-word-long-token-lines5-batch-jumps`     | `6576 -> 5616` (`-14.6%`)  | `4656 -> 3696` (`-20.6%`)  | `3232/3232 -> 2752/2752`     | `141.3 -> 139.8 ms`, RME `2.1% / 3.6%`  |

Across all six focused rows, mutation records moved `78418 -> 74130` (`-5.5%`), child-list records
`46352 -> 42240` (`-8.9%`), and added/removed nodes both `37376 -> 35440` (`-5.2%`). The ordinary
word-copy row was unchanged. The metadata-affix row now shows the correctness guard's local cost:
some prefixes that looked reusable before are rebuilt because their source prefix is not
byte-for-byte present in the clamped DOM. Across the four affected long-token rows only, mutation
records moved `46866 -> 42482` (`-9.4%`), child-list records `41072 -> 36688` (`-10.7%`), and
added/removed nodes both `34064 -> 31872` (`-6.4%`).

Active time is not the primary proof. The simple long-token row moved clearly in the right
direction with low RME, but the font-size and tight-font rows were essentially neutral while
structural counters improved. The retained claim is therefore structural workload reduction for
root-space rich inputs, strongest on long-token rows, at a measured package cost of about
`+1.06 kB` raw and `+0.16 kB` gzip against the immediate before package.

Browser regressions `preserves complete rich prefix nodes when growing from a trimmed root space`
and `preserves complete rich prefix nodes when shrinking to a trimmed root space` cover the exact
identity invariant: `<span>alpha</span> <span>beta</span>` can grow from the trimmed root-space
boundary to `alpha beta…` and shrink back to `alpha…` while preserving the first wrapper and root
ellipsis. The regression
`rebuilds rich content when a trimmed root space hides inner prefix whitespace` covers the safety
guard: `<span>alpha </span> <span>beta</span>` may initially clamp to `alpha…`, but growing to full
must restore `<span>alpha </span> <span>beta</span>` rather than preserving the trimmed
`<span>alpha</span>` prefix.

## Rejected precise Rich trimmed-prefix restore point

A follow-up tried to reduce the safety guard's local metadata-affix cost by returning the exact
boundary before the leaf that `trimTrailingWhitespace` had modified, instead of making generic
patching rebuild from the rich root. Log: `/tmp/vue-clamp-rootspace-restorepoint-ab-report.log`.

The focused six-row structure returned to the earlier best root-space shape: totals moved
`78418 -> 73890` mutation records, `46352 -> 42000` child-list records, and
`37376 -> 35200` added/removed nodes. Compared with the simpler guarded version, that only recovers
`240` mutation records, `240` child-list records, and `240` added/removed nodes across the focused
matrix, mainly by changing `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter` from the guard's
`18464 / 4768 / 3120` shape to `18224 / 4528 / 2880`.

The cost was not worth retaining: package size rose from the simple guard's
`120.30 kB / gzip 25.55 kB` to `121.05 kB / gzip 25.72 kB`, and the helper code became more complex.
The experiment was reverted; the retained rule stays deliberately simple and correctness-first:
if the clamped prefix is not byte-for-byte present in live DOM, generic patching starts from the
root.

## Rejected Rich simple-line full-disable follow-up

The remaining Rich word scenarios still show non-trivial `styleReads`, especially long-token rows.
A temporary experiment disabled `simpleLineFit` publication so Rich always used exact rect-list line
counting instead of revalidating the simple-line layout. Logs:
`/tmp/vue-clamp-current-rich-diagnostic.log` and
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-disable-simple-line-experiment.log`.

This is not a valid general optimization. It removes style reads but replaces them with many
rect-list reads and rect entries:

| Scenario                                  | Current retained path                        | Simple-line disabled                             |
| ----------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------ |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jumps`              | style `576`, rects `0/0`, active `63.1 ms`   | style `0`, rects `1824/10176`, active `69.8 ms`  |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`             | style `3840`, rects `0/0`, active `301.6 ms` | style `0`, rects `5200/23488`, active `418.4 ms` |
| `rich-word-long-token-lines5-batch-jumps` | style `7840`, rects `0/0`, active `142.3 ms` | style `0`, rects `2288/61248`, active `140.3 ms` |

The long-token row is the only one with a small active-time improvement, but the structural trade is
not a clear workload reduction: it trades style reads for thousands of rect-list reads and 61k rect
entries, while ordinary Rich copy rows regress sharply. A future dynamic strategy would need a real
cost model for `styleReads` versus rect-list reads/entries and must preserve the correctness guard
that rechecks child metrics and atomic inline wrappers when CSS changes. The one-line disable was
reverted.

## Rejected shared text equal-write guard

A follow-up tried the same equal-write idea in the shared `setElementText` helper used by
LineClamp/InlineClamp candidate patches: skip `Text.data` assignment when the sole live text node
already equals the requested text. The direct behavior is true, but it did not hit the measured hot
paths. Same-process package A/B used fresh tarballs:
`/tmp/vue-clamp-set-element-text-guard-before.tgz` and
`/tmp/vue-clamp-set-element-text-guard-after.tgz`; log
`/tmp/vue-clamp-set-element-text-guard-ab-report.log`.

The four focused Line/Inline rows had identical structural counters before and after:

| Scenario                          | Mutation records | Character-data records | Layout reads |
| --------------------------------- | ---------------- | ---------------------- | ------------ |
| `line-word-copy-batch-jumps`      | `3648 -> 3648`   | `1344 -> 1344`         | unchanged    |
| `line-word-copy-batch-jitter`     | `11536 -> 11536` | `4272 -> 4272`         | unchanged    |
| `inline-path-middle-batch-jitter` | `11164 -> 11164` | `4327 -> 4327`         | unchanged    |
| `inline-word-copy-batch-jumps`    | `2720 -> 2720`   | `1584 -> 1584`         | unchanged    |

The package grew from `119.19 kB / gzip 25.40 kB` to `119.25 kB / gzip 25.41 kB`, and the timing
differences were inside active-time RME. The guard was reverted; the current measured Line/Inline
hot paths do not spend work on same-value text writes at this helper boundary.

## Rejected Rich hinted-run disable experiment

A temporary smoke disabled `preferHintedTextRun` to test whether the hinted text-run refinement was
overfitting the current benchmark widths. Log: `/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-no-hinted-run-smoke.log`.

The result was structurally worse in every covered Rich scenario:

| Scenario                                      | Retained workload                                  | Disabled workload                                  |
| --------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------- |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`            | bbox `9280`, rects `7616/18964`, mutations `22960` | bbox `9280`, rects `9424/25748`, mutations `37728` |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`                 | bbox `10960`, rects `0/0`, mutations `21824`       | bbox `12880`, rects `0/0`, mutations `39104`       |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`   | bbox `4096`, rects `272/9408`, mutations `22130`   | bbox `4432`, rects `272/13344`, mutations `31138`  |
| `rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` | bbox `4496`, rects `480/15408`, mutations `23216`  | bbox `4800`, rects `480/23600`, mutations `29504`  |

The disabled run had low active-time RME (`1.2-2.7%`) and still failed structurally: it created far
more DOM churn and more rect entries. This means the hinted-run path is not just a benchmark
shortcut for repeated widths; it prevents cross-run candidate jumps from falling back to broader
subtree replacement. The experiment was reverted. Future work should keep hinted-run refinement and
look below it, at preserving wrapper chains across the remaining generic clamped-to-clamped patches.

## Rejected Rich rank-map experiment

A small Rich word-boundary experiment replaced the linear `rankForState` scan over rank points with
a cached `Map<BoundaryPoint, rank>` on the search index. This reduced theoretical JS lookup work but
did not change browser-visible layout reads or DOM mutation counts. Same-process package A/B used
fresh before/after tarballs in one browser run. Log:
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-rank-map-ab-report.log`.

The experiment added package size (`dist/index.js` `119.17 -> 119.28 kB`, gzip
`25.40 -> 25.44 kB`) and did not produce a consistent low-noise timing win:

| Scenario                                      |     Before |      After |   Delta | Active RME before/after |
| --------------------------------------------- | ---------: | ---------: | ------: | ----------------------: |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`                 | `510.5 ms` | `504.9 ms` | `-1.1%` |           `4.6% / 9.7%` |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-novel-jitter`           | `158.0 ms` | `153.1 ms` | `-3.1%` |           `5.8% / 7.3%` |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`   | `241.5 ms` | `238.4 ms` | `-1.3%` |           `2.1% / 2.0%` |
| `rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` | `197.5 ms` | `198.7 ms` | `+0.6%` |           `2.7% / 1.8%` |

Totals moved `1107.5 -> 1095.1 ms` (`-1.1%`), but every structural counter was identical and one
low-noise long-token row moved backward. The Map version was reverted. This is not strong enough to
justify extra bytes and memory; rank lookup is not a current proved hotspot compared with DOM patch
shape and layout/style validation.

## Rejected Rich pass-local fit cache experiment

A second Rich experiment cached `fitsContent` results for identical `BoundaryPoint` objects inside a
single `clampRich` pass. The cache still patched the probe DOM to the candidate before returning a
cached fit, so it preserved search state; the intended win was skipping repeated layout reads when a
hinted text-run refinement had already measured the same coarse point. Log:
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-fit-cache-ab-report.log`.

Same-process package A/B rejected it. The cache added package size (`dist/index.js`
`119.17 -> 119.49 kB`, gzip `25.40 -> 25.47 kB`) and did not reduce any structural counter in the
covered Rich word scenarios:

| Scenario                                      |     Before |      After |   Delta | Active RME before/after | Structure |
| --------------------------------------------- | ---------: | ---------: | ------: | ----------------------: | --------- |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`                 | `503.8 ms` | `521.5 ms` | `+3.5%` |           `5.1% / 9.0%` | same      |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-novel-jitter`           | `155.7 ms` | `148.6 ms` | `-4.6%` |           `1.7% / 8.5%` | same      |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`   | `239.9 ms` | `240.4 ms` | `+0.2%` |           `2.3% / 1.1%` | same      |
| `rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` | `191.3 ms` | `195.4 ms` | `+2.1%` |           `1.9% / 1.1%` | same      |

Totals moved `1090.7 -> 1105.9 ms` (`+1.4%`). Because bbox reads, client-rect reads/entries, style
reads, and mutation records were identical, the cache did not remove browser work in this matrix.
It was reverted. The current hinted-run/coarse-search flow is not paying a measurable repeated-fit
tax for identical boundary-point objects; remaining Rich work is still in structural patch shape and
layout/style validation.

## Affix novel-width hotspot guard rows

The latest report views made it clear that the highest Line/Rich rows still include affix-heavy
hotspots: `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter` and `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`. The existing
large-novel coverage guarded word-boundary, CJK, and long-token shapes, but not these slot-heavy
affix paths. Two rows were added for that input-space hole:
`line-cta-affix-batch-novel-jitter` and `rich-metadata-affix-batch-novel-jitter`.

Both rows keep the same public component shapes as their existing affix jitter rows, but every width
is fresh inside the row. The Line sequence has 35 unique widths, 22 transitions wider than 32px, and
a max delta of `78px`. The Rich sequence has 35 unique widths, 20 transitions wider than 32px, and a
max delta of `70px`. This means the rows exercise affix-heavy paths under fresh large width jumps
instead of mostly revisiting a small width set.

Current targeted smoke log: `/tmp/vue-clamp-affix-novel-jitter-smoke.log`.

| Scenario                                 | Structural shape                                                                                          | Active time / RME       |
| ---------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------- |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-novel-jitter`      | bbox `4816`, client rects `660 / 2640`, mutations `3995`, child-list `352`, style reads `672`             | `129.1 ms`, RME `11.7%` |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-novel-jitter` | bbox `2720`, client rects `3312 / 8512`, mutations `10544`, child-list `7104`, added/removed nodes `4944` | `162.2 ms`, RME `7.2%`  |

The active-time RME is above the low-noise threshold for both rows, so the timing values are not a
performance claim. The retained value is benchmark coverage: future affix-path optimizations now
have a fresh-width, large-jump guard alongside the existing repeated/jitter hotspot rows.

## Width-profile benchmark metadata

The package benchmark harness now attaches a scenario-level width profile to both full benchmark
payloads and compact `PACKAGE_MATRIX_SUMMARY` payloads. The renderer exposes the same metadata in a
`Width profile matrix` section when logs contain it. Historical logs without the field still render;
their JSON rows use `widthProfile: null` and the Markdown table is omitted.

The profile is computed from the actual measured width writes, including writes inside a
`widthBursts` step. It records stable step count, total width assignments, unique width count,
repeated assignments/transitions, the large-delta threshold, transitions wider than that threshold,
and the maximum adjacent width delta. This directly exposes whether a row is mostly revisiting old
widths or exercising fresh width inputs, which is required when interpreting warm-start and
threshold optimizations. The threshold is stored in the payload rather than only in the renderer, so
future changes to the large-delta definition do not make old logs display a misleading table label.

Validation log: `/tmp/vue-clamp-affix-novel-jitter-width-profile-smoke.log`.
Rendered smoke report: `/tmp/vue-clamp-width-profile-report/310-package-benchmark-matrix.md`.

| Scenario                                 | Width assignments | Unique widths | Repeated transitions | Large-delta threshold | Large deltas | Max delta |
| ---------------------------------------- | ----------------- | ------------- | -------------------- | --------------------- | ------------ | --------- |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-novel-jitter`      | `35`              | `35`          | `0`                  | `32px`                | `22`         | `78px`    |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-novel-jitter` | `35`              | `35`          | `0`                  | `32px`                | `20`         | `70px`    |

This is not a new performance claim. It is a report-quality guardrail: future benchmark
comparisons can no longer hide repeated-width bias in raw fixture definitions.

## Rich full-to-clamped prefix patch

A fresh Rich patch diagnostic reopened the remaining generic patch family after the retained
same-text, root-ellipsis, root-space, and forward text-prefix paths. The high-value rect-list
hotspot remained `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`, but the only small uncovered structural family
with a simple correctness proof was `full -> clamped`: when the probe or visible DOM currently
contains the full source tree, a later clamped candidate can trim that live tree in place instead of
removing the prefix and cloning it back from the prepared source.

Temporary diagnostic smoke over
`rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`, `rich-metadata-affix-batch-novel-jitter`,
`rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`, and `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` showed the
pre-change generic `full -> clamped` counts:

| Scenario                                    | Generic `full -> clamped` |
| ------------------------------------------- | ------------------------: |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`          |                     `144` |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-novel-jitter`    |                      `32` |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`               |                     `112` |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` |                       `0` |

The retained patch handles only that transition. Text cuts update the live text prefix, remove
following source siblings, trim trailing whitespace exactly like generic clamped output, and append
the root ellipsis. Non-text structural boundaries remove the live suffix from the boundary and use
the same trailing trim. A browser regression checks that clamping from full
`<span>alpha</span> <span>beta</span> <span>gamma</span>` to a cut inside `beta` keeps the existing
`alpha` span, root space, `beta` span, and beta text node identities.

Clean smoke after removing diagnostics kept layout/search counters unchanged and moved only DOM
mutation shape:

| Scenario                                    |        Mutations |       Child-list | Character-data |                Added/removed |
| ------------------------------------------- | ---------------: | ---------------: | -------------: | ---------------------------: |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`          | `18464 -> 18320` |   `4368 -> 4080` | `6672 -> 6816` |     `2720/2720 -> 2576/2576` |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-novel-jitter`    | `10544 -> 10544` |   `6368 -> 6368` | `2000 -> 2000` |     `4208/4208 -> 4208/4208` |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`               | `13184 -> 13072` |     `672 -> 448` | `4832 -> 4944` |         `336/336 -> 224/224` |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` | `16114 -> 16114` | `15120 -> 15120` |       `0 -> 0` | `13728/13728 -> 13728/13728` |

Across those rows, mutation records moved `58306 -> 58050` (`-0.4%`), child-list records
`26528 -> 26016` (`-1.9%`), and added/removed nodes both `20992 -> 20736` (`-1.2%`). Active time
is not claimed; the benefit is the deterministic reduction in subtree churn for a clear patch
invariant. Focused Rich browser tests and `vp check --fix` passed, and `git diff --check` was clean.

## Rich suffix range deletion rejection

A follow-up diagnostic asked whether the remaining long-token child-list hotspot was caused by an
uncovered generic patch family. It was not. Temporary patch counters showed that
`rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` and
`rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` were dominated by already-retained whole-prefix
patches:

| Scenario                                      | Forward whole clamped-to-clamped | Backward whole clamped-to-clamped | Same-state clamped-to-clamped |
| --------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------: | --------------------------------: | ----------------------------: |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`   |                           `1488` |                            `1520` |                         `720` |
| `rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` |                           `2032` |                            `1680` |                         `784` |

That pointed to the suffix-removal helper rather than to a missing patch strategy. A trial replaced
the helper's per-child removal loop with a single `Range.deleteContents()` over the suffix. Browser
smoke showed no structural improvement: every tracked counter stayed byte-for-byte unchanged,
including long-token child-list records (`15120` and `14832`) and added/removed nodes (`13728` and
`13120`). Active time moved worse in the same run (`240.6 -> 272.9 ms` for the font-size row and
`191.2 -> 249.4 ms` for the tight-font row), so the trial was reverted.

The useful conclusion is that current Chromium/MutationObserver accounting still exposes these
suffix deletions at node granularity for our workload. Reducing the long-token child-list hotspot
would require changing how much DOM is materialized or removed, not just batching removal calls.
The previously rejected hidden-suffix strategy remains out of scope until a separate diagnostic
proves that visibility/attribute churn is lower than child-list churn.

## Rich metadata full-verification scope check

A later fit-source diagnostic tested whether the remaining Rich metadata-affix rect-list hotspot was
mostly caused by the safety guard that verifies the bare full candidate after skipped full-fit
passes. It was not. Temporary counters over the two metadata-affix rows showed:

| Scenario                                 | Client rect reads | Clamped candidate fits | Full-candidate fits | Guard-triggered full verifications |
| ---------------------------------------- | ----------------: | ---------------------: | ------------------: | ---------------------------------: |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`       |            `7616` |                 `7472` |               `144` |                              `144` |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-novel-jitter` |            `3312` |                 `3120` |               `192` |                               `32` |

For the repeated jitter row, the full verification guard accounts for only about `1.9%` of exact
rect-list reads. For the novel-width row, most full-candidate fits are ordinary search/full checks,
not post-search safety verification. The dominant cost is the actual monotonic candidate search:
about `3.9` clamped candidate probes per component-step in the repeated row and `5.7` in the novel
row.

The conclusion is that optimizing the full-candidate guard would add correctness risk and code
complexity for too little structural upside on this hotspot. Future Rich metadata work should focus
on either reducing candidate probes with a stronger search invariant, or changing the exact
line-counting model with a safety predicate that avoids per-candidate bounding-box probes. The
previously rejected affix simple-line expansion and range-delete experiments remain rejected.

## Rich metadata search-path decomposition

A follow-up search-path diagnostic split the remaining metadata-affix rect-list workload by
`clampRich` return path and candidate-fit count. Logs:
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-search-path-diagnostics.log` and
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-search-path-duplicates.log`.

| Scenario                                 |  Calls | Client rect reads | Avg clamped fits | Avg full fits | Dominant paths                                                                         |
| ---------------------------------------- | -----: | ----------------: | ---------------: | ------------: | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`       | `1856` |            `7616` |           `4.03` |        `0.08` | `HintedFineInside` `1840`, `HintedNextAtomicFails` `16`                                |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-novel-jitter` |  `544` |            `3312` |           `5.74` |        `0.35` | `CoarseFine` `304`, `HintedFineInside` `96`, `CoarseNextAtomic` `80`, atomic fail `64` |

The duplicate-candidate diagnostic then counted repeated fits to the same rich boundary point within
a single clamp pass:

| Scenario                                 | Duplicate clamped fits | Share of client rect reads |
| ---------------------------------------- | ---------------------: | -------------------------: |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`       |                    `0` |                     `0.0%` |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-novel-jitter` |                   `64` |                     `1.9%` |

This rejects a small known-fit search-helper optimization for the metadata-affix hotspot. Avoiding
the duplicate fits would remove at most `64` of `3312` exact rect-list reads in the novel row and
nothing in the repeated row, while adding another search API shape. The repeated-width row is almost
entirely warm same-run fine search; the novel-width row is mostly legitimate cold coarse/fine search.

The remaining rect-list workload is therefore close to the current exact-search model's expected
cost. A meaningful next Rich metadata improvement needs a different proof, such as a line-counting
predicate that avoids exact rect lists for safe candidates, or a layout-identity cache that can prove
revisited widths still have the same font/style/affix geometry. Without that identity proof, an
exact-width result cache would mostly optimize repeated-width benchmark rows and could be stale after
same-width font or style changes.

## Rich metadata line-height predicate follow-up

A targeted follow-up rechecked the tempting line-height predicate specifically on the current
metadata-affix hotspot. The temporary diagnostic evaluated, for every exact rect-list candidate, the
simple rule `contentBoundingHeight <= lineHeight * lineLimit + 0.5` and compared it with exact
`getClientRects()` line grouping. Log:
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-line-height-predicate-diagnostics.log`.

| Scenario                                 | Candidates | Exact fits/rejects | Height fits/rejects | Mismatches | BBox reads with diagnostic |
| ---------------------------------------- | ---------: | -----------------: | ------------------: | ---------: | -------------------------: |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`       |     `7616` |      `3968 / 3648` |       `3968 / 3648` |        `0` |            `9280 -> 16896` |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-novel-jitter` |     `3312` |      `1504 / 1808` |       `1504 / 1808` |        `0` |             `2720 -> 6032` |

This proves only that the predicate classifies the current metadata fixtures. It does not overturn
the earlier same-process Rich affix/atomic experiment, which already implemented the retainable
version of this idea by measuring compatible atomic inline boxes and affix wrappers before allowing
height-based line counting. That broader version removed all rect-list reads in the focus set, but
increased bbox reads `27824 -> 62397`, left mutations unchanged, and regressed the low-RME rows
(`rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous`, `rich-word-class-atomic-batch-jumps`, and
`rich-dense-batch-jumps`). The experiment remains rejected.

The narrowed conclusion is that a bbox/line-height predicate is not missing; it is already known to
be a read-type swap that does not pay for Rich affix/atomic content once the safety checks are
included. Future Rich metadata work should not reopen this path unless it can avoid per-candidate or
per-atomic bbox reads, or it introduces a stronger layout identity proof that makes those checks
unnecessary across width-only reclamps.

## Rich first-jump rank-slope rejection

A later Rich word experiment tested whether `rankObserved` could be relaxed for the first large
width jump. The hypothesis was that the initial `rankPerPx` estimate might be enough to decide
whether warm search beats cold search before a different-width resize has been observed.

The baseline focused ten Rich word rows at:

| Counter                     |       Baseline |
| --------------------------- | -------------: |
| BBox reads                  |        `34016` |
| Client rect reads / entries | `4240 / 11200` |
| Mutation records            |        `55138` |
| Child-list records          |        `19760` |

Allowing the first large jump to use the rank model did find local wins:
`rich-word-copy-batch-novel-jitter` moved bbox `3872 -> 3824` and mutations `4832 -> 4768`,
`rich-word-copy-lines1-batch-jumps` moved mutations `4128 -> 4032`,
`rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps` moved bbox `3408 -> 3360` and mutations `4960 -> 4080`, and
`rich-word-long-token-batch-novel-jitter` moved bbox `3712 -> 3632` and mutations
`8480 -> 8352`.

The same run regressed the atomic risk rows more than the local wins saved:
`rich-word-class-atomic-batch-jumps` moved client rect reads `1840 -> 2160`, entries
`4720 -> 6480`, and mutations `5360 -> 7040`; `rich-word-dynamic-atomic-batch-jumps` moved client
rect reads `2400 -> 2912`, entries `6480 -> 8720`, and mutations `5314 -> 6994`. Focused totals
became bbox `33936`, client rect reads / entries `5072 / 15200`, mutations `57330`, and child-list
records `22032`.

Two narrower variants were also rejected. A text-run-only flag and then a `simpleLineFit`-based flag
kept the local wins, but both still allowed the same atomic regressions. The current Rich search
metadata therefore does not contain a reliable enough signal to distinguish "plain text density can
predict the first jump" from "atomic layout will make the unobserved slope misleading."

Conclusion: Rich word warm reuse beyond the fixed pixel window must continue to require an observed
different-width slope. The first-jump opportunity should only be reopened with a stronger
layout-identity or atomic-free proof over the entire candidate space, not with another local rank
flag.

## Inline scrollWidth precision probe

The earlier precision concern was rechecked against the current source. LineClamp, RichLineClamp,
and InlineClamp no longer use `offsetWidth` or `offsetHeight` in clamp decisions. InlineClamp still
uses `scrollWidth` as the one-line fit predicate, while the available width comes from
`getBoundingClientRect().width`.

A temporary browser probe mounted an InlineClamp-like root using the benchmark inline style
(`display:inline-block`, `overflow:hidden`, `white-space:nowrap`, `font:16px Georgia,serif`) and
compared `root.scrollWidth` with the live body span's `getBoundingClientRect().width` for every
prefix candidate of the current path fixture. Across `87` candidates, the rounding delta stayed
within `-0.484375` and `0.5`, and no candidate exceeded the existing `0.5px` fit tolerance in either
direction.

That rejects replacing the Inline fit predicate with a bbox-sum measurement solely for precision.
The current benchmarked one-line shape does not show a precision bug, and a bbox-sum predicate would
add geometry reads to every candidate probe. Reopen only with a browser case whose
`scrollWidth`/actual-width delta exceeds the current tolerance under real InlineClamp styles.

## Rich hidden-suffix mutation probe

The remaining long-token Rich rows still contain high child-list churn, so a hidden-suffix strategy
was isolated before changing `patchRich`. The temporary browser probe built a Rich-like long-token
DOM with a `<strong>` prefix, `28` token spans, and text-node spaces, then replayed `100`
repetitions of the token-count pattern
`[28, 12, 26, 10, 24, 8, 28, 14, 22, 6, 28, 16, 20, 4, 28]`.

It compared current-style suffix removal/reclone with a guarded hidden-suffix variant that sets
token spans to `display:none` and clears suffix text-node spaces:

| Strategy            | Records | Child-list | Attributes | Character-data | Added / removed | Probe active |
| ------------------- | ------: | ---------: | ---------: | -------------: | --------------: | -----------: |
| Remove/clone suffix | `42401` |    `42401` |        `0` |            `0` | `21201 / 21200` |    `15.8 ms` |
| Hidden suffix       | `42401` |        `1` |    `21200` |        `21200` |         `1 / 0` |    `13.1 ms` |

The probe shows a real trade: hiding can eliminate child-list churn and node allocation/removal in
the isolated DOM loop, but it does not reduce total mutation records; it converts the work into
attribute and character-data mutations. It also changes the live DOM invariant. Hidden suffix nodes
would still exist under the Rich body, so `textContent` shape, accessibility expectations, and
path-based patching would all need a new semantic contract.

Conclusion: do not implement hidden suffixes from this probe alone. The path remains a possible
larger design only if there is first a semantic plan for hidden rich content and then a package A/B
proving it beats the current visible-prefix DOM, not just an isolated child-list counter reduction.

## Rejected Rich full-to-clamped equal text guard

A small follow-up tested whether `patchFullToClamped` should guard its text-node assignment and
skip `liveNode.data = text` when the current full DOM text node already has the clamped prefix. The
target was the extra `characterData` churn introduced by preserving full-to-clamped text nodes.

Focused smoke before/after used
`rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`, `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`,
`rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`, and
`rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps`. Logs:
`/tmp/vue-clamp-full-to-clamped-text-guard-before.log` and
`/tmp/vue-clamp-full-to-clamped-text-guard-after.log`.

| Counter                     |          Before |           After |
| --------------------------- | --------------: | --------------: |
| BBox reads                  |         `28832` |         `28832` |
| Client rect reads / entries |  `8368 / 43780` |  `8368 / 43780` |
| Mutation records            |         `63298` |         `63298` |
| Child-list records          |         `34480` |         `34480` |
| Character-data records      |         `11760` |         `11760` |
| Added / removed nodes       | `29648 / 29648` | `29648 / 29648` |
| Style reads                 |         `19216` |         `19216` |

The guard was removed. It did not touch the measured Rich hotspots, while the temporary pack grew
slightly (`124.44 kB / gzip 26.13 kB` to `124.47 kB / gzip 26.14 kB`). Active-time movement is not
evidence here because every structural counter stayed identical.

## Current Line/Inline hotspot refresh

After rejecting another Rich DOM micro-guard, a current Line/Inline smoke refreshed the non-Rich
hotspot shape before narrowing the next search scope. Log:
`/tmp/vue-clamp-line-inline-hotspot-current.log`.

| Scenario                           |         Active / RME | Main structural shape                                     |
| ---------------------------------- | -------------------: | --------------------------------------------------------- |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous`  |  `515.5 ms` / `2.0%` | bbox `14976`, style reads `2272`, mutations `12139`       |
| `line-word-copy-batch-jitter`      |  `469.4 ms` / `3.8%` | bbox `12272`, style reads `2160`, mutations `11536`       |
| `inline-path-end-batch-continuous` | `406.5 ms` / `42.3%` | bbox `7296`, scroll-width reads `4512`, mutations `10416` |
| `inline-path-middle-batch-jitter`  |  `483.9 ms` / `3.5%` | bbox `7680`, scroll-width reads `5010`, mutations `11164` |

The refreshed shape supports the same narrowing as the Rich rejected-guard work: Line and Inline
should not spend more complexity on equal-write micro-guards. The remaining visible work is real
candidate probing (`bbox` / `scrollWidth`) plus Vue width/style churn in the multi-instance fixture.
Further performance work needs either a search-level proof that reduces candidate probes or a
stronger state-identity proof for safe result reuse; otherwise the next useful direction is
maintainability around the already-retained search/hint logic.

## Rejected text layout warm expansion change

A search-level follow-up tested whether the remaining Line/Inline candidate probes could be reduced
by changing the local warm-search expansion budget.

First, lowering the shared default expansion limit from `2` to `1` was rejected immediately on the
Line/Inline hotspot set. It increased every probe-shaped counter that mattered:

| Counter                | Current | Limit 1 |
| ---------------------- | ------: | ------: |
| BBox reads             | `42224` | `43797` |
| Scroll-width reads     |  `9522` | `13638` |
| Mutation records       | `45255` | `51451` |
| Character-data records | `17122` | `23318` |

Raising the shared default to `3` gave a small `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous` structural win
without changing Inline, but that global scope was wrong because it also changes non-text callers
and Rich's derived budget. A narrower text-layout-only expansion `3` then reproduced the local win
while leaving Inline unchanged, so it was tested against a broader grapheme Line set. Logs:
`/tmp/vue-clamp-text-layout-expansion-3-line-broad.log` and
`/tmp/vue-clamp-text-layout-expansion-2-line-broad.log`.

| Scenario                             | Structural delta from default `2` to text-layout `3`                               |
| ------------------------------------ | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous`    | bbox `14976 -> 14855`, mutations `12139 -> 12000`                                  |
| `line-height-affix-card-batch-jumps` | bbox `20576 -> 20430`, mutations `13154 -> 13106`                                  |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter`        | bbox `19719 -> 20104`, mutations `17702 -> 18124`                                  |
| Broad totals                         | bbox `85362 -> 85480`, mutations `70068 -> 70303`, character-data `30004 -> 30239` |

The experiment was removed. The current expansion limit remains the best covered trade-off. The
useful lesson is more specific: one extra local expansion helps some smooth affix width changes,
but the same budget over-probes jitter. A future retained algorithm would need an input or state
signal that distinguishes smooth local movement from jitter, not another single constant.

## Rejected Rich simple-line overflow cache

A subsequent Rich hotspot refresh used a current-only smoke over Line/Rich rows with CJK, novel
jitter, dynamic atomic, and font-size tick coverage. The low-noise Rich candidates were:
`rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter` (`555.1 ms` / RME `2.3%`, bbox `9280`, client rect
`7616 / 18964`, mutations `18320`) and
`rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` (`238.0 ms` / RME `3.1%`, bbox `4096`, style reads
`8496`, mutations `16114`).

A temporary diagnostic split the remaining Rich work by patch/search path. It showed
`rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter` spends `7472` candidate fits, mostly same-text cuts (`6560`) and
same-state validations (`3056`), while `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` spends only
`2704` candidate fits but mostly whole-prefix patching (`1552` forward, `1584` backward) plus
style reinspection. `rich-word-dynamic-atomic-batch-jumps` confirmed that atomic rows still depend
on whole-prefix/fallback paths.

The tested candidate set `verifyOverflow: true` on Rich simple-line search indexes, mirroring the
existing conservative LineClamp overflow-height cache. It produced no structural movement in the
focused rows:

| Scenario                                                                             |               Before |            Candidate |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | -------------------: | -------------------: |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter` client rect reads / entries                       |       `7616 / 18964` |       `7616 / 18964` |
| `rich-word-dynamic-atomic-batch-jumps` client rect reads / entries                   |        `2400 / 6480` |        `2400 / 6480` |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` bbox / client rect entries / style reads | `4096 / 9408 / 8496` | `4096 / 9408 / 8496` |

The candidate was removed. The result narrows the next Rich work: current simple-line Rich rows are
not repeatedly paying overflow rect-list verification that this cache can remove. Further gains
need either fewer candidate probes, cheaper whole-prefix patching, or a stronger freshness signal
that can avoid full style reinspection without missing CSS-driven layout changes. In particular,
same-state hint fits cannot be trusted solely from same or growing width because font-size ticks can
change the fit boundary while width looks reusable.

## Rich patch fragment commit refactor

After the remaining Rich patch hotspot was narrowed to larger representation questions, the retained
patcher received a small maintainability refactor instead of another local micro-optimization. The
root-ellipsis fragment commit rule had been repeated in three places: `patchForwardWholePrefix`,
`patchForwardTextPrefix`, and the generic `patchRich` fallback. It is now centralized in one helper
that inserts a source fragment before an existing root ellipsis when possible, or appends the
fragment and adds a root ellipsis for clamped output when needed.

This is not a performance claim. Focused Rich browser tests passed, and the guard smoke in
`/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-append-fragment-refactor.log` kept structural counters unchanged:

| Scenario                                    | Structural shape after refactor                                        |
| ------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`          | bbox `9280`, rects `7616 / 18964`, mutations `18320`                   |
| `rich-word-dynamic-atomic-batch-jumps`      | bbox `1440`, rects `2400 / 6480`, mutations `5314`                     |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` | bbox `4096`, rects `272 / 9408`, style reads `8496`, mutations `16114` |

The smoke pack measured `124.35 kB` raw / `26.15 kB` gzip. The practical value is that future Rich
patch work has one root-ellipsis commit rule to audit instead of three duplicated copies. Any future
performance patch in this area should still prove fewer child-list records or candidate probes
against the same Rich guard rows.

## Rich dynamic atomic reverse invalidation

A follow-up correctness pass found that Rich search-index invalidation was asymmetric. The existing
reinspection covered transparent inline wrappers that later became atomic, because cached all-text
indexes with `simpleLineFit` were rechecked before reuse. The reverse direction was not covered:
when a wrapper first measured as an atomic `inline-block` and later became transparent inline through
a CSS custom property, the cached logical runs still treated it as unsliceable. A direct browser
regression now starts with `display:var(--token-display)` resolving to `inline-block`, clamps to
only the ellipsis, then changes the variable to `inline` and reuses the previous search index. The
fixed result slices inside the wrapper and shows `observability…` instead of staying at `…`.

The retained fix records whether an atomic rich path came from a variable-backed `display`
declaration. Only those indexes force a full current-DOM layout reinspection on reuse; static
inline-style atomics and static class atomics keep the previous cached shape. Focused validation:

- Browser tests:
  `vp test -c vite.browser.config.ts packages/vue-clamp/tests/clamp.browser.test.ts -t "inline wrappers become atomic|atomic wrappers become inline|rich child line metrics"`
  passed `4` tests.
- Focused smoke log:
  `/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-atomic-refresh-narrow-after.log`.

| Scenario                               | Structural shape after fix                                                                        |
| -------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`     | unchanged guard shape: bbox `9280`, rects `7616 / 18964`, mutations `18320`, style reads `0`      |
| `rich-word-class-atomic-batch-jumps`   | unchanged static class shape: bbox `1440`, rects `1840 / 4720`, mutations `5360`, style reads `0` |
| `rich-word-dynamic-atomic-batch-jumps` | correctness refresh shape: bbox `2816`, rects `1008 / 1536`, mutations `6018`, style reads `1584` |

The dynamic row is not claimed as a pure performance win: it trades stale under-rendering for current
layout reinspection, lowering rect-list work but adding style reads, bbox reads, and mutation work.
The important result is that the extra work is limited to the CSS-variable display input where the
old cached logical runs were wrong; the static atomic and metadata guard rows do not regress
structurally.

A second pass widened that detection to CSS grouping rules. The first retained scanner only checked
top-level `CSSStyleRule` objects, so a rule such as
`@media (min-width:1px){.token{display:var(--token-display)}}` still missed the same reverse
invalidation and kept rendering only `…`. A browser regression now covers the grouped-rule form, and
the scanner recursively checks nested `cssRules`.

Focused validation after the grouped-rule fix:

- Browser tests:
  `vp test -c vite.browser.config.ts packages/vue-clamp/tests/clamp.browser.test.ts -t "grouping rules|atomic wrappers become inline|inline wrappers become atomic|rich child line metrics"`
  passed `5` tests.
- Focused smoke log:
  `/tmp/vue-clamp-rich-atomic-refresh-grouped-after.log`.

The smoke structure stayed identical to the narrowed dynamic-display version:
`rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter` stayed bbox `9280`, rects `7616 / 18964`, mutations `18320`,
style reads `0`; `rich-word-class-atomic-batch-jumps` stayed bbox `1440`, rects `1840 / 4720`,
mutations `5360`, style reads `0`; `rich-word-dynamic-atomic-batch-jumps` stayed bbox `2816`,
rects `1008 / 1536`, mutations `6018`, style reads `1584`. The smoke pack measured `126.29 kB`
raw / `26.60 kB` gzip.

The grouped-rule scanner is limited to currently active media rules. A negative regression covers a
static atomic rule plus an inactive
`@media (max-width:1px){.token{display:var(--token-display)}}` rule. Before the media guard, the
cached-index reuse pass paid `2` unnecessary `getComputedStyle` calls even though the variable rule
could not affect the current layout; after the guard it pays `0` calls and keeps the static atomic
result. The positive grouped-rule regression still passes for matching media, so the reverse
invalidation is preserved where the declaration can affect layout. Focused Rich smoke stayed
structurally unchanged from the grouped-rule pass, and the pack measured `126.50 kB` raw /
`26.67 kB` gzip.

A third pass covered dynamic stylesheet insertion. The failing case started with a static cascade
rule making `.dynamic-token` an `inline-block`, so the first cached search index treated that span as
an atomic run and cached a negative variable-display lookup. The application then appended a later
stylesheet with `.dynamic-token{display:var(--token-display)}` while the CSS variable resolved to
`inline`. Before the fix, the next clamp reused the stale atomic index and rendered only `…`; after
the fix, rich indexes with element descendants compare the current `document.styleSheets.length`
with the count recorded at inspection time and reinspect once when it changes. Stable benchmark rows
do not pay this refresh. Focused tests for later stylesheets, active/inactive media rules, and atomic
direction changes passed, and the same three-row Rich smoke stayed structurally unchanged: metadata
affix `9280` bbox / `7616` rect reads / `18320` mutations / `0` style reads, static atomic `1440` /
`1840` / `5360` / `0`, dynamic atomic `2816` / `1008` / `6018` / `1584`. The pack measured
`127.39 kB` raw / `26.81 kB` gzip.

That count-only signal still missed CSSOM edits inside an existing stylesheet. A focused regression
now keeps the same `<style>` element, starts with a static
`.dynamic-token{display:inline-block}` rule, then inserts a later top-level CSSOM rule
`.dynamic-token{display:var(--token-display)}` at the end of the same stylesheet. Before the
rule-list signature, the second clamp still rendered only `…`. The retained signal now records the
stylesheet count plus each accessible stylesheet's top-level rule count, so top-level
`insertRule` / `deleteRule` changes invalidate cached rich runs without monkey-patching browser
prototypes. The same active/inactive media and atomic-direction tests passed, and the same three-row
Rich smoke stayed structurally unchanged: metadata affix `9280` / `7616` / `18320` / `0`, static
atomic `1440` / `1840` / `5360` / `0`, dynamic atomic `2816` / `1008` / `6018` / `1584`. The pack
measured `127.66 kB` raw / `26.87 kB` gzip.

The next adjacent case moved the same `insertRule` operation inside an already-present active
`@media` rule. Top-level stylesheet rule counts did not change, so the second clamp again reused the
stale atomic index and rendered only `…` before the fix. The retained signature now recurses through
active grouping rules and records nested rule-list lengths; it still ignores inactive media bodies
for this purpose, matching the variable-display scanner's current-layout scope. Focused CSSOM,
media, and atomic-direction tests passed, and the same three-row Rich smoke stayed structurally
unchanged: metadata affix `9280` / `7616` / `18320` / `0`, static atomic `1440` / `1840` / `5360` /
`0`, dynamic atomic `2816` / `1008` / `6018` / `1584`. The pack measured `127.96 kB` raw /
`26.92 kB` gzip.

One remaining same-count CSSOM case changed the `display` declaration on an existing
`CSSStyleRule`. The first clamp cached a static `.dynamic-token{display:inline-block}` atomic run;
then the test mutated `rule.style.display = "inline"` without changing any rule-list length. Before
the fix, the second clamp still rendered only `…`. The retained signature now records each active
style rule's `selectorText` and `style.display`, not full `cssText`, because rich logical-run
staleness is driven by display changes that move wrappers between atomic and searchable inline
layout. Focused CSSOM/media tests passed, and the same three-row Rich smoke stayed structurally
unchanged: metadata affix `9280` / `7616` / `18320` / `0`, static atomic `1440` / `1840` / `5360` /
`0`, dynamic atomic `2816` / `1008` / `6018` / `1584`. The pack measured `128.07 kB` raw /
`26.93 kB` gzip.

The final media-match boundary did not require more runtime code. A regression now starts with an
inactive `@media (max-width:1px)` rule containing the variable display declaration, then changes the
same `CSSMediaRule` to `(min-width:1px)` before reclamping with the cached search index. The test
passes with the existing signature: inactive media bodies are absent from the signature, and once
the media rule matches, the nested rule-list plus display declaration enter the signature and force
one rich layout reinspection. This closes the current CSS identity pass without adding a new
signature dimension or changing package size.

A final local simplification removed duplicate stylesheet signature scans inside one cached rich
metadata refresh. The same signature value now feeds variable-display cache invalidation and cached
search-index identity checks during a single synchronous `clampRich` pass. A browser structural test
patches `CSSStyleSheet.prototype.cssRules` and verifies that a cached dynamic-atomic rich reclamp
reads `cssRules` exactly once per stylesheet, while still refreshing the stale atomic run after
`--token-display` changes from `inline-block` to `inline`. Focused CSS identity tests passed
(`12 passed | 71 skipped`), full clamp browser tests passed (`83 passed`), and default tests passed
(`29 passed`). The same three-row Rich smoke stayed DOM-structurally unchanged: metadata affix
`9280` / `7616` / `18320` / `0`, static atomic `1440` / `1840` / `5360` / `0`, dynamic atomic
`2816` / `1008` / `6018` / `1584`. The pack measured `128.51 kB` raw / `26.98 kB` gzip, so this is
retained only as a narrow CSSOM-work reduction, not as a new DOM/layout benchmark claim.

The same CSSOM path was narrowed once more for all-text rich content. Rich indexes whose inspected
layout has no element descendants now store an empty stylesheet signature and skip stylesheet scans
entirely, because CSS selectors cannot change their logical run shape. A browser structural test
covers both first index creation and cached reclamp, asserting `0` `cssRules` reads for
`"observabilityPlatform1 trailing copy"`. The dynamic-atomic signature test still proves one
stylesheet scan for element-containing cached refreshes. Focused CSS identity tests passed
(`13 passed | 71 skipped`), full clamp browser tests passed (`84 passed`), and default tests passed
(`29 passed`). The four-row Rich smoke stayed DOM-structurally unchanged, including
`rich-word-copy-batch-jitter` at bbox `10960`, rects `0 / 0`, mutations `13072`, style reads
`3840`. The pack measured `128.50 kB` raw / `26.97 kB` gzip.

The element-containing first-pass case was then tightened as well. The stylesheet signature walker
now records active selectors whose `display` declaration contains `var(...)`, and
`hasVariableDisplayDeclaration` matches elements against that selector list instead of reading
`cssRules` again. A browser structural test verifies that first-time dynamic-atomic rich index
creation reads `CSSStyleSheet.cssRules` exactly once per current stylesheet, the same as cached
metadata refresh. Focused CSS identity tests passed (`14 passed | 71 skipped`), full clamp browser
tests passed (`85 passed`), default tests passed (`29 passed`), and the four-row Rich smoke stayed
DOM-structurally unchanged. The pack measured `128.46 kB` raw / `26.97 kB` gzip.

The adjacent maintainability pass removed hidden default stylesheet scans from the internal
signature consumers: rich layout inspection, variable-display detection, and variable-display cache
refresh now require the caller-provided lazy signature reader/value explicitly. This is behavior
neutral because all retained call sites already shared the same per-clamp reader. Focused CSS
identity tests, full clamp browser tests (`85 passed`), default tests (`29 passed`), and package
build passed. The pack measured `128.37 kB` raw / `26.97 kB` gzip.

One more CSS identity correctness boundary covers unreadable stylesheets. A browser regression now
patches one test stylesheet's `cssRules` getter to throw while the stylesheet still applies
`.dynamic-token{display:var(--token-display)}`. Before the fix, the first clamp could cache the
wrapper as a static atomic run because the selector list was unknowable; changing
`--token-display` to `inline` then risked reusing that stale index. The retained behavior treats the
variable-display selector list as incomplete when any active stylesheet cannot expose rules, so rich
atomic descendants are marked style-dependent and re-inspected on reclamp. Focused CSS identity
tests passed (`15 passed | 71 skipped`), full clamp browser tests passed (`86 passed`), default
tests passed (`29 passed`), and the same four-row Rich smoke stayed DOM-structurally unchanged. The
pack measured `128.61 kB` raw / `27.00 kB` gzip, so this is retained as correctness coverage with a
small size cost, not as a performance win.

After the correctness and CSS-identity passes, the next change is a behavior-neutral text warm-gate
cleanup. The LineClamp/InlineClamp text path now computes the estimated warm target, local movement,
and warm-versus-cold probe budget through one helper, and both warm hint reuse and guarded
full-source-fit skipping consume that same estimate. This does not claim a new runtime win; it
reduces the chance that the two gates drift apart when the rank model changes again.

Validation stayed focused on equivalence and structure: `vp test packages/vue-clamp/tests/text.test.ts`
passed (`18` tests), the text layout browser tests passed (`22` tests), `vp check --fix` passed,
default `vp test` passed (`29` tests), and the clamp/inline/layout/text-layout browser suite passed
(`127` tests). A three-row package smoke also stayed on the known structural shape:
`line-cta-affix-batch-continuous` at bbox `14976`, rects `16 / 64`, mutations `12139`, style reads
`2272`; `line-word-copy-batch-jitter` at bbox `12272`, rects `0 / 0`, mutations `11536`, style
reads `2160`; and `inline-path-middle-batch-jitter` at bbox `7680`, scrollWidth `5010`, mutations
`11164`, style reads `0`. The smoke pack measured `129.17 kB` raw / `27.16 kB` gzip. The inline
row's active-time RME was `54.58%`, so the timing result is deliberately not used as evidence.

The next retained Rich optimization narrows cached simple-line refresh for trusted width-only
RichLineClamp reclamps. Before this pass, a cached rich search index with transparent element
wrappers still reran full `inspectLayout` on every simple-line refresh, which meant reading computed
style for the currently rendered rich descendants even when only the root width changed. The retained
path lets the component mark root-width-snapshot reclamps as width-only: if the stylesheet signature
is unchanged, no variable-driven display or line metric rule can affect the rich tree, and the rich
body's `font-size` / `line-height` / `vertical-align` key is unchanged, the pass reuses the cached
simple-line fit after one body `getComputedStyle` read. Any failed guard falls back to full
inspection. The stylesheet signature now includes active `font-size`, `line-height`, and
`vertical-align` declarations so CSSOM changes to line metrics invalidate cached metadata, and any
active `var(...)` use in those declarations conservatively disables the shortcut.

Correctness checks intentionally cover the escape hatches. A new browser test proves the trusted
static path uses one computed-style read on a width-only reclamp. Existing child-inline-style metric
changes still force exact rect verification when the direct helper is used without the trusted
component hint. The stylesheet-driven `font-size: var(--metric-size)` test was rerun with the
trusted hint enabled and still forces exact rect verification. The dynamic `display: var(...)`
atomic-to-inline test was also rerun with the trusted hint enabled and still rebuilds cached rich
search metadata.

Focused Rich browser tests passed (`87` tests), `vp check --fix` passed, default `vp test` passed
(`29` tests), and the clamp/inline/layout/text-layout browser suite passed (`128` tests). Same-turn
Rich smoke before/after over the four narrowed rows showed deterministic structural movement:

| Scenario                                      | Before                                         | After                                         | Structural result                                                                |
| --------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`            | style `0`, rects `7616 / 18964`, bbox `9280`   | style `0`, rects `7616 / 18964`, bbox `9280`  | unchanged                                                                        |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`                 | style `3840`, rects `0 / 0`, bbox `10960`      | style `1920`, rects `0 / 0`, bbox `10960`     | `-1920` style reads                                                              |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`   | style `8496`, rects `272 / 9408`, bbox `4096`  | style `8496`, rects `272 / 9408`, bbox `4096` | unchanged                                                                        |
| `rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` | style `6880`, rects `480 / 15408`, bbox `4496` | style `480`, rects `0 / 0`, bbox `4976`       | `-6400` style reads, `-480` rect reads, `-15408` rect entries, `+480` bbox reads |

Across these rows, style reads moved `19216 -> 10896` (`-8320`, `-43.3%`), client rect reads
`8368 -> 7888` (`-480`, `-5.7%`), client rect entries `43780 -> 28372` (`-15408`, `-35.2%`), and
bounding rect reads `28832 -> 29312` (`+480`, `+1.7%`). Mutation records were unchanged at `63298`.
The pack measured `132.24 kB` raw / `27.66 kB` gzip, versus the pre-pass `129.17 kB` raw /
`27.16 kB` gzip, so the retained cost is about `+3.07 kB` raw / `+0.50 kB` gzip for a proved
Rich style/rect-list workload reduction. Active-time medians were mixed and some rows had high RME,
so timing is not used as proof.

A follow-up audit found a correctness issue in that signature walker: the first implementation used
`||=` while merging the "has variable line metrics" flag, which could short-circuit the recursive
stylesheet scan after the first matching rule. That was wrong because the scan has required side
effects beyond the boolean: it appends later rules to the stylesheet signature and collects later
`display: var(...)` selectors. The bug could appear when an earlier stylesheet contained
`font-size: var(...)` and a later stylesheet contained the display rule needed to rebuild rich
metadata.

The fix always executes each active stylesheet/grouping scan and merges the boolean result
afterward. A browser regression now puts a line-metric variable rule in one stylesheet and a dynamic
display rule in a later stylesheet, enables trusted simple-line reuse, then verifies that changing
`--token-display` from `inline-block` to `inline` still rebuilds cached rich metadata and exposes
the token text. Focused Rich browser tests passed (`88` tests), `vp check --fix` passed, and the same
four-row Rich smoke kept the retained structural result: style reads `10896`, client rect reads
`7888`, client rect entries `28372`, bbox reads `29312`, and mutation records `63298`. The pack
measured `132.38 kB` raw / `27.68 kB` gzip after the regression fix.

A final simplification pass compressed the retained Rich simple-line reuse implementation without
changing the measured work shape. The code now uses the same combined line-metric key for inline
style checks and stylesheet signatures, stores an incomplete variable-display selector list as
`null` instead of a separate boolean, and removes a duplicate helper around line-metric `var(...)`
detection. Focused Rich browser tests and `vp check --fix` passed after each simplification. The
four-row Rich smoke still reported style reads `10896`, client rect reads `7888`, client rect entries
`28372`, bbox reads `29312`, and mutation records `63298`, while pack size moved from `132.38 kB`
raw / `27.68 kB` gzip to `131.88 kB` raw / `27.65 kB` gzip. Compared with the pre-pass `129.17 kB`
raw / `27.16 kB` gzip baseline, the retained cost is now about `+2.71 kB` raw / `+0.49 kB` gzip for
the proved Rich computed-style and rect-list workload reduction.

A current-only eight-row hotspot smoke then refreshed the narrowed search space after the Rich
simple-line pass. The retained package size was still `131.88 kB` raw / `27.65 kB` gzip. The
structural shape was:

| Scenario                                      | Structural shape                                                              |
| --------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous`             | bbox `14976`, client rects `16 / 64`, mutations `12139`, style reads `2272`   |
| `line-word-copy-batch-jitter`                 | bbox `12272`, client rects `0 / 0`, mutations `11536`, style reads `2160`     |
| `inline-path-end-batch-continuous`            | bbox `7296`, scrollWidth `4512`, mutations `10416`                            |
| `inline-path-middle-batch-jitter`             | bbox `7680`, scrollWidth `5010`, mutations `11164`                            |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`            | bbox `9280`, client rects `7616 / 18964`, mutations `18320`, style reads `0`  |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`                 | bbox `10960`, client rects `0 / 0`, mutations `13072`, style reads `1920`     |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`   | bbox `4096`, client rects `272 / 9408`, mutations `16114`, style reads `8496` |
| `rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` | bbox `4976`, client rects `0 / 0`, mutations `15792`, style reads `480`       |

This refresh keeps the next scope narrow: Inline's end-continuous row has no repeated width
assignments, so a same-width result cache would target the benchmark's jitter rows but not the
unrepeated smooth path. The remaining Inline cost is still candidate `scrollWidth` probing plus root
signature reads and text mutation work.

One Inline experiment tried to reuse `ResizeObserverEntry` root border-box snapshots in
`InlineClamp`, mirroring the multiline shell's root-width shortcut. The hypothesis was that RO
callbacks might be scheduling recomputes without passing the fresh subpixel root width into
`clampBody`, causing duplicate root `getBoundingClientRect()` reads. Focused smoke rejected the
hypothesis: `inline-path-end-batch-continuous` stayed bbox `7296`, scrollWidth `4512`, mutations
`10416`; `inline-path-middle-batch-jitter` stayed bbox `7680`, scrollWidth `5010`, mutations
`11164`. The patch also grew the package to `132.87 kB` raw / `27.75 kB` gzip. It was removed. The
result shows the remaining Inline bbox reads are not coming from a missing RO-width handoff in the
current fixture; they belong to clamp measurement and post-recompute layout signatures.

The retained Inline follow-up targeted the latter source directly. On Vue-driven style updates,
`InlineClamp` already reads a parent/root layout snapshot in `onUpdated` and passes the fresh root
width into `clampBody`. For inline content-independent widths such as the package benchmark's
`width:${n}px`, the body rewrite cannot change the root width or one-line border-box height, and
the hidden source span is absolutely positioned. The component now reuses that `onUpdated` signature
as the settled post-recompute signature only when the root width is still trusted. Requests without
a fresh snapshot, such as font events and ResizeObserver invalidations, clear the pending signature
and keep the post-recompute read.

Focused validation:

- `vp check --fix` passed.
- Inline browser contract passed (`13` tests).
- Default tests passed (`29` tests).
- Clamp/inline/layout/text-layout browser suite passed (`129` tests).
- Focused package smoke kept scroll/probe/mutation work unchanged and halved Inline bbox reads:
  `inline-path-end-batch-continuous` bbox `7296 -> 3648`, scrollWidth `4512 -> 4512`, mutations
  `10416 -> 10416`; `inline-path-middle-batch-jitter` bbox `7680 -> 3840`, scrollWidth
  `5010 -> 5010`, mutations `11164 -> 11164`.

The focused smoke pack measured `132.13 kB` raw / `27.70 kB` gzip, about `+0.25 kB` raw /
`+0.05 kB` gzip over the prior `131.88 kB` raw / `27.65 kB` gzip retained shape. This is a narrow
structural win: it does not reduce candidate `scrollWidth` probes, but it removes the duplicate
settled signature layout read for fixed-width Inline churn.

## Review residual correctness audit

After comparing the external review against the current worktree, most cited correctness hazards
already have direct guards in current code and tests: skip-full text/rich recovery, Inline
percentage and CSS-variable width distrust, font-load argument isolation, transformed
ResizeObserver entry comparison, max-height visible-bounds refresh, Rich float fallback, trailing
whitespace full-state verification, and native multiline zero-width content measurement.

One missing direct component guard was absolute-positioned rich descendants. The design already
requires out-of-flow Rich content to fall back to raw HTML, but the component suite only covered a
float descendant and block wrapper. A browser regression now mounts RichLineClamp with a fitting
absolute-positioned child under `maxHeight` and verifies raw HTML is preserved, `clamped` is false,
and the root clears max-height clipping. Focused validation passed:

- `vp test -c vite.browser.config.ts packages/vue-clamp/tests/clamp.browser.test.ts -t "absolute-positioned rich html"`
  passed (`1` test).
- `vp test -c vite.browser.config.ts packages/vue-clamp/tests/clamp.browser.test.ts` passed (`89`
  tests).

No performance claim is attached to this guard. It narrows the remaining review risk before the next
optimization loop and keeps future Rich search/index caching from accepting an unsupported
out-of-flow layout merely because the full tree currently fits.

## Inline exact-width result cache

The next Inline pass tested the repeated-width cache idea that the previous hotspot refresh left
open. The retained version is deliberately narrower than a generic layout cache: it is used only
when `onUpdated` has already supplied a fresh parent/root layout signature, the root width is an
inline content-independent length, the root has no non-empty class attribute, the root inline style
contains no unresolved `%` or `var(...)` references, and the root inline style declares its own text
metrics through `font` or `font-size` plus `font-family`. Requests without such a snapshot clear the
cache, so font events and ResizeObserver invalidations still take the measured path. This keeps the
optimization scoped to repeated exact-width Vue style churn, not to class-styled, variable-driven,
or stylesheet-driven text metrics.

A new Inline browser regression covers the most direct stale-cache hazard: it caches a clamped
result at one fixed root width under a `16px` inline font, visits another width, then returns to the
same width after changing the root inline font to `10px`. The full body now fits, and the test
asserts that the component recomputes instead of reusing the old clamped result. Inline browser tests
passed (`14` tests), and `vp check --fix` passed.

A convergence follow-up covered the adjacent CSS-variable font-metric boundary. Browser coverage
keeps a fixed-width InlineClamp root whose `font-size` comes from a parent custom property, seeds the
repeated-width path, then shrinks the font via that variable and verifies the full body is restored.
The shared inline-font-metrics gate now also rejects unresolved `%` / `var(...)` metric values in
unit coverage, so exact-result caches cannot start depending on browser-specific CSSOM treatment of
custom-property font declarations.

The next cache-boundary check found a real stale-cache case rather than a theoretical one:
`letter-spacing: var(...)` on the fixed-width InlineClamp root reused an old repeated-width result
after the parent variable changed to a spacing where the full text fit. The focused browser test
failed before the guard change and passed after `canCacheInlineResult` rejected unresolved inline
text-width style references.

The first implementation of that guard was too broad: scanning the whole rendered root `style`
string also saw InlineClamp's own `max-width:100%` safety style and disabled the exact-result cache
for legitimate fixed-width benchmark rows. A focused two-row smoke showed the cache-off shape:
`inline-path-middle-batch-jitter` scrollWidth `5010` / mutations `11164`, and
`inline-word-copy-batch-jumps` scrollWidth `2016` / mutations `2720`. The retained guard now scans
only inline declarations that can change one-line text width, such as font longhands,
`letter-spacing`, `word-spacing`, and `text-transform`. `vp test packages/vue-clamp/tests/layout.test.ts`
and the full Inline browser suite passed, including the `letter-spacing:var(...)` stale-cache
regression. The same focused smoke then returned to the retained exact-cache shape:
`inline-path-middle-batch-jitter` scrollWidth `2116` / mutations `9168`, and
`inline-word-copy-batch-jumps` scrollWidth `672` / mutations `1856`.

The workload proof used a same-process two-run smoke over the full Inline package group. The before
run temporarily set the cache limit to `0`, which keeps the same code shape but prevents cache hits;
the after run restored the retained `64`-entry limit and the narrowed cache guards.

| Scenario                              | Width profile                         | ScrollWidth reads | Mutation records | Active time / RME                         |
| ------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------- | ----------------: | ---------------: | ----------------------------------------- |
| `inline-path-end-batch-continuous`    | `0` repeated transitions, max delta 4 |    `4512 -> 4512` | `10416 -> 10416` | `485.5 -> 466.9 ms`, RME `7.8% -> 0.4%`   |
| `inline-path-end-batch-jumps`         | `15` repeated transitions             |     `2688 -> 896` |   `3824 -> 2224` | `92.0 -> 77.1 ms`, RME `15.3% -> 22.7%`   |
| `inline-path-middle-batch-continuous` | `0` repeated transitions, max delta 4 |    `4556 -> 4556` | `10481 -> 10481` | `462.1 -> 470.9 ms`, RME `3.9% -> 2.8%`   |
| `inline-path-middle-batch-jitter`     | `68` repeated transitions             |    `5010 -> 2116` |  `11164 -> 9168` | `461.2 -> 427.8 ms`, RME `14.9% -> 41.5%` |
| `inline-path-middle-batch-jumps`      | `15` repeated transitions             |     `2748 -> 916` |   `3893 -> 2247` | `96.6 -> 75.8 ms`, RME `7.3% -> 7.1%`     |
| `inline-path-start-batch-jumps`       | `15` repeated transitions             |     `2781 -> 927` |   `4004 -> 2284` | `96.8 -> 73.9 ms`, RME `3.2% -> 8.8%`     |
| `inline-split-file-path-batch-jumps`  | `15` repeated transitions             |      `432 -> 144` |    `1152 -> 960` | `64.2 -> 47.6 ms`, RME `7.3% -> 22.3%`    |
| `inline-word-copy-batch-jumps`        | `15` repeated transitions             |     `2016 -> 672` |   `2720 -> 1856` | `92.1 -> 72.3 ms`, RME `34.0% -> 5.5%`    |
