| `inline-custom-marker-batch-jumps`    | `15` repeated transitions             |     `2688 -> 896` |   `3824 -> 2224` | `94.7 -> 69.8 ms`, RME `6.1% -> 18.2%`    |

Totals moved from scrollWidth `27431 -> 15635` (`-11796`, `-43.0%`) and mutation records
`51478 -> 41860` (`-9618`, `-18.7%`). The mutation reduction is exactly the character-data
reduction (`25361 -> 15743`), which matches the mechanism: repeated exact-width hits apply the
known final text instead of replaying the candidate search. Bounding-rect reads stayed flat at
`14592`, and the two continuous rows with no repeated width transitions stayed structurally
unchanged, so the retained claim is explicitly repeated-width only. Active medians mostly moved in
the expected direction, but several rows still have high RME; timing is supporting evidence, not the
proof.

The retained package build measured `134.02 kB` raw / `28.16 kB` gzip. Compared with the preceding
Inline signature snapshot retained shape (`132.13 kB` raw / `27.70 kB` gzip), the cost is about
`+1.89 kB` raw / `+0.46 kB` gzip for the proved repeated-width scroll/mutation reduction. This is a
real workload optimization for repeated exact-width inputs, but it should not be generalized to
novel-width rows or class/stylesheet-driven text metrics.

## External review reconciliation follow-up

The external review usefully identified the main correctness class behind the earlier warm/skip
work: fast paths must not remove the "verify full source when needed" invariant. Comparing that
review against the current worktree shows that the high-risk items are now guarded directly rather
than just inferred from the implementation: text and rich skipped-full searches verify the bare full
candidate when monotonicity does not prove it, Inline percentage and CSS-variable widths are not
trusted in shrink-to-fit layouts, font-load events cannot flow into width parameters, transformed
ResizeObserver entries use visual signatures, Rich out-of-flow descendants fall back before any
full-fit success can be accepted, and native multiline still refuses zero-width content boxes.

The remaining Rich long-token mutation hotspot was also rechecked against the existing diagnostics.
It is not an uncovered `full -> clamped` or missing generic patch family: current evidence shows the
long-token rows are dominated by retained whole-prefix clamped-to-clamped suffix changes, and
`Range.deleteContents()` does not change MutationObserver node accounting. The isolated hidden-suffix
probe proved only a work-shape trade, converting child-list records into attribute and
character-data records without reducing total mutation records and with a different DOM semantic
contract. That keeps the next credible Rich mutation step at the representation-design level, not at
another small patch-helper tweak.

One review scenario did not yet have the narrow component-level guard it deserved: a non-native
LineClamp that is currently unclamped and then receives either an empty source string or another
unclamped source string. Two browser regressions now cover those paths with an after slot forcing the
measured DOM path. They assert that the visible body becomes empty or the new source text, no
visually hidden source wrapper remains, and `clamped` stays false. Focused validation passed for the
new guard rows (`2` tests). This adds no performance claim, but it closes a correctness blind spot
before future text warm-path simplification.

## Rich warm-gate convergence cleanup

The next pass avoided another speculative Rich patch experiment and instead reduced drift risk in
the existing warm gates. `RichLineClamp` now computes the affix-identity comparison once per probe
and passes that boolean into both search-hint reuse and skipped-full-fit gating. The fixed `32px`
window is documented as a bootstrap locality window before a measured word-rank slope exists, not as
an independent correctness proof. A later cleanup named the shared observed-word-rank guard used by
both beyond-window search hints and full-fit skipping, while keeping `textRankSafe` required only for
search-hint reuse because that path chooses the local search starting point. The same cleanup phase
made Rich rank-slope updates receive the previous rank hint as an explicit snapshot instead of
reading the mutable module variable inside each metric helper. The convergence cleanup then renamed
the stored boolean to `hasObservedRankSlope` and centralized Rich rank clamping, so the code now
distinguishes an observed resize slope from a raw word-rank value at the call sites that cross the
bootstrap width window. The same maintenance pass replaced the Rich exact-result cache's type
assertion with an explicit cacheable-result type guard, so only non-fallback results with a concrete
state can reach the LRU helper.

Focused Rich validation kept the expected structural shape: `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`
reported bbox `9280`, client rects `7616 / 18964`, mutations `18320`, style reads `0`; and
`rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` reported bbox `4976`, client rects `0 / 0`, mutations
`15792`, style reads `480`. The smoke build measured `133.90 kB` raw / `28.14 kB` gzip. This is a
maintainability convergence step only; it carries no new performance claim.

## Current focused hotspot refresh

After the Rich warm-gate cleanup, an eight-row current-only smoke refreshed the remaining Line,
Inline, and Rich hotspot shape. The build stayed at `133.90 kB` raw / `28.14 kB` gzip.

| Scenario                                      | Structural shape                                                              | Active RME |
| --------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------: |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous`             | bbox `14976`, client rects `16 / 64`, mutations `12139`, style reads `2272`   |     `6.5%` |
| `line-word-copy-batch-jitter`                 | bbox `12272`, client rects `0 / 0`, mutations `11536`, style reads `2160`     |    `12.0%` |
| `inline-path-end-batch-continuous`            | bbox `3648`, scrollWidth `4512`, mutations `10416`                            |    `32.3%` |
| `inline-path-middle-batch-jitter`             | bbox `3840`, scrollWidth `2116`, mutations `9168`                             |     `7.8%` |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`            | bbox `9280`, client rects `7616 / 18964`, mutations `18320`, style reads `0`  |     `4.2%` |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`                 | bbox `10960`, client rects `0 / 0`, mutations `13072`, style reads `1920`     |    `50.0%` |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`   | bbox `4096`, client rects `272 / 9408`, mutations `16114`, style reads `8496` |     `4.7%` |
| `rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` | bbox `4976`, client rects `0 / 0`, mutations `15792`, style reads `480`       |     `4.0%` |

The useful reading is structural. Inline's repeated-width row still benefits from the exact-width
result cache, while the smooth continuous row has no repeated width assignments and remains normal
candidate search work. Rich metadata affix remains an exact rect-list/search hotspot. Rich long-token
rows remain dominated by child-list/added/removed suffix churn even where rect-list reads are gone.
This keeps the next credible performance step at the Rich DOM representation level, or otherwise at
readability/convergence cleanup; another small warm-threshold or patch-helper tweak is unlikely to
move these counters without new evidence.

## Rich probe-only hidden suffix feasibility audit

The hidden-suffix idea was revisited specifically for the hidden probe, not the visible rich body.
That removes the public text/accessibility concern because the probe subtree is already
`aria-hidden`, but it does not make the change a small patch: the hidden probe and visible body share
the same `patchRich` state machine and therefore the same live-DOM invariant.

Today a clamped rich state means the source suffix has been physically removed from the rich body and
the clamp ellipsis, when present, is a root-level trailing text node. Several patch paths depend on
that exact shape:

- `rootEllipsisNode` and `removeRootEllipsis` only recognize an ellipsis as `target.lastChild`.
- `removeAfterBoundary` and `removeChildrenFrom` assume suffix nodes after the retained boundary can
  be removed, optionally preserving that final root ellipsis.
- forward grow paths insert cloned source suffixes before the existing root ellipsis only when the
  patch anchor is the rich body root.
- same-text and whole-prefix fast paths resolve source paths directly in the live body, so hidden
  retained suffix nodes would change child indexes unless a separate path mapping existed.

A probe-only hidden suffix would therefore need a different representation contract, not just a
`display:none` flag. It would have to specify where hidden suffix nodes live relative to the root
ellipsis, how text-node whitespace is restored, how source paths map through hidden retained nodes,
and how fallback/full-state patches recover a byte-for-byte source tree. Without that design,
keeping suffix nodes in the hidden probe risks making the search measure one DOM shape while
`patchRich` believes it is operating on another.

Conclusion: the remaining Rich long-token child-list hotspot is real, but probe-only hidden suffixes
are not the next low-risk optimization. Reopen this only as a separate representation experiment
with an explicit invariant and package-level A/B. The current convergence path should prefer either
readability work around the existing patch/search code or a new diagnostic that proves a complete
hidden-probe representation beats the current delete-and-clone model.

## Text warm-gate affix signal cleanup

The text warm-search cost model no longer parses the affix layout key string to decide whether an
affix is present. `LineClamp` now derives an explicit `hasAffixes` flag from the observed before/after
slot size signatures and passes that flag into `clampTextToLayout` and `canSkipFullTextFit`.
`layoutKey` remains the layout identity used to invalidate stale hints; it is no longer overloaded
as both identity and semantic state.

This is a convergence cleanup, not a new performance claim. It removes the previous
`"0x0|0x0"` knowledge from `text.ts`, keeps direct helper callers defaulting to no affixes, and
stores the optional flag on new text clamp hints so inconsistent helper inputs do not silently share
warm state. A follow-up removed the now-dead `layoutKey` plumbing from the warm cost-model input
itself; `layoutKey` remains only as hint identity and result metadata.

Validation:

- `vp check --fix` passed.
- `vp test -c vite.browser.config.ts packages/vue-clamp/tests/text-layout.browser.test.ts` passed
  (`22` tests).
- focused LineClamp browser coverage passed (`91` tests).
- A current-only two-row Line smoke kept the prior structural shape:
  `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous` bbox `14976`, client rects `16 / 64`, mutations `12139`, style
  reads `2272`; `line-word-copy-batch-jitter` bbox `12272`, client rects `0 / 0`, mutations
  `11536`, style reads `2160`. The build measured `134.54 kB` raw / `28.26 kB` gzip.

## Rejected text target-specific cold-cost gate

A follow-up tested whether the text warm gate should compare estimated warm-search probes against
the cold binary-search probe count for the same estimated target, rather than against the cold
maximum probe count. The idea was more precise on paper: if the target estimate points to an easy
cold-search boundary, the warm path should have to beat that cheaper cold path.

The package smoke did not support retaining it. A same-process before/after run over
`line-cta-affix-batch-continuous`, `line-word-copy-batch-jitter`,
`inline-path-end-batch-continuous`, `inline-path-middle-batch-jitter`, and
`inline-word-copy-batch-jumps` produced identical structural counters in every row:

| Scenario                           | Key structural counters before -> after                                     |
| ---------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous`  | bbox `14976 -> 14976`, mutations `12139 -> 12139`, style `2272 -> 2272`     |
| `line-word-copy-batch-jitter`      | bbox `12272 -> 12272`, mutations `11536 -> 11536`, style `2160 -> 2160`     |
| `inline-path-end-batch-continuous` | bbox `3648 -> 3648`, scrollWidth `4512 -> 4512`, mutations `10416 -> 10416` |
| `inline-path-middle-batch-jitter`  | bbox `3840 -> 3840`, scrollWidth `2116 -> 2116`, mutations `9168 -> 9168`   |
| `inline-word-copy-batch-jumps`     | bbox `576 -> 576`, scrollWidth `672 -> 672`, mutations `1856 -> 1856`       |

The experimental build also moved from `134.42 kB` raw / `28.25 kB` gzip to `134.66 kB` raw /
`28.27 kB` gzip. With no structural workload reduction and a small size cost, the experiment was
reverted. The retained max-cold comparison remains because it is the existing behavior and the more
specific alternative did not prove a benefit in the covered Line/Inline warm-path rows.

## Rejected Rich rank-move cold-depth guard

The next Rich warm-gate experiment tested whether `RichLineClamp` should mirror Text's
`rankMove <= coldProbes` guard before accepting a beyond-window rank hint. The hypothesis was that
large estimated rank movement might over-trust warm search in the same way a text helper could.

A same-process before/after smoke over the current Rich hotspot rows rejected that hypothesis:

| Scenario                                      | Key structural counters before -> after                                         |
| --------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`            | bbox `9280 -> 9280`, client rects `7616 -> 7616`, mutations `18320 -> 18320`    |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`                 | bbox `10960 -> 10960`, style `1920 -> 1920`, mutations `13072 -> 13072`         |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`   | bbox `4096 -> 4512`, mutations `16114 -> 20530`, added/removed `13728 -> 17824` |
| `rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` | bbox `4976 -> 4976`, mutations `15792 -> 15792`, style `480 -> 480`             |

The guard was therefore reverted. This is useful evidence for keeping Rich separate from Text here:
the scalar rank-move model undercounts the value of staying on Rich's current hidden-probe DOM
suffix path for long-token font-tick inputs. Making the gate stricter did not reduce probes in the
covered rows and materially increased child-list churn in the row that already carries the largest
long-token mutation load.

## Rejected Rich affix simple-line gate widening

The remaining `rich-metadata-affix-*` rows still spend most of their structural work on exact
client-rect line counting. A plausible next experiment was to let Rich's height-based simple-line
shortcut run even when the probe content also contains before/after affix wrappers, instead of
limiting it to the no-affix `content -> body` shape. The safety hypothesis was narrow: `fitsContent`
would still use real rects until a line-box height had been calibrated, then only use content height
as a later shortcut.

The experiment did not hit the actual hotspot. Browser behavior tests still passed, but a focused
current smoke over the relevant Rich rows produced the same structural counters as the retained
baseline:

| Scenario                                    | Key structural counters under the experiment                            |
| ------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-continuous`      | bbox `8800`, client rects `4992 / 12400`, mutations `14208`, style `0`  |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`          | bbox `9280`, client rects `7616 / 18964`, mutations `18320`, style `0`  |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-novel-jitter`    | bbox `2720`, client rects `3312 / 8512`, mutations `10544`, style `0`   |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` | bbox `4096`, client rects `272 / 9408`, mutations `16114`, style `8496` |

The smoke build measured `134.36 kB` raw / `28.23 kB` gzip with the widened gate. With no structural
workload reduction, the change was reverted. The useful conclusion is that metadata-affix rect-list
cost is not an accidental miss in the no-affix simple-line gate; it remains the cost of exact
line-counting for affix-bearing inline flow. The next credible reduction there needs a new
line-count proof for affix layouts, not a broader reuse of the existing simple-line shortcut.

## Rejected Rich atomic verify-overflow line fit

The next stricter experiment tried to copy LineClamp's affix line-fit strategy into Rich: even when
Rich layout inspection saw atomic inline runs, it would publish a `verifyOverflow` line-fit cache
using the body line height. The intended safety model was that exact client rects would calibrate
the line box first, and height would only reject or accept later candidates after that calibration.

This failed correctness before benchmark evidence was needed. The Rich browser suite reported two
regressions:

- `treats inline-block descendants as atomic runs` kept part of an inline-block descendant visible
  when the atomic run should have been dropped as a unit.
- `ignores variable rich display declarations inside inactive media rules` observed an unexpected
  stylesheet signature scan in a path that should stay cold.

After reverting the experiment, those two tests passed again. This closes another tempting path:
Rich atomic runs cannot inherit LineClamp's affix overflow-height proof directly. The atomic
keep/drop boundary is semantic, not just a line-height counting problem. Any future affix-aware rich
line-count proof must keep atomic-run monotonicity explicit and cannot be implemented by publishing
generic `verifyOverflow` line-fit metadata for mixed Rich runs.

## Rich simple-line boundary naming cleanup

After the two rejected Rich line-fit experiments, the retained code was tightened around the exact
boundary those experiments established. The simple-line cache now flows through named helpers:
`canUseBodyOnlyLineFit` for the no-affix `content -> body` probe shape and
`textOnlySimpleLineFit` for the "all logical runs are searchable text" condition. This keeps the two
separate safety gates from drifting in `createSearchIndex` and the cached-index refresh path.

This is a maintainability convergence step, not a performance claim. Focused Rich browser tests for
inline-block atomic runs, inactive media rules, simple-line reuse, and atomic wrapper refresh passed
(`7` tests). A focused Rich smoke kept the same structural totals as the retained baseline:
bbox `29312`, client-rect reads `7888`, client-rect entries `28372`, mutation records `63298`, and
style reads `10896`. The smoke build measured `134.69 kB` raw / `28.32 kB` gzip.

## Text warm-gate input-object cleanup

The next maintainability pass removed the last long positional parameter lists from the text warm
gate. `warmSearchStaysLocalBySlope` and `warmSearchStaysLocalByVisibleDensity` now both take
a named `WarmHintInput`, so `boundary`, affix presence, line capacity, root width,
candidate count, and full-candidate inclusion cannot be silently swapped between the slope and
visible-density paths.

A later convergence pass made the call site construct that `WarmHintInput` once and share it between
the slope and visible-density checks. This does not change the warm policy; it only keeps the two
fallback strategies from drifting when future context fields are added. The follow-up also
centralized the final conversion from a hint plus chosen `rankPerPx` / reference width into the
shared `WarmSearchInput`, so the two strategies differ only in how they choose those rank
metrics.

This is also a convergence cleanup, not a performance claim. Validation passed:

- `vp check --fix`
- `vp test packages/vue-clamp/tests/text.test.ts` (`18` tests)
- `vp test -c vite.browser.config.ts packages/vue-clamp/tests/text-layout.browser.test.ts` (`22`
  tests)
- focused Line/Inline package smoke with unchanged structural counters:
  `line-cta-affix-batch-continuous` bbox `14976`, client rects `16 / 64`, mutations `12139`;
  `line-word-copy-batch-jitter` bbox `12272`, mutations `11536`, style reads `2160`;
  `inline-path-middle-batch-jitter` bbox `3840`, scrollWidth `2116`, mutations `9168`;
  `inline-word-copy-batch-jumps` bbox `576`, scrollWidth `672`, mutations `1856`.

The smoke build measured `134.83 kB` raw / `28.33 kB` gzip. The retained value is readability and
call-site safety around an already proven warm-search policy.

## Rich exact-width result cache

The next Rich pass revisited the earlier rejected "exact-width result cache" idea with the missing
layout-identity proof filled in. The retained cache is deliberately narrow: it only runs when the
reclamp arrives with a fresh root-width snapshot, the root uses fixed inline width/font styles and no
class, the current search index has no style-dependent display or line metrics, source inline styles
do not contain unresolved `%` or `var(...)`, active stylesheets are readable and contain no
`var(...)`, and the cache key includes the exact stylesheet rule text, root/ancestor id/class/style
context, the affix signature, atomic-path signature, and simple-line metric key. Font-load
invalidations clear the cache.

The first over-conservative version required `document.styleSheets.length === 0`; focused Rich smoke
showed no structural movement. Temporarily removing that guard proved the direction itself was real,
so the retained version replaced it with the stricter stylesheet/ancestor identity key above.

A same-shape before/after smoke then toggled only `resultCacheLimit` (`0` vs `64`) over the four
current Rich hotspot rows:

| Scenario                                      | Before cache off                              | After cache on                                | Structural result                                                                  |
| --------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`            | rects `7616 / 18964`, mutations `18320`       | rects `5728 / 14340`, mutations `17008`       | `-1888` rect reads, `-4624` rect entries, `-1312` mutations                        |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`                 | bbox `10960`, style `1920`, mutations `13072` | bbox `8848`, style `1136`, mutations `11440`  | `-2112` bbox reads, `-784` style reads, `-1632` mutations                          |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`   | bbox `4096`, rects `272 / 9408`, style `8496` | bbox `4096`, rects `272 / 9408`, style `8496` | unchanged; `var(...)` font-size/font-load path correctly bypasses the result cache |
| `rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` | bbox `4976`, style `480`, mutations `15792`   | bbox `2160`, style `96`, mutations `7408`     | `-2816` bbox reads, `-384` style reads, `-8384` mutations                          |

Totals moved from bbox `29312 -> 24384` (`-4928`, `-16.8%`), client rect reads
`7888 -> 6000` (`-1888`, `-23.9%`), client rect entries `28372 -> 23748` (`-4624`, `-16.3%`),
mutation records `63298 -> 51970` (`-11328`, `-17.9%`), and style reads `10896 -> 9728`
(`-1168`, `-10.7%`). Active time moved `1509.9 -> 1367.4 ms`, but timing is treated only as
supporting evidence because the tight long-token row still had high RME with the cache enabled.

A new Rich browser regression covers the most direct stale-cache hazard: after seeding a repeated
fixed-width clamped result at `24px`, the component revisits the same width with a `12px` root font
and must restore the full rich text. Focused validation passed for that regression. The retained
smoke build measured `138.78 kB` raw / `29.30 kB` gzip; compared with the previous documented
focused build (`134.83 kB` raw / `28.33 kB` gzip), this pass costs about `+3.95 kB` raw /
`+0.97 kB` gzip for the proved repeated-width Rich workload reduction.

## Rich exact-width cache size cleanup

A follow-up kept the exact-width cache behavior and reduced its implementation cost. The Inline and
Rich exact-result caches now share a tiny LRU touch/remember helper and the same cache entry limit,
and the cache guards share the content-independent inline-width and inline-font-metric predicates
from `layout.ts` instead of duplicating them between components. The Rich cache key also stopped
repeating the root inline style outside the ancestor context key, and remembering a Rich result no
longer clones the result object before storing it. Later helper-only passes made cache hit and
eviction state explicit: `touch` uses `Map` key presence as the hit signal, and `remember` uses the
iterator result's `done` flag when evicting the oldest entry. Current callers still use string keys
and store only concrete clamp results, so these helper cleanups did not change runtime workload.
The Rich result-cache key path also uses explicit early returns for root inline-style cacheability,
checks root/search-index cacheability before scanning prepared rich inline styles, and checks
ancestor inline-style cacheability before scanning stylesheets. That keeps non-cacheable inputs on
the cheapest early-return path.
A final attempt to extract `element.style` into a local variable in the same guard was rejected:
it had no workload benefit and moved the pack smoke back to `138.38 kB` raw / `29.20 kB` gzip.

This is a maintainability cleanup, not a new workload optimization. Focused browser coverage passed
for the Rich repeated-width stale-cache regression and the full Inline browser suite. The four-row
Rich smoke kept exactly the retained cache structure:

| Scenario                                      | Structural shape after cleanup                                         |
| --------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`            | bbox `9280`, rects `5728 / 14340`, mutations `17008`, style reads `0`  |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`                 | bbox `8848`, rects `0 / 0`, mutations `11440`, style reads `1136`      |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`   | bbox `4096`, rects `272 / 9408`, mutations `16114`, style reads `8496` |
| `rich-word-long-token-tight-font-batch-jumps` | bbox `2160`, rects `0 / 0`, mutations `7408`, style reads `96`         |

Totals stayed at bbox `24384`, client rect reads `6000`, client rect entries `23748`, mutation
records `51970`, and style reads `9728`. The smoke build measured `138.37 kB` raw /
`29.19 kB` gzip, saving about `0.40 kB` raw and `0.11 kB` gzip versus the first retained cache
build. Compared with the pre-cache focused build (`134.83 kB` raw / `28.33 kB` gzip), the retained
cache now costs about `+3.55 kB` raw / `+0.87 kB` gzip for the repeated-width Rich reduction.

## Local optimization convergence boundary

The latest audit closes the current small-change loop. The retained exact-width caches and text/Rich
warm-search guards already have structural evidence. The follow-up attempts that only tightened a
guard, adjusted a warm threshold, changed a simple-line gate, or rearranged patch helper details have
either stayed structurally flat, increased package size, or failed correctness. That is now a
stop condition for local micro-optimization: another small Rich cache-key/guard edit should not be
retained unless it first names a browser-work counter it can remove and then proves that reduction in
a same-process A/B.

The remaining known performance space is no longer a local tweak:

- Rich long-token rows still have real child-list churn, but reducing it requires a new hidden-probe
  DOM representation or path-mapping invariant. Probe-only hidden suffixes remain a design
  experiment, not a patch-helper change.
- Rich metadata-affix rows still pay exact rect-list line counting, but previous attempts to widen
  the no-affix simple-line proof or copy LineClamp's overflow-height proof either did not move
  counters or broke atomic-run correctness. Reopening this needs a new affix/atomic line-count proof.
- Broader benchmark coverage can still strengthen confidence around overfitting risk, especially
  novel-width jitter, CJK, line-limit variation, token density, affix occupancy, and repeated-width
  ratio. That is validation work unless it exposes a new structural hotspot.

Until one of those larger hypotheses is made concrete, further work should prefer readability and
maintainability around the retained optimizations over more performance tuning. Timing-only movement
inside the current noisy range is not enough to keep adding algorithmic branches.

## Remaining Rich design-direction audit

A convergence audit rechecked the two remaining Rich performance directions against the evidence
already gathered in this session. Neither direction is ready as a local patch in the current branch;
both require a stronger design artifact before another runtime experiment is worth retaining.

| Direction                               | Current evidence                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | Required next proof                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |
| --------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Rich metadata-affix line counting       | The full-candidate verification guard explains only `144 / 7616` rect reads in the repeated jitter row. Duplicate same-pass candidate fits are `0%` there and only `64 / 3312` in novel jitter. A simple height predicate matched the current metadata fixtures, but the broader safe implementation already regressed by swapping rect reads for many more bbox reads (`27824 -> 62397`) and by breaking low-RME rows. | A new affix/atomic line-count proof must avoid per-candidate or per-atomic bbox reads, preserve atomic keep/drop monotonicity, and prove lower structural counters in same-process A/B. Reopening the existing simple-line/overflow-height route is not justified.           |
| Rich hidden-probe suffix representation | The isolated hidden-suffix probe reduced active time (`15.8 ms -> 13.1 ms`) and converted child-list churn into attribute/character-data records, but total mutation records stayed `42401`. Probe-only hidden suffixes also conflict with current `patchRich` invariants: clamped suffix nodes are physically removed, root ellipsis is the final body text node, and source paths map directly through the live body. | A representation spec must define hidden suffix placement, root ellipsis ownership, whitespace restoration, source-path mapping, and full/fallback recovery before implementation. It then needs package-level A/B proving total work improves, not only child-list records. |

This means the current branch should not continue with incremental Rich cache-key, warm-gate,
simple-line, or patch-helper tuning. The next performance-bearing move is either a separate
hidden-probe representation design/prototype or a new affix/atomic line-count proof with an explicit
counter target.

## Exact-result cache key boundary hardening

The next convergence pass tightened the retained Inline/Rich exact-result caches without changing
their cacheability gates. Their string keys now come from a shared tuple encoder instead of raw
`"|".join(...)` concatenation. This keeps field boundaries explicit when attribute values,
ancestor context, or stylesheet rule text themselves contain delimiter characters. A small unit test
guards the representative collision shape: `["a|b", "c"]` and `["a", "b|c"]` must produce different
keys.

Validation passed:

- `vp check --fix`
- `vp test packages/vue-clamp/tests/cache.test.ts`
- `vp test -c vite.browser.config.ts packages/vue-clamp/tests/inline.browser.test.ts`
- `vp test -c vite.browser.config.ts packages/vue-clamp/tests/clamp.browser.test.ts`
- `vp pack src/index.ts` from `packages/vue-clamp`

The pack smoke measured `138.59 kB` raw / `29.26 kB` gzip. Compared with the previous retained
cache cleanup build (`138.37 kB` raw / `29.19 kB` gzip), the hardening costs about `+0.22 kB` raw /
`+0.07 kB` gzip. This is not a new workload optimization; it is a small correctness/maintainability
guard around an optimization that now carries richer style and ancestor identity in its keys.

A follow-up widened the shared cache-helper unit coverage without changing runtime code. The helper
contract now also asserts that touching a key refreshes its LRU position before the oldest entry is
evicted, and that `undefined` keys are ignored. This keeps the retained Inline/Rich exact-result
caches from depending on untested `Map` ordering behavior. Validation passed with
`vp test packages/vue-clamp/tests/cache.test.ts`, `vp check --fix`, `vp test`, and `git diff --check`.
The same cache-helper contract now also covers remembering an existing key: the helper must update
the value and refresh that entry's LRU position before later eviction.
A later convergence pass named the allowed tuple key part type and added a unit assertion that
numeric and string fields remain distinct (`[1, "2"]` versus `["1", 2]`). This preserves the exact
cache-key boundary contract without changing the JSON tuple encoding or LRU behavior.
The shared exact-result cache limit was then renamed to `exactResultCacheEntryLimit`, and the LRU
helper parameter now says `entryLimit`. This is another readability-only cleanup: the value is an
entry count, not a byte size, width range, or timing threshold.
The Inline exact-result cache naming was also tightened without changing behavior: local helper
names now rely on the component file for Inline context, while the lookup helper still says
`matching` because it validates the current prepared text and clamp context before touching the LRU
entry. This carries no new performance claim.
RichLineClamp received the same local naming cleanup around its exact-result cache: helper names now
avoid repeating Rich context that the component file already supplies, while `touchResultCache`
keeps the LRU side effect visible. No cache guard, key field, or reuse rule changed.
The same pass shortened local cache-only type names such as `KeyPart` and `CachedResult`; exported
names and runtime contracts were left unchanged.
A follow-up shortened the local affix-identity variable from `sameProbeAffix` to `sameAffix`,
matching the helper contracts without changing the affix guard itself.
The local warm-rank helper names were then shortened in the same spirit: `RankHint`,
`warmBootstrapWidthDelta`, `canUseSearchHint`, and related helpers now rely on the component file for
Rich context while preserving the same probe estimates and full-fit guards.
Text warm-search local names followed the same rule: `WarmHintInput`, `WarmSearchEstimate`,
`estimateWarmSearch`, `warmSearchStaysLocal*`, and `searchCountForCandidates` keep the local
warm-search meaning without repeating the `text.ts` file context.

## Inline pending root-width snapshot cleanup

The next convergence cleanup fixed the lifecycle around `InlineClamp`'s same-flush root-width
handoff. The exact-result cache already clears on font, ResizeObserver, mount, and semantic
invalidations, but the pending fresh root width was only overwritten when a later Vue layout
snapshot arrived. A non-snapshot invalidation could therefore clear cache state while leaving the
previous same-flush width available for the next coalesced clamp pass.

The fix keeps the two pieces of freshness state together: snapshot requests set both the layout
signature and root width, while non-snapshot requests clear both values and clear the cache. This is
not a performance change; it removes a stale-width state that would be especially hard to reason
about around retained exact-width cache and warm-search behavior.

Focused validation passed:

- `vp check --fix`
- `vp test`
- `vp test -c vite.browser.config.ts packages/vue-clamp/tests/inline.browser.test.ts`
- `vp test packages/vue-clamp/tests/cache.test.ts`
- `vp test -c vite.browser.config.ts packages/vue-clamp/tests/clamp.browser.test.ts packages/vue-clamp/tests/inline.browser.test.ts packages/vue-clamp/tests/layout.browser.test.ts packages/vue-clamp/tests/text-layout.browser.test.ts`
- `vp pack src/index.ts` from `packages/vue-clamp`, measuring `138.67 kB` raw / `29.32 kB` gzip

## Search probe-count proof extraction

The next convergence pass moved the generic warm/cold probe-count proof out of `text.test.ts` and
into `packages/vue-clamp/tests/search.test.ts`. This keeps text helper behavior separate from the
search algorithm contract that both Text and Rich warm gates rely on. The extracted test still
checks estimated cold and warm probe counts against the actual `findLastFittingIndex` probe order
across candidate counts, targets, hints, and expansion budgets.

A small new assertion documents the local-coverage meaning of the retained expansion budgets:
default text search with two expansions covers `3` local ranks before binary fallback, while Rich's
three-expansion budget covers `7`. This is a proof-structure cleanup only; it does not change search
runtime behavior or attach a new performance claim.

Validation passed:

- `vp test packages/vue-clamp/tests/search.test.ts packages/vue-clamp/tests/text.test.ts`
- `vp check --fix`
- `vp test`

The warm probe-count estimator now mirrors `findLastFittingIndex` for non-finite hints:
`NaN` / `Infinity` hints fall back to the cold-search estimate instead of being counted as a
one-probe warm search. The search proof matrix keeps exhaustive finite targets from `-1` through
`count` and adds those hints and non-finite targets, so the estimator cannot drift from actual probe
order on invalid warm-start or target-rank inputs. The
target normalization is explicit in the helper: `+Infinity` means the last candidate, while `NaN`
and `-Infinity` mean no candidate fits.

The same `search.test.ts` proof was then widened to cover `findLargestFittingCount`, which is the
count-search helper used by WrapClamp materialized/live settlement. The added assertions fix four
contracts that affect DOM-search cost and correctness: empty or single-count ranges return the
known-safe lower bound without probing, the no-hint path keeps its ceil-midpoint probe order, hinted
count search starts from the provided count after applying the low-bound offset, and an unusual
all-failing predicate returns the known-safe lower bound instead of underflowing. This also changes
no runtime behavior; it only makes the existing search helper contract executable. Validation passed
with `vp test packages/vue-clamp/tests/search.test.ts`, `vp check --fix`, and `vp test`.

## Content-independent width gate coverage

The next convergence pass added pure unit coverage for the shared layout style gates that protect
Inline/Rich exact-result caches and Inline's current-root-width shortcut. The new
`packages/vue-clamp/tests/layout.test.ts` asserts that `%` and `var(...)` references are treated as
unresolved/content-dependent, while absolute numeric widths and percentage-free `calc(...)` /
`clamp(...)` widths remain cacheable. This test mirrors the shrink-to-fit correctness issue from the
external review: a percentage root width can depend on the currently truncated content and must not
be trusted as a stable available width.

This also changes no runtime behavior and carries no new performance claim. It makes the retained
width-trust rule executable so future cache or full-body-restore cleanups cannot accidentally widen
it.

Validation passed:

- `vp test packages/vue-clamp/tests/layout.test.ts`
- `vp check --fix`
- `vp test`

A follow-up widened the same unit file to cover the inline-font-metrics gate used by the retained
exact-result caches. The cache remains eligible only when the root inline style declares `font`, or
declares both `font-family` and `font-size`; either field alone is not enough because stylesheet or
inheritance changes could still alter text metrics at the same width. This is another test-only
contract hardening step. Validation passed with `vp test packages/vue-clamp/tests/layout.test.ts`,
`vp check --fix`, and `vp test`.

The font-metrics gate was then tightened to require resolved inline metric values. Unit coverage now
rejects `font`, `font-family`, or `font-size` values that still contain `%` or `var(...)`, and Inline
browser coverage exercises a fixed-width root whose `font-size` comes from a parent CSS custom
property before restoring from a repeated-width cache path. This is cache-boundary hardening rather
than a performance claim.

## Coalescing runner contract coverage

The next convergence pass extended `packages/vue-clamp/tests/layout.test.ts` to cover the shared
`createCoalescingRunner` contract used by Inline, Line/Rich multiline, and Wrap recompute paths. The
new test holds the first task open, issues multiple requests while it is still running, then verifies
that exactly one follow-up task runs afterward and no two tasks overlap.

This does not change runtime behavior and carries no performance claim. It makes the existing
async-invalidation guarantee executable: ResizeObserver, font, prop, and Vue update bursts can
coalesce, but a request made during an active clamp pass must not be dropped.

Validation passed:

- `vp test packages/vue-clamp/tests/layout.test.ts`
- `vp check --fix`
- `vp test`

## Subpixel border-box signature coverage

The next convergence pass added a focused layout browser contract for `borderBoxSizeSignature`.
It verifies that two widths with the same integer `offsetWidth` but different fractional CSS-pixel
widths produce different border-box signatures.

The direct `borderBoxWidth` helper now has the same browser guard, because LineClamp and
RichLineClamp use it when no fresh root-width snapshot is available. That helper must return the
fractional visual width, not the integer offset width.

The synchronous `borderBoxSizeSnapshot` path now has the same guard: its `width` field must match
the fractional `getBoundingClientRect().width` value and differ from the integer `offsetWidth`.

The same browser file then added the matching ResizeObserver-entry contract: when the stored
signature comes from the earlier fractional width, `hasBorderBoxEntrySignatureChange` must report
the later fractional width even though `offsetWidth` is still unchanged.

The contract was then widened one more step to cover `observedBorderBoxSizeSnapshot` itself. For an
ordinary fractional-width entry, the snapshot must carry the same subpixel width as
`getBoundingClientRect().width`, not the integer `offsetWidth`, because that width can be handed
directly into a reclamp.

The transformed visual fallback now uses the same fractional-width fixture. The browser test asserts
that a transformed entry falls back to the visual `getBoundingClientRect()` width and that the width
is genuinely non-integer, so this path cannot regress to integer offset boxes or untransformed entry
sizes without failing.

This directly guards the precision regression class behind the earlier `offsetWidth` /
`offsetHeight` concern: layout signatures must stay based on subpixel visual
`getBoundingClientRect()` data and subpixel `ResizeObserverEntry.borderBoxSize` payloads rather
than integer offset boxes. No runtime behavior changed and no performance claim is attached.

Validation passed:

- `vp test -c vite.browser.config.ts packages/vue-clamp/tests/layout.browser.test.ts`

## Current full-matrix convergence refresh

A current-only full package smoke over the expanded `102`-scenario public matrix refreshed the
post-cache convergence shape. It is not a release timing claim, but it gives the latest structural
hotspot map after the Line/Inline/Rich warm-search, exact-result cache, and subpixel signature
passes:

| Component     | Scenarios | Active sum | Bbox reads |  Client rects | Mutations | Scroll reads | Style reads |
| ------------- | --------: | ---------: | ---------: | ------------: | --------: | -----------: | ----------: |
| LineClamp     |        33 |  5091.6 ms |     160498 |    `352/1328` |    138156 |          512 |       21328 |
| InlineClamp   |         9 |  1818.9 ms |      14592 |         `0/0` |     41860 |        15635 |           0 |
| RichLineClamp |        33 |  5021.1 ms |      94825 | `20379/65095` |    202005 |            0 |       17312 |
| WrapClamp     |        27 |  3209.9 ms |     318408 |         `0/0` |    142652 |            0 |       72528 |

All package rows reported zero `offsetWidth` / `offsetHeight` reads, confirming the retained
subpixel border-box signature path has replaced integer offset-box measurements in production clamp
paths.

The highest active rows remain expected structural work rather than an obvious cache miss:

| Scenario                                    | Structural shape                                                                      |
| ------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `line-cta-affix-batch-jitter`               | bbox `19719`, mutations `17702`, style reads / after slot calls `2240`                |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`          | bbox `9280`, client rects `5728 / 14340`, mutations `17008`                           |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`               | `72` unique widths / `49` repeated transitions; style reads `1136`, mutations `11440` |
| `inline-path-end-batch-continuous`          | no repeated widths; scroll reads `4512`, mutations `10416`                            |
| `inline-path-middle-batch-continuous`       | no repeated widths; scroll reads `4556`, mutations `10481`                            |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` | cache-bypassed `var(...)` font path; style reads `8496`, mutations `16114`            |

The `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter` row is a useful convergence check: its `1136` style reads are
approximately the `72` unique widths times `16` component instances, so the repeated-width exact
cache is already doing the expected work. Its remaining cost is novel-width measurement and public
DOM patching, not a loose cache guard. The Inline continuous rows similarly have `0` repeated
transitions, so their scroll reads are normal candidate-search work. The Rich long-token
font-size-tick row intentionally bypasses exact-result caching because the root font-size uses
`var(...)` and font invalidation is part of the scenario.

This refresh keeps the local performance stop condition unchanged. The next retained performance
change should start from a new structural counter target. The known candidates are still design-level
work: a Rich hidden-probe suffix representation that reduces total mutation work, or a new
affix/atomic Rich line-count proof that reduces client-rect reads without adding per-candidate bbox
reads. Otherwise, the branch should continue with maintainability cleanup around the retained
policies rather than more cache-threshold or patch-helper tuning.

## Border-box signature sentinel cleanup

The next convergence cleanup named the shared empty border-box signature as
`emptyBorderBoxSignature` and replaced the remaining component-local `"0x0"` initializers in the
multiline shell, InlineClamp, and WrapClamp. This does not change the subpixel signature algorithm
or ResizeObserver comparison behavior; it just keeps the "no observed box yet" state tied to the
layout helper that owns the signature format.

Validation passed:

- `vp test packages/vue-clamp/tests/layout.test.ts`
- `vp test -c vite.browser.config.ts packages/vue-clamp/tests/layout.browser.test.ts packages/vue-clamp/tests/inline.browser.test.ts packages/vue-clamp/tests/clamp.browser.test.ts`
- `vp test -c vite.browser.config.ts packages/vue-clamp/tests/wrap.browser.test.ts`

A follow-up naming pass made the same boundary clearer without changing behavior: the internal
positive cache is now named around visual border-box fallback, and the browser tests use
`emptyBorderBoxSignature` instead of a `"1x1"` placeholder when they intentionally force a previous
signature mismatch. Validation passed with
`vp test -c vite.browser.config.ts packages/vue-clamp/tests/layout.browser.test.ts`.
The adjacent helper surface was then reduced without changing the ResizeObserver policy: the
entry-size snapshot/signature helpers are private to `layout.ts`, and the multiline shell calls
`observedBorderBoxSizeSnapshot` directly instead of through a one-line wrapper.

## Rich hidden-probe mutation breakdown

A focused current-only smoke added hidden-subtree mutation counters to the package benchmark and ran
three Rich hotspot rows:

| Scenario                                    | Hidden mutations | Hidden child-list records | Hidden added/removed nodes |
| ------------------------------------------- | ---------------: | ------------------------: | -------------------------: |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`          |   `9472 / 17008` |             `3056 / 3824` |              `1984 / 2448` |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`               |   `5184 / 11440` |               `448 / 448` |                `224 / 224` |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` |  `14016 / 16114` |           `13536 / 15120` |            `12352 / 13728` |

Across those rows, `64.3%` of mutation records, `87.9%` of child-list records, and `88.8%` of
added/removed nodes came from `aria-hidden` probe subtrees. The child-list evidence is stronger than
the total mutation ratio because visible roots still account for many attribute and text-data
records, especially slot and status updates.

This makes the next Rich performance spike more concrete: a hidden-probe DOM representation must
reduce hidden child-list churn and hidden added/removed nodes first. It should not start by tuning
warm thresholds or visible patch paths unless a same-process A/B shows those counters move.

## Rich cache-hit probe DOM deferral

The first retained hidden-probe step splits RichLineClamp's probe state into two meanings:

- `measuredState` remains the latest measured or cached result used for warm search, full-fit skip,
  and rank hints.
- `probeDomState` tracks the actual hidden probe body state used as the next `patchRich` origin.

On an exact-result cache hit, the component now updates the logical state and visible DOM but does
not immediately patch the hidden probe body. The next uncached measurement still patches from the
real `probeDomState`, so incremental patch correctness is preserved.

A temporary reverse run on repeated-width Rich rows quantified the useful part of this change:

| Scenario                           | Hidden mutations | Hidden child-list records | Hidden added/removed nodes |
| ---------------------------------- | ---------------: | ------------------------: | -------------------------: |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jumps`       |   `1392 -> 1200` |              `384 -> 384` |               `192 -> 192` |
| `rich-word-cjk-batch-jitter`       |   `1456 -> 1456` |              `448 -> 448` |               `320 -> 320` |
| `rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps` |   `2224 -> 1648` |            `1744 -> 1168` |             `1408 -> 1024` |

Across those three rows, hidden mutation records moved `5072 -> 4304` (`-15.1%`), hidden child-list
records moved `2576 -> 2000` (`-22.4%`), and hidden added/removed nodes moved `1920 -> 1536`
(`-20.0%`). The same run also reduced total mutation records `9904 -> 9136` (`-7.8%`) and total
child-list records `3488 -> 2912` (`-16.5%`).

The earlier three-row hotspot sample barely moved: hidden child-list records changed
`17040 -> 17008`, because the font-size invalidation row intentionally bypasses exact-result cache
and most of its hidden probe churn comes from real uncached candidate search. This means the retained
deferral is a bounded cache-hit optimization, not the full hidden-probe DOM representation. The
larger remaining target is still to reduce child-list churn during uncached long-token probe search.

## Rejected Rich stable-probe tree

A follow-up spike tested a narrower hidden-probe representation for the uncached long-token search:
keep the full inline wrapper tree in the hidden probe and update text nodes to represent each
candidate, instead of deleting and recloning suffix wrapper spans. The temporary implementation was
removed after measurement.

Counter-tracked current-only smoke showed that the idea hit the child-list target but increased total
DOM writes:

| Scenario                                  | Hidden child-list | Hidden added/removed | Character data | Total mutations |       Active median |
| ----------------------------------------- | ----------------: | -------------------: | -------------: | --------------: | ------------------: |
| `rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps`        |       `1168 -> 0` |   `1024/1024 -> 0/0` |    `0 -> 2048` |  `3808 -> 4688` |  `89.3 -> 111.5 ms` |
| `rich-word-long-token-batch-novel-jitter` |      `5744 -> 64` | `5024/5088 -> 32/32` |  `16 -> 10048` | `8480 -> 12832` | `116.3 -> 169.1 ms` |

The counters-off check rejected the same direction without MutationObserver instrumentation:

| Scenario                                  | Baseline active median | Stable-probe active median |
| ----------------------------------------- | ---------------------: | -------------------------: |
| `rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps`        |              `87.2 ms` |                 `104.5 ms` |
| `rich-word-long-token-batch-novel-jitter` |             `118.5 ms` |                 `161.8 ms` |

The spike also grew the packed library from `139.35 kB / 29.59 kB gzip` to
`143.72 kB / 30.46 kB gzip`, about `+4.37 kB` raw and `+0.87 kB` gzip.

Conclusion: preserving wrapper nodes and clearing suffix text is not a retained optimization. It
turns fewer child-list records into many text writes, and the browser still spends more time even
when benchmark counters are disabled. Any future hidden-probe representation needs to reduce total
mutation work or counters-off active time, not only hidden child-list records.

## Rich inherited simple-line metric refresh

A later convergence pass found one narrow structural optimization outside the rejected affix/atomic
line-count and hidden-probe representation directions. The `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps`
row changes the root font metrics through `font-size:var(...)` while its rich child wrappers are
transparent inline descendants that inherit font size and line height. Before this pass, every root
metric tick refreshed the cached Rich search index by re-reading each child wrapper's computed style.

The retained rule is deliberately small: after the initial layout inspection has proved the rich
children are transparent inline wrappers with matching line metrics, and the current stylesheet scan
contains no line-metric declarations, a later root metric change can rebuild `simpleLineFit` from the
root computed style alone. Inline child line-metric styles, stylesheet line-metric declarations,
style-dependent display, and non-baseline root vertical alignment still use the old full inspection
path.

Final focused smoke evidence:

| Scenario                                    | Before retained rule                                     | After retained rule                                      |
| ------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------- |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` | style reads `8496`, active median `253.4 ms`             | style reads `1152`, active median `245.3 ms`             |
| `rich-word-copy-batch-jitter`               | style reads `1136`, mutations `11344`                    | style reads `1136`, mutations `11344`                    |
| `rich-metadata-affix-batch-jitter`          | style reads `0`, rects `5728 / 14340`, mutations `16832` | style reads `0`, rects `5728 / 14340`, mutations `16832` |

The package smoke build moved from `139.13 kB / 29.54 kB gzip` before this rule to
`139.18 kB / 29.65 kB gzip` after the retained implementation and cleanup. The proven
benefit is the browser work counter: `7344` fewer `getComputedStyle` reads in the target row with
unchanged structural layout/mutation counters. The active-time smoke moved in the expected direction
under counters, but it remains a small timing delta and is not used as the primary proof.

## Rich long-token patch-path diagnosis

After the inherited line-metric refresh, the remaining Rich long-token hotspot still showed high
hidden child-list churn. A temporary local patch counter was added around `patchRich` fast paths and
then removed after measurement. The goal was to test whether the remaining child-list records came
from a missing same-text fast path, which would be a small local optimization, or from cross-wrapper
structural moves, which would require a representation/search change.

Counter-tracked smoke with the temporary probe showed:

| Scenario                                    | Patch-path counters per sample run                                                                              | Hidden child-list |
| ------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------: |
| `rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps`          | `patchForwardWholePrefix=416`, `patchBackwardWholePrefix=416`, `patchSameState=176`                             |            `1168` |
| `rich-word-long-token-batch-novel-jitter`   | `patchForwardWholePrefix=1008`, `patchBackwardWholePrefix=1104`, `patchFullToClamped=16`, `patchSameState=1040` |            `5744` |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` | `patchForwardWholePrefix=1552`, `patchBackwardWholePrefix=1584`, `patchSameState=720`                           |           `13536` |

The important negative result is the absence of meaningful `patchSameTextCut` traffic. The long-token
candidate search is not repeatedly slicing the same text node; it is moving the legal rich boundary
forward and backward across many transparent inline wrapper end points. Those moves necessarily add
or remove whole wrapper subtrees under the current probe representation.

This closes the small-local-fast-path hypothesis for the long-token child-list hotspot. Reducing that
work now means either reducing the number of whole-prefix probes, or changing the hidden-probe
representation in a way that avoids trading child-list records for even more `characterData` writes.
The earlier stable-probe-tree spike already failed the second condition, so any future representation
proposal must prove lower total mutation work or counters-off active time before it is retained.

## Rejected Rich warm-hint disable spike

A follow-up tested the most direct "fewer whole-prefix probes" idea: disable RichLineClamp's search
hint and let each reclamp search from a colder state. The temporary patch forced
`const searchHint = null` in `RichLineClamp.vue`, then was removed after measurement.

Focused counter smoke compared the restored warm-hint path with the disabled-hint patch in the same
working tree:

| Scenario                                    | Warm hint mutations | No hint mutations | Warm hint hidden child-list | No hint hidden child-list | Warm hint active | No hint active |
| ------------------------------------------- | ------------------: | ----------------: | --------------------------: | ------------------------: | ---------------: | -------------: |
| `rich-word-long-token-batch-jumps`          |              `3808` |            `8016` |                      `1168` |                    `5376` |       `106.2 ms` |     `120.4 ms` |
| `rich-word-long-token-batch-novel-jitter`   |              `8480` |           `34064` |                      `5744` |                   `31328` |       `116.1 ms` |     `218.5 ms` |
| `rich-word-long-token-font-size-tick-jumps` |             `16114` |           `30898` |                     `13536` |                   `28320` |       `242.1 ms` |     `310.6 ms` |

Conclusion: disabling the search hint does reduce none of the relevant browser work. It forces many
more structural probes and multiplies the same whole-prefix DOM churn that the hint path avoids.
Warm hints should stay; future search-shape experiments must be more selective than turning the
existing hint off.
